601 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Owen v. State


No. SC95526


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


862 So. 2d 687; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1778; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 790



October 23, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Owen v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2256 (Fla., Dec. 19, 2003)
Motion granted by Owen v. Florida, 542 U.S. 902, 124 S. Ct. 2851, 159 L. Ed. 2d 266, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 4188 (2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Owen v. Florida, 543 U.S. 986, 125 S. Ct. 494, 160 L. Ed. 2d 370, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7530 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief denied at Owen v. Fla., 2008 Fla. LEXIS 809 (Fla., May 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Harold J. Cohen, Judge-Case No. 84-4014CF A02 T.
Owen v. Crosby, 854 So. 2d 182, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1174 (Fla., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted sexual battery with a deadly weapon or force likely to cause serious personal injury, and burglary of a dwelling while armed. The Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Florida, sentenced him to death pursuant to the jury's recommendation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed a 14-year-old girl 18 times and sexually assaulted her. His first conviction was reversed on appeal. In the appeal from his second conviction, the supreme court held that, as he presented no new evidence, the law of the case doctrine barred him from re-arguing that his confession was not voluntary and should have been suppressed because he had invoked his right to remain silent. Further, the record showed that his confession was voluntary, as he had been Mirandized many times, and had not been threatened or coerced; as his statement to police, " I don't want to talk about it," was equivocal, they had not been required to end their questioning. Evidence of the multiple stab wounds, and defendant's desire to inflict pain and fear, supported the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator. Evidence that he had carefully planned the crime supported the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator. The death sentence was proportionate in light of the aggravators, including his other conviction for a similar murder. Neither Florida's death penalty statute nor the aggravating factor of murder in the course of a specified felony were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the conviction and sentence of death.

604 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Cummings-El v. State


Nos. SC01-1501 & SC02-1784


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


863 So. 2d 246; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1717; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 757



October 9, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County, Joseph P. Farina, Chief Judge - Case No. 91-33268 and

An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Cummings-El v. State, 684 So. 2d 729, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1636 (Fla., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and denied in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate had been convicted of first-degree murder and armed burglary and sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County, Florida, denied the inmate's Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief. He appealed, and also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate broke into his former girlfriend's home and stabbed her to death. He argued that trial counsel should have more thoroughly investigated mitigating evidence about his personal history and mental health. The circuit court found that (1) he waived presentation of mitigating evidence and made it difficult for counsel to obtain such evidence, (2) he did not suffer from a brain injury, (3) counsel's decision not to present evidence of the inmate's drug use or poor upbringing due to its potential to adversely affect the jury was reasonable, and (4) the alleged additional mitigating evidence was essentially the same as evidence presented at the penalty phase. The supreme court agreed that the inmate failed to show the outcome would have been different had the proposed mitigating evidence been presented. As to the habeas petition, appellate counsel was not ineffective for not raising unpreserved claims regarding witness testimony and prosecutorial comments because no fundamental error occurred, or by failing to include with the appellate record the transcript of a hearing in which the inmate complained of trial counsel's representation. The death sentence was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The circuit court's order denying the inmate postconviction relief was affirmed, and his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

605 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Tompkins v. State


No. SC01-1619


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


872 So. 2d 230; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1718; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 177



October 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised April 22, 2004 Released for Publication June 25, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Tompkins v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 547 (Fla., Apr. 22, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Tompkins v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1148 (Fla., June 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: A Notice of Appeal and Cross Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Daniel L. Perry, Judge - Case No. 84-10538.
Tompkins v. State, 502 So. 2d 415, 1986 Fla. LEXIS 3020 (Fla., 1986)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. The Circuit Court, Hillsborough County, Florida, denied in part his successive motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, from which the inmate appealed. Appellee State cross-appealed the postconviction court's order granting the inmate a new penalty phase.


OVERVIEW: The inmate strangled his girlfriend's teenage daughter. The supreme court held the postconviction court's summary denial of the inmate's Brady claim was proper; either the undisclosed documents were not Brady material because they were neither favorable to the inmate nor suppressed, or he failed to show he was prejudiced by the lack of disclosure. The inmate's motion for DNA testing was properly denied, as there was no issue of the identity of the decedent, and any DNA samples obtained would have been contaminated due to the location of the remains and would not prove the inmate's innocence or result in mitigation of his sentence. As the inmate was not required under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.852(i) to wait until the death warrant was signed to make an additional public records request, and he gave no reason as to why the requests were not made until after the death warrant was signed, the trial court properly denied a request for the records. However, the postconviction court erred in granting a new penalty phase based on evidence that the trial court had, ex parte, directed the State to prepare the sentencing order, as the inmate was not prejudiced if the State had prepared the order.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the portion of the postconviction court's order denying the inmate's motion for postconviction relief and reversed the portion of its order granting a new penalty phase. It reinstated the death sentence and ordered the stay of execution dissolved effective 30 days after the instant decision became final.

 

606 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Henry v. State


No. SC02-804


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


862 So. 2d 679; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1719; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 753



October 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 19, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Henry v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2257 (Fla., Dec. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Maynard F. Swanson, Jr., Judge - Case No. 85-2685 CFAES.
Henry v. Florida, 515 U.S. 1148, 132 L. Ed. 2d 839, 115 S. Ct. 2591, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 4190 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The judgment was affirmed on direct appeal. The Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Florida, denied his motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate fatally stabbed his estranged wife. His first conviction was reversed; he was convicted again after a retrial. On appeal, he argued that retrial counsel was ineffective during the guilt and penalty phases. The supreme court held that the defenses retrial counsel presented (self-defense and "depraved mind" second-degree murder) were valid and supported by the evidence, and the inmate's proposed alternative theory of defense was either unsupported by the evidence (voluntary intoxication) or inadmissible (diminished capacity). The inmate argued that retrial counsel was ineffective during the penalty phase for failing to present available mental health mitigation evidence. The supreme court disagreed. Such evidence had been presented in the first trial, which resulted in a death sentence. Retrial counsel specifically chose not to present mental health mitigation through experts because he believed their testimony at the first trial was more devastating than helpful, especially testimony that the inmate was very dangerous. He instead presented evidence from people who knew the inmate that he was a nonviolent, peaceful individual; this was a reasonable strategic decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

607 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sarkis v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. SC02-428


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


863 So. 2d 210; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1710; 119 A.L.R.5th 611; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 740



October 2, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Fifth District - Case No. 5D00-2217 (Brevard County).
Allstate Ins. Co. v. Sarkis, 809 So. 2d 6, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 17190 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insured sued respondent insurer, seeking compensation under her uninsured motorist coverage. The insurer's offer of judgment for $ 10,000 was rejected; the insured was awarded a judgment of $ 87,700. The trial court computed the award of attorney fees to the insured under Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79 by using contingency risk multipliers. The District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida), reversed the fee award. The insured appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the jury verdict returned on behalf of the insured was 25 percent greater than the offer of judgment, thereby entitling her to attorney fees under Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79 and Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442. The district court of appeal held that the trial court erred by applying contingency risk multipliers in computing the attorney fees under Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79. The supreme court agreed. Neither Fla. Stat. ch. 768.79 nor Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442 authorized the use of a multiplier in determining the amount of attorney fees as a sanction for the rejection of an offer. Pirelli Armstrong Tire Corp. v. Jensen, 752 So. 2d 1275 (Fla. 2d Dist. Ct. App. 2000); Island Hoppers, Ltd. v. Keith, 820 So. 2d 967 (Fla. 4th Dist. Ct. App. 2002); and Lewis v. Bondy, 752 So. 2d 1225 (Fla. 1st Dist. Ct. App. 2000), to they extent they held otherwise, were disapproved. The supreme court noted that the trial court did not use the factors of Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442(h)(2) in determining the amount of the attorney fees award. Upon remand, the trial court had to use these factors in calculating the award, as well as the reasonable hourly rate and time.


OUTCOME: The supreme court approved the decision of the court of appeal and remanded for further proceedings in accord with its opinion.

Wilson v. State (Amendments to Fla. Rule of Crim. Procedure 3.853(d)(1)(A))

609 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Miami-Dade County v. Omnipoint Holdings, Inc.


No. SC02-815


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


863 So. 2d 195; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1620; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 717



September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
On remand at, Remanded by, Writ of certiorari denied Miami-Dade County v. Omnipoint Holdings, Inc., 863 So. 2d 375, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 18721 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., Dec. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal--Direct Conflict Third District--Case No. 3D01-2347. (Dade County).
Miami-Dade County v. Omnipoint Holdings, Inc., 811 So. 2d 767, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 2339 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent corporation sought an "unusual use" exception to petitioner county's zoning ordinances. The zoning board denied the application. On review, the circuit court granted the corporation's petition and quashed the zoning board decision. The county petitioned for writ of certiorari in the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which denied the petition and left intact the circuit court's ruling. The supreme court granted jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Because the district court decision exceeded the proper scope of second-tier certiorari review by addressing, sua sponte, the facial constitutionality of the ordinances at issue, the supreme court quashed that decision and remanded for further review. The circuit court had properly limited its remand to the zoning board with instructions to determine the application in accordance with its opinion. The district court modification exceeded its certiorari review power. An appellate court had no power in exercising its jurisdiction in certiorari to direct the corporation to take any particular action. It could only quash the order or decision under review and remand for further proceedings. Instead of limiting itself to addressing the two prongs of second-tier certiorari review, the district court reached an issue neither party raised in any phase of the proceedings. Sua sponte, the district court considered the facial constitutionality of the county ordinances. The district court exceeded the proper scope of second-tier certiorari review when it, sua sponte, held the ordinances in question facially unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court quashed the decision of the district court and remanded to that court with instructions to review the circuit court's decision pursuant to the proper standards.

 

610 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. State


No. SC01-336


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


863 So. 2d 169; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1622; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 731



September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Anderson v. Florida, 541 U.S. 940, 124 S. Ct. 1662, 158 L. Ed. 2d 363, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2104 (2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Anderson v. State, 18 So. 3d 501, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 1021 (Fla., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, G. Richard Singletary, Judge--Case No. 99-572-CF-A-03.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction by the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) and from his death sentence for grand theft of a firearm, robbery with a firearm, attempted first-degree murder, and first-degree murder, following the denial of his motion to suppress statements he made to the police, and the denial of his motion for a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court improperly weighed the aggravating and mitigating factors. The State's highest court held that there was sufficient evidence supporting the convictions. The findings of the cold, calculated, and premeditated manner and the pecuniary gain aggravating factors were supported by substantial evidence. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in considering the mitigating factors of defendant's employment history and his potential for rehabilitation, but assigning them little weight. Allowing the blood stain pattern expert's testimony was not an abuse of discretion. The issues raised as to the denial of the suppression motion were not preserved for review. The photographs of the surviving victim were relevant to show the victim's identity and the location of her wounds. The trial court's curative instruction was sufficient to correct any potential misconception that the jury had about the duty the defense had to rebut the serologist's testimony and the denial of the motion for mistrial was not an abuse of discretion. The prosecutorial misconduct in closing did not entitle defendant to relief. The death sentence was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence of death were affirmed.

 

611 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Griffin v. State


No. SC01-457


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


866 So. 2d 1; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1621; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 723



September 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised January 29, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Griffin v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 104 (Fla., Jan. 29, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Griffin v. Florida, 543 U.S. 962, 125 S. Ct. 413, 160 L. Ed. 2d 328, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7211 (2004)
Related proceeding at Griffin v. State, 104 So. 3d 990, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 1663 (Fla., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Alex E. Ferrer, Judge--Case No. 90-16875-C.
Griffin v. State, 639 So. 2d 966, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1007 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Circuit court's denial of postconviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the denial by the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) of his motion for postconviction relief after his convictions for murder of a law enforcement officer, attempted murder of a law enforcement officer, burglary of a hotel room, grand theft, and the unlawful possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, and his death sentence were affirmed, and the United States Supreme Court denied his petition for certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his trial counsel was ineffective. The State's highest court held that there was not improper ex parte contact with the prosecutor. Trial counsel was not ineffective in not presenting certain mental health and other mitigating evidence, as it could have opened the door to other damaging testimony. The postconviction court properly denied the remaining 19 issues summarily, as the alleged errors were either meritless, procedurally barred, or did not meet the Strickland standard for ineffective assistance of counsel. For instance, conceding guilt to the lesser charges was a recognized strategy. Filing a motion to disqualify the trial judge would not have succeeded, nor would a motion for a change in venue. Defendant did not show that any realistic evidence existed to support his theory that the officers fired the first shot. Eight members of the jury venire were excused due to their opinions in favor of the death penalty, refuting defendant's argument that voir dire was ineffective. Because the alleged individual errors were without merit, the contention of cumulative error was similarly without merit.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

612 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fitzpatrick v. State


No. SC00-2589


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


859 So. 2d 486; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1537; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 679



September 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 31, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Fitzpatrick v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1947 (Fla., Oct. 31, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Lauren C. Laughlin, Judge--Case No. CRC9616773CFANO-D.



DISPOSITION: Conviction reversed, sentence vacated and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida). A jury found that defendant was guilty of first-degree murder and recommended a sentence of death by an eight to four majority, and the trial court sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: The victim was found stabbed to death in his home, and the evidence established that there was no forced entry into his home. Defendant testified that both he and an accomplice accompanied the victim to his home, that the three men consumed alcohol, and that he awoke to see the victim and his accomplice fighting in the kitchen. The court reversed defendant's conviction after concluding that the jury might have relied on an erroneous definition of burglary as the basis for the felony murder conviction. The jury had been instructed on premeditated murder and felony murder, and the felony murder instruction was based on alternate theories, namely, robbery and burglary. However, where an individual entered a dwelling with consent, the burglary statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 810.02, only applied if the individual remained there surreptitiously. As defendant argued, the evidence showed that he was a consensual invitee into the victim's home but did not show that he had surreptitiously remained there. The general jury verdict thus could not stand because one of the prosecution's theories was legally inadequate, and the court could not discern on what grounds defendant had been convicted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction, vacated his sentence, and remanded for a new trial.

 

613 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. State


No. SC01-1998


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


872 So. 2d 226; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1538; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 700



September 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Stewart v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 647 (Fla., Apr. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Barbara Fleischer, Judge--Case No. 85-5667.
Stewart v. State, 620 So. 2d 177, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 826 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida). The trial court resentenced petitioner to death following a new sentencing hearing.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was originally sentenced to death following a murder and robbery. During postconviction proceedings, petitioner agreed to waive any potential guilt-phase claims, and the State agreed to a new sentencing. A jury recommended a death sentence. After weighing three aggravating circumstances and 25 mitigating factors, including two statutory mitigating factors, the trial court again sentenced petitioner to death. The court affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by reducing the weight given to the two statutory mental mitigators from "full weight" to "some weight" in light of the contradictory evidence in the record. The death penalty was also not disproportional even with 25 mitigating factors. Proportionality was not a comparison between the number of aggravating and mitigating factors but was rather a qualitative comparison. Petitioner's death sentence was proportional to other cases where the death sentence had been applied, for example, where there were aggravators of a previous violent felony conviction and pecuniary gain, where both statutory mental mitigators were present, and where there were other nonstatutory mitigators.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment.

 

614 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Diaz v. State


No. SC01-278


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


860 So. 2d 960; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1536; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 687



September 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 18, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Diaz v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2322 (Fla., Nov. 18, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Diaz v. Florida, 541 U.S. 1011, 124 S. Ct. 2068, 158 L. Ed. 2d 622, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 3098 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Diaz v. State, 132 So. 3d 93, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2559 (Fla., 2013)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Stay granted by, Motion granted by Diaz v. Sec'y, DOC, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111195 (M.D. Fla., Aug. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lee County, Thomas S. Reese, Judge--Case No. 97-3305CF.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Lee County (Florida), which entered a conviction against him for first-degree murder and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased a gun, went to his former girlfriend's house, and planned to kill her for allegedly betraying him. However, she managed to drive away, although she was shot. Defendant then confronted the girlfriend's father and fatally shot him. He threatened a neighbor, who then called police and defendant was arrested. The jury found him guilty of first-degree murder and he was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court initially noted that there was sufficient support for the conviction. The court held that application of the aggravating circumstance of heinous, atrocious, and cruel was erroneous, as the trial court misconstrued the evidence. Although defendant reloaded the gun, there was no indication that it was done "slowly," nor was there proof as to which of the five shots caused the fatal injury. However, the court held that such error was harmless, in that two other aggravators were found. The court noted that there was support for the finding that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated, based on the pre-planning of the murder. The doctrine of transferred intent was applicable on this aggravator. The sentence was proportionate to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

615 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. SC00-313


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


859 So. 2d 465; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1539; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 692



September 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Davis v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1948 (Fla., Oct. 31, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Davis v. State, 990 So. 2d 459, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1063 (Fla., June 5, 2008)
Dismissed by State v. Davis, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1162 (Fla., May 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Cynthia A. Holloway, Judge--Case No. 98-11873.
Davis v. State, 789 So. 2d 978, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1407 (Fla., July 12, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death, finding both the heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC), as well as the cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) aggravating factors. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence. The appeals court rejected them all. First, the fact that defendant talked with detectives about the murder prior to receiving a Miranda warning did not by itself affect the admissibility of his subsequent confession. The circumstances surrounding a warned confession properly cured the condition that rendered the unwarned statement inadmissible. Second, each venireperson challenged indicated that they could fairly and impartially consider the evidence presented and apply the law as instructed. Third, there was no basis to determine whether the police detectives could testify as to statements made to them by a co-defendant, under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.804(2)(c). Fourth, the autopsy photographs admitted aided in explaining the examiner's testimony. Fifth, the trial court applied the correct law in considering the disproportionate sentences of the co-defendants. Sixth, given the way the victim was murdered, the evidence supported both the HAC and CCP aggravating factors. Seventh, there was no proportionality error. Finally, defendant's confession to the murder, as well as the events surrounding it, supported the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the sentence were affirmed.

 

616 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


Nos. SC01-734 & SC02-605


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


855 So. 2d 611; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1532



September 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Jones v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1714 (Fla., Sept. 11, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jones v. State, 966 So. 2d 319, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 950 (Fla., May 24, 2007)
Related proceeding at Jones v. State, 93 So. 3d 178, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 818 (Fla., Apr. 26, 2012)
Post-conviction relief denied at Jones v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1943 (Fla., Sept. 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Victoria Platzner, Judge--Case No. 90-50143 and An Original Proceeding--Habeas Corpus.
Jones v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 781 (Fla., May 8, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the lower court's denial of Jones's motion for postconviction relief, and denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from an order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief, brought pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The trial court also denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, arising from his convictions for first-degree murder and armed robbery, and his sentences to death and to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant killed two elderly people that he worked for and he stole their valuables. He was convicted and sentenced, and a direct appeal resulted in an affirmance. His motion for postconviction relief was denied by the trial court. On appeal from that order, the court found that his counsel was not ineffective in failing to investigate, failing to raise the defense of voluntary intoxication, or in failing to provide evidence in mitigation at the penalty phase. The court noted that many claims raised by appellant were found to lack merit because they did not satisfy the two prongs of the Strickland ineffective assistance of counsel test. As to the voluntary intoxication defense, the court found that such was a trial strategy by appellant's counsel and there was no credible evidence to support such a defense. Similarly, there was no finding of credible evidence to support any alleged mitigation factors that appellant raised. The court concluded that appellant's counsel acted reasonably and no prejudice was shown. The court summarily denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus without discussion, and found that the capital sentencing scheme was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus relief.

 

617 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Conde v. State


No. SC00-789


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


860 So. 2d 930; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1474; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 669



September 4, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 5, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Conde v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1949 (Fla., Nov. 5, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Conde v. Florida, 541 U.S. 977, 124 S. Ct. 1885, 158 L. Ed. 2d 475, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2642 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Conde v. State, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 177 (Fla., Feb. 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Jerald Bagley, Judge--Case No. F95-019816.
State v. Conde, 743 So. 2d 78, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 11938 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had sexual relations with a prostitute, strangled her to death, and then disposed of her body by driving it to another location and leaving it on the side of the road. He was charged with six serial murders, all following the same pattern, which counts were severed. He was found guilty of first-degree murder in this, the first murder trial. On appeal, the court found that denial of cause challenges to six prospective jurors was proper because they were shown to be impartial, and the use of Williams rule evidence of the other five murders was proper to establish premeditation. Similarly, evidence that led the police to suspect defendant of the serial murders was relevant. There was sufficient evidence of premeditation to support the denial of defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal. Other evidentiary rulings did not require reversal, and there was no fundamental error in the prosecutor's opening and closing arguments. Defendant's confession was voluntary. There was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's sentencing determination, based on the aggravating and mitigating circumstances found, and the death sentence was proportional to the crime committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

618 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


DeGregorio v. Balkwill


No. SC02-1161


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


853 So. 2d 371; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1406; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 643



August 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 8, 2003.
On remand at In re One 1988 Lincoln Town Car v. Degregorio, 857 So. 2d 341, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 15643 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., Oct. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal--Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District--Case No. 2D01-1249. (Sarasota County).
In re One 1988 Lincoln Town Car v. Balkwill, 826 So. 2d 992, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1997 (Fla., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remaneded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, owner of a seized vehicle, sought review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the owner in respondent sheriff's forfeiture action of his vehicles, under the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 932.701 to -.707 (1999). There was a conflict certified with the Fifth District Court of Appeals as to the effect of the time limitations.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff's office investigated two vehicles on petitioner's business property and determined that the vehicle identification numbers were altered. Accordingly, the sheriff seized the vehicles; almost four months later, he filed a complaint for forfeiture under the Act, based on further investigation that revealed that one vehicle was listed as stolen. However, petitioner filed a bill of sale and a Florida vehicle registration, claiming that he was a bona fide purchaser for value. The trial court granted summary judgment to petitioner, holding that the forfeiture required dismissal because it was filed more than 45 days after seizure. On appeal, the appellate court reversed, holding that the 45-day limit was not a bar and that petitioner lacked standing to assert a claim. On further appeal due to conflict between districts, the court held that the 45-day limit was mandatory, which was the holding espoused by the Fifth District Court of Appeal. The court noted that forfeiture statutes were construed strictly, and by using the word "shall," it was determined that the requirement to "promptly proceed" within 45 days was required under Fla. Stat. chs. 932.704(4) and 932.701(2)(c).


OUTCOME: The court quashed the Second District's decision, approved the holding of the Fifth District with respect to the mandatory nature of the time limits, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

619 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Owen v. Crosby


Nos. SC01-2146 & SC01-2476


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


854 So. 2d 182; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1174; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 615



July 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 2, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Owen v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1525 (Fla., Sept. 2, 2003)
Subsequent appeal at Owen v. State, 862 So. 2d 687, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1778 (Fla., Oct. 23, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Consolidated Cases: An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Hubert R. Lindsey, Judge - Case No. 84-4000CF A02.
Owen v. State, 596 So. 2d 985, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 100 (Fla., 1992



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court's denial of postconviction relief and denied Owen's petition for writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County (Florida) denied appellant inmate's motion for post-conviction relief, filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The inmate appealed that ruling. Additionally, the inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his post-conviction motion. The instant court upheld the denial on his first three claims, because they were raised in a prior Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion and were not based on newly discovered evidence. A fourth claim was insufficiently pled. Because the claims were either successive or insufficiently pled, it was unnecessary to reach the merits of the fifth claim. As to the habeas request, all seven claims of ineffective assistance of counsel were rejected. The fact that appellate counsel could have, but did not, challenge the admission of certain testimony was not deficient. Further, appellate counsel could not be deemed deficient for failing to raise a procedurally barred issue. Third, since the sufficiency of the State's evidence to prove the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator was addressed and disposed of on direct appeal, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a meritless claim. A claim that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to argue that the trial court did not properly consider all of the mitigation was meritless. Finally, his conflict of interest claim was rejected as insufficiently pled.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying post-conviction relief was affirmed, and the writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

620 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fennie v. State


Nos. SC01-2480 & SC02-1180


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


855 So. 2d 597; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1176; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 619



July 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 18, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Fennie v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1935 (Fla., Sept. 18, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Fennie v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1936 (Fla., Sept. 18, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Fennie v. Florida, 541 U.S. 975, 124 S. Ct. 1877, 158 L. Ed. 2d 471, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2611 (2004)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Claim dismissed by Fennie v. Crosby, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15308 (M.D. Fla., Apr. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hernando County, and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus. Richard Tombrink, Jr., Judge - Case No. 91-756-CF.
Fennie v. State, 648 So. 2d 95, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1004 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the circuit court's denial of Fennie's rule 3.850 motion and denied his habeas petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of first degree murder, robbery with a firearm, and armed kidnapping and was sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Hernando County, Florida, denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. He appealed, and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The victim was found with her hands bound and a gunshot wound to her head. The inmate was found in possession of her car, rope matching that used to bind her, and the murder weapon. His accomplice testified against him under a plea bargain. The supreme court held that application of the Cronic presumption of prejudice standard based on egregiously deficient performance by counsel during voir dire was not supported by the record, as counsel conducted a vigorous voir dire, and two jurors and both alternate jurors were black (as was the inmate). Though the sentencing order did not comply with Campbell, as the trial court failed to assign weights to aggravating and mitigating circumstances on an individualized basis, there was no fundamental error, since the order was otherwise thorough and detailed. The State's reference to the inmate's uncharged sexual encounter with the victim was supported by testimony and was used to rebut his claim that he had consensual sex with the victim, and as support for statutory aggravators--not to establish nonstatutory aggravation. The State's comments about the victim's last words were based on testimony and were neither hypothetical nor improper.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's denial of the inmate's motion for post-conviction relief and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

621 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Allen v. State


No. SC02-371, No. SC02-1079


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


854 So. 2d 1255; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1156; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 604



July 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Allen v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1713 (Fla., Sept. 8, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Allen v. State, 957 So. 2d 635, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 367 (Fla., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Monroe County, Richard Payne, Judge - Case No. 92-30056-CF and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Allen v. State, 662 So. 2d 323, 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1148 (Fla., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Postconviction relief denied, petition for habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and grand theft of an automobile. He was sentenced to death. The state supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The Circuit Court in and for Monroe County (Florida) denied the motion without an evidentiary hearing. Defendant appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised 18 claims. Sixteen of the claims were summarily affirmed because they were procedurally barred or lacked merit. Only the first and fifth claims, asserting a Brady violation and ineffective assistance of counsel, were addressed. The state supreme court concluded that the State's failure to disclose the hair analysis did not prejudice defendant. It was undisputed that defendant was present at the scene shortly before the victim's death. The jury concluded that defendant killed the victim, stole her $ 4,100, fled with her car to a lodge, abandoned the car there, and continued his getaway in a taxi. The fact that two hairs found in or on the victim's hand did not belong to defendant did not place the case in such a different light as to undermine confidence in the verdict. Also, although trial counsel did question the medical examiner about the possibility of suicide, such questioning was only a small part of an overall defense that defendant did not commit the murder. Finally, defendant's habeas corpus claims were denied because one claim had already been raised on direct appeal, and the other had been rejected by the state supreme court in a previous case.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed the denial of defendant's postconviction motion and denied the petition for habeas corpus.


 

622 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


N. Fla. Women's Health & Counseling Servs. v. State


No. SC01-843


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


866 So. 2d 612; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1160; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 549



July 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 23, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal -Statutory Validity First District - Case Nos. 1D00-1983 and 1D00-2106 (Leon County).
Fla. Dep't of Health v. N. Fla. Women's Health & Counseling Servs., Inc., 852 So. 2d 254, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 1217 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Court quashed the district court's decision and approved the trial court's decision permanently enjoining enforcement of the Parental Notice Act.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When the Parental Notice Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 390.01115 (1999) was enacted, petitioners, several women's clinics, women's rights groups, and physicians sought injunctive and declaratory relief to block the enforcement of the Act, claiming that it violated a minor's constitutional rights. The trial court agreed, but the First District Court of Appeal, Florida, reversed. The women's groups appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the women's groups contended that the trial court properly applied a prior case as controlling precedent in finding the Act unconstitutional. Emphasizing the doctrine of stare decisis, the supreme court declined the State's invitation to recede from the prior case's decision. The supreme court held that the Act's requirement that a minor must notify a parent of her decision to have an abortion violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 23, as it was a significant intrusion on a minor's right of privacy. Further, the district court's ultimate determination, that the Act furthered a compelling State interest because it allowed parents to assist in giving post-abortion care to a minor, was controverted by the findings of the trial court. The trial court found that, while such parental support was preferable, most minors, especially older minors, were capable of following directions for aftercare treatment. By ignoring the trial court's findings, the district court violated the basic precept of appellate review. Any comparison between the federal and Florida rights of privacy was inapposite, in light of the fact that there was no express federal right of privacy clause.


OUTCOME: The district court's holding was quashed, and the trial court's decision permanently enjoining enforcement of the Act was approved.

Nelson v. State


No. SC00-876


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


850 So. 2d 514; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1170; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 579



July 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nelson v. Florida, 540 U.S. 1091, 124 S. Ct. 961, 157 L. Ed. 2d 797, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 9241 (Dec. 15, 2003)
Petition dismissed by Nelson v. State, 969 So. 2d 1014, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2094 (Fla., Oct. 26, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Nelson v. State, 43 So. 3d 20, 2010 Fla. LEXIS 647 (Fla., Apr. 29, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, J. Michael Hunter, Judge.
Nelson v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1947 (Fla., Oct. 3, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, Florida, of first-degree murder, burglary of a dwelling with a battery, grand theft (motor vehicle), kidnapping, burglary of a conveyance with a battery, and sexual battery. He was sentenced to death, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant broke into the elderly victim's home, robbed and raped her, put her in the trunk of her car, took her to a secluded area, and killed her. He was found asleep in the victim's car, and, after an interrogation, confessed to the killing and took police to the body. The supreme court held that (1) an officer's reference to DNA evidence, where DNA tests had not yet been performed, and (2) his reference to finding the victim's body so that it could be buried (the "Christian burial" technique) were insufficient to make defendant's otherwise voluntary statement inadmissible. As defendant drove around with the victim in the trunk for several hours and took her to two remote locations before killing her through the use of multiple means, the trial court properly found the "cold, calculated, and premeditated" aggravator. It properly found the "avoid arrest" aggravator, as defendant admitted he killed the victim because he was afraid she could identify him. It was entitled to disregard defendant's expert's opinion that defendant was under extreme mental or emotional disturbance if it felt that the opinion was unsupported by facts. The death penalty was not a disproportionate sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Belcher v. State


No. SC01-1414


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


851 So. 2d 678; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1161; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 575



July 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Belcher v. Florida, 540 U.S. 1054, 124 S. Ct. 816, 157 L. Ed. 2d 706, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 8687 (Dec. 1, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Belcher v. State, 961 So. 2d 239, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1050 (Fla., June 14, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by, Certificate of appealability denied Belcher v. Sec'y of the Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 108300 (M.D. Fla., Sept. 28, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Remanded by Belcher v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 2183 (Fla., Nov. 2, 2017)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Duval County (Florida) convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence. The appeals court first held that eyewitness testimony connected him to the victim and incriminating physical evidence linked him to her home where her body was found. Thus, the evidence supported the conviction. Second, defendant was not entitled to a mistrial due to the prosecutor's penalty phase closing argument in which he stated that defendant's actions were to eliminate the victim as a witness. Third, the prosecutor's argument of an improper aggravating circumstance did not taint the penalty phase nor did it cause the death sentence to be unconstitutionally imposed. Fourth, after trial court gave serious consideration to defendant's special instruction, it was not superior to the catch-all instruction. Fifth, prior convictions were exempt from facts that had to be submitted to a jury because they increased the penalty for a crime. Because a unanimous jury convicted defendant of both murder and sexual battery, the guilt phase verdicts reflected that the jury independently found the aggravator of the murder being committed in the course of a sexual battery. Finally, the death sentence was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Both the conviction and the sentence were affirmed.

Wright v. State


No. SC00-1389, No. SC01-2866


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


857 So. 2d 861; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1144; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 517



July 3, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Wright v. Crosby, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1785 (Fla., Oct. 10, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wright v. Crosby, 541 U.S. 961, 124 S. Ct. 1715, 158 L. Ed. 2d 402, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2416 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Wright v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1637 (Fla., Sept. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County, A. W. Nichols, III, Judge - Case No. 83-0376-CF-52 and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Wright v. State, 770 So. 2d 163, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1685 (Fla., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County (Florida) of first-degree murder, sexual battery, burglary of a dwelling, and grand theft. After his direct appeal and his first motion for postconviction relief were denied, he filed a second motion for postconviction relief. The trial court denied the motion. He appealed and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate raped and murdered the victim while robbing her home. In the appeal, the supreme court found that (1) in the first postconviction proceeding, the trial court did not make false findings that were erroneously adopted on appeal; (2) the State did not fail to disclose exculpatory evidence; (3) there was no newly discovered admissible evidence of innocence; (4) while the inmate's appointed trial counsel and his investigator were bonded deputy sheriffs, this did not interfere with their ability to provide effective assistance of counsel; and (5) disqualification of the trial judge was not warranted by the judge's failure to reveal at the time of trial and the first postconviction proceeding that he was a special deputy sheriff. In the habeas petition, the supreme court found that (1) the State did not fail to disclose pertinent facts; (2) appellate counsel did not fail to raise numerous meritorious issues on appeal; (3) the presiding judge did not unconstitutionally make factual findings in support of the death sentence; and (4) the supreme court did not fail to make an appropriate harmless error analysis after striking an aggravating circumstance on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed; furthermore, the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Nettles v. State


No. SC02-1523


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


850 So. 2d 487; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1068; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 487



June 26, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions First District. Case No. 1D01-3441. (Escambia County).
Nettles v. State, 819 So. 2d 243, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 8428 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion, pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b)(2), to correct a sentence that was imposed by the Circuit Court of Escambia County (Florida) after he entered pleas to attempted lewd and lascivious conduct. The trial court denied the motion and the Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court of appeal certified the existence of a conflict between appellate court decisions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered pleas to two counts of attempted lewd and lascivious conduct, a third-degree felony, in exchange for concurrent sentences of 66.4 months under Florida's Prison Releasee Reoffender Punishment Act (PRRPA), Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(9) (2000), and Florida's Criminal Punishment Code (CPC), Fla. Stat. chs. 921.002 to 921.0027 (2000). During the plea colloquy, the judge advised him that the PRRPA designation would require him to serve the entire sentence day-for-day. Nevertheless, he filed a motion to correct his sentence, arguing his sentence was illegal under State v. Wilson, 793 So. 2d 1003 (Fla. 2d DCA 2001) and Irons v. State, 791 So. 2d 1221 (Fla. 5th DCA 2001). The trial court denied the motion and the Court of Appeal of Florida, First District, affirmed. The supreme court held PRRPA established a mandatory minimum sentence and did not prevent the trial court from imposing a greater sentence of incarceration as authorized by law; and the trial court did not violate defendant's rights by sentencing him to 60 months under the PRRPA and an additional 6.4 months under CPC. To the extent Wilson and Irons were inconsistent with the decision, they were disapproved.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court approved the intermediate appellate court's decision.

Duest v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

June 26, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Duest v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1942 (Fla., Sept. 8, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Duest v. Florida, 541 U.S. 993, 124 S. Ct. 2023, 158 L. Ed. 2d 500, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 2835 (2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at Duest v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 246 (Fla., Feb. 19, 2009)

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an opinion of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which, after a new penalty phase was held on his conviction of first-degree murder in a general verdict, imposed a death sentence on him after the prior sentence of death that had been imposed was vacated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder after he had indicated his intention to "roll a fag," had a knife, was seen in a gay bar talking to the victim and then leaving with him, and thereafter, the victim was found dead of multiple stab wounds. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death, which was affirmed on appeal. However, the sentence was reversed due to a judicial precedent. The court's proportionality review affirmed that the sentence of death was appropriate in the circumstances. The court declined to apply the Ring requirement of submitting the existence of facts necessary to impose the death penalty to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the opinion of the trial court.

Cooper v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the circuit court affirmed, and Cooper's habeas petition denied.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 from his convictions for three counts of first-degree murder and sentences of death. He also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and his accomplices went into a residence in the middle of the night and shot the three adult occupants to death. Their decisions regarding whether to present mitigating evidence and regarding his mental state at the time of the crimes were strategically reasonable, and there was no reason to have sought a continuance. Although it was error to have allowed the State to present evidence of his lack of remorse, there was no prejudice that resulted therefrom. The sentencing order was found to have been made appropriately.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court with respect to the inmate's motion for postconviction relief, and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Hodges v. State


Nos. SC01-1718 & SC02-949


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


885 So. 2d 338; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1062; 29 Fla. L. Weekly S 598



June 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised October 14, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Hodges v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 1812 (Fla., Oct. 14, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Hodges v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2467 (Fla., Dec. 22, 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hodges v. Crosby, 907 So. 2d 1170, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1526 (Fla., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Dennis P. Maloney, Judge - Case No. 89-2165.
Hodges v. State, 619 So. 2d 272, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 679 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Court affirmed the trial court's decision denying Hodges' motion for postconviction relief and denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 from his conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death. He also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for indecent exposure and his victim was found shot and later died. Appellant was indicted by a grand jury and convicted of first-degree murder. During the penalty phase when the jury had already retired, he tried to commit suicide. He was accordingly absent from the trial court's discussion of the jury's request on instructions, and was still absent when they returned with their death sentence recommendation. Appeals resulted in an affirmance, and appellant sought a writ of habeas corpus and postconviction relief. The court held that his counsel's background investigation was sufficient, and accordingly there was no ineffective assistance. There was no due process violation by the State's conducting mental health evaluations shortly before his postconviction evidentiary hearing, nor was there an Ake rule violation. The judge's conversations with the State's counsel were impartial and concerned administrative matters. Summary denial of an evidentiary hearing on certain claims was proper where they were already appealed or could have been, and an objection to a potential juror's dismissal did not properly preserve the issue for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court and denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

Welsh v. State


No. SC02-1092


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


850 So. 2d 467; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1049; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 452



June 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 5, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions First District - Case No. 1D01-648 (Duval County).
Welsh v. State, 816 So. 2d 175, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 5891 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a trial court decision which denied his request for an instruction on lewd and lascivious conduct as a lesser included offense of sexual battery in his trial on both charges, under Fla. Stat. chs. 800.04, 797.011(2)(a) (1997). The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the denial of such an instruction and the matter was certified for review due to a conflict with other decisions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with capital sexual battery upon a person less than 12 years of age and with lewd and lascivious assault of the victim, in violation of Fla. Stat. chs. 794.011(2)(a), 800.04(1) (1997). The trial court denied defendant's request for a lesser included offense instruction of lewd and lascivious conduct with respect to the sexual battery charge. Defendant was convicted on both counts and sentenced. On appeal, the First District held that the trial court properly denied the requested instruction. The matter was certified for review due to holdings in other precedents which indicated that such an instruction was permitted. The court adopted the First District's reasoning, holding that the crimes of sexual battery and lewd and lascivious conduct were mutually exclusive, and accordingly, a lesser included instruction was inappropriate. The court reviewed the statutory language and the Schedule of Lesser Included Offenses in arriving at its conclusion. Accordingly, it noted its disapproval, to the extent of a conflict, with the holdings of King v. State, 642 So.2d 649 (Fla. 2d DCA 1994), and Velazquez v. State, 648 So.2d 302 (Fla. 5th DCA 1995).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the First District's holding that the instruction requested by defendant was not permitted.

Harvey v. State


No. SC01-1139


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


848 So. 2d 1060; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1051; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 470



June 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Vacated by, Corrected by Harvey v. State, 850 So. 2d 675, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 11439 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., July 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 1D99-4629 (Duval County).
Harvey v. State, 786 So. 2d 28, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 5954 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) denying defense counsel's motion to withdraw his Anders brief and finding that defendant failed to preserve his sentencing issue as to his probation violation sentence, as no Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b) (as amended) (2000) motion was filed. The intermediate court certified the issue as a question of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that to require him to raise a single subject challenge to 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 184 by filing a motion to correct sentencing error under Rule 3.800(b) would have been a useless act because at the time that he filed his first appellate brief, Trapp v. State, 736 So. 2d 736 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1999) was binding precedent and resolved the issue against him. The State's highest court held that defendant should not be penalized for the failure to file a Rule 3.800(b)(2) motion based on speculation that the Heggs opinion would disapprove the Trapp decision. There was no sentencing error at the time the Anders brief was filed. The Heggs decision was issued a week later, and created a sentencing error that did not exist before the first brief was filed. Defense counsel filed a motion to withdraw his Anders brief and an initial brief on the merits raising the Heggs issue two weeks later, notwithstanding the fact that Rule 3.800(b) was applicable to defendant. Due to the interests of justice, judicial efficiency, and the unique circumstances of the case, defendant was permitted to raise his Heggs error as a fundamental sentencing error for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated. The case was remanded for resentencing in accordance with the laws in effect on the date on which defendant committed his original offense. The intermediate court's decision was quashed, and the certified question was answered in the affirmative for the limited purpose it expressed.

633 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Brannon v. State


No. SC01-1538


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


850 So. 2d 452; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1055; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 456



June 12, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 1D99-4243. (Taylor County).
Brannon v. State, 792 So. 2d 498, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 3421 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) declined to address sentencing issues raised by defendant, as they were unpreserved, and denied his motion for rehearing. The court did however certify two questions of great public importance for further review.


OVERVIEW: The two questions for review were: (1) whether the concept of fundamental sentencing error applied to defendants who could have availed themselves of the most recent amendments to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(b); and, (2) Did the Florida Supreme Court decision in Maddox v. State preclude the district court from ruling on the issue as a matter of fundamental error? The supreme court answered no to the first question, with the exception of fundamental error arising from the facial unconstitutionality of a sentencing statute, and yes to the second, approving the decision below. Defendant did not raise his unpreserved sentencing errors in the trial court before presenting them in his direct appeal. He filed the initial appeal brief more than a year after the window for raising unpreserved sentencing errors on appeal closed. Thus, he was precluded from raising his claims for the first time on appeal. Finally, the supreme court reaffirmed that the window period recognized for raising unpreserved fundamental sentencing errors closed with the effective date of amendments to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.111(e), 3.800 and Fla. R. App. P. 9.020(h), 9.140, 9.600, and not with the issuance of Maddox.


OUTCOME: The decision in the appellate court was approved.

 

634 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Marshall v. State


No. SC00-1186


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


854 So. 2d 1235; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1056; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 461



June 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Marshall v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1656 (Fla., Sept. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County, Dwight L. Geiger, Judge. Case No. 89-174 CFA.
Marshall v. State, 604 So. 2d 799, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1274 (Fla., July 16, 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who had been convicted of and sentenced to death for murder, filed a motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The Circuit Court, Martin County, Florida, denied his motion, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of killing another inmate. He claimed the trial court erred in denying an evidentiary hearing on his claim of juror misconduct. He presented an affidavit of a lawyer who alleged that a woman claiming she was a juror at the inmate's trial told the lawyer that jurors (1) told racial jokes about the inmate, (2) said they would vote for guilt and a life sentence because they wanted the inmate to go back to prison to kill more black inmates, and (3) discussed outside articles about the trial in violation of a court order. The supreme court held that the trial court erred in finding that this alleged juror misconduct inhered in the verdict, and thus could not be considered. Appeals to racial bias made openly among jurors, and any receipt by jurors of prejudicial non-record information, constituted sufficient overt acts of misconduct to permit court inquiry. As the inmate had advised his trial counsel that he had not been abused as a child, counsel was not ineffective for failing to investigate the abuse issue. He failed to prove a Brady or a Giglio violation; and even if he had, he failed to show that such violation could have affected the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed, with the exception of the claim of juror misconduct. The case was remanded for an evidentiary hearing on that claim, with the scope of the hearing limited to attempting to obtain the identity of the juror who spoke to the attorney about alleged misconduct, to interview her, and then to conduct further interviews only if the court determined there was a reasonable probability of juror misconduct.

Taylor v. State


No. SC96959


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


855 So. 2d 1; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 926; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 439



June 5, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 8, 2003.

Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Taylor v. State, 120 So. 3d 540, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 1137 (Fla., May 30, 2013)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Clay County (Florida), which entered a conviction against him for first-degree murder and robbery with a deadly weapon, and imposed a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery and murder. The record revealed that the victim was seen with defendant in her car, and she indicated to witnesses that she was giving him a ride. The court found sufficient evidence to support the convictions. PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida) of first-degree murder and armed robbery. Moreover, the postconviction court did not deny defendant access to public records. Additionally, Florida's capital sentencing scheme was not unconstitutional. Finally, the supreme court did not affirm defendant's death sentence without assessing proportionality.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion for postconviction relief was affirmed; and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

State v. Diaz


No. SC01-2779


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


850 So. 2d 435; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 802; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 397



May 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Diaz, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1357 (Fla., July 15, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Florida v. Diaz, 540 U.S. 1075, 124 S. Ct. 936, 157 L. Ed. 2d 745, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 9029 (U.S., Dec. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions

Second District - Case No. 2D00-3542.

(Hillsborough County).
Diaz v. State, 800 So. 2d 326, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 15984 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which certified direct conflict with the Fourth and Fifth District Court of Appeal's decisions in Bass and Wikso relating to detention of a motorist after the purposes of an investigatory stop had been removed.


OVERVIEW: Because a police officer could not read a temporary tag on defendant's vehicle as it drove by, the officer initiated a traffic stop pursuant to Fla. Stat. chs. 320.131(4), 316.605(1) (2000). Although the officer read the tag as he approached the car and found nothing improper, he obtained information from defendant, which ultimately led to a charge of felony driving with a suspended license. The state supreme court held that pursuant to U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV and Fla. Const. art. I, § 12, the original purpose of the investigatory stop was satisfied before the officer made personal contact with defendant. Having verified the total validity of defendant's temporary tag, the officer could lawfully make personal contact only to explain the reason for the initial stop. Therefore, to the extent they were inconsistent, the Wikso and Bass decisions were disapproved.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the conflict was resolved.

Jones v. State


Nos. SC01-734 & SC02-605

2003 Fla. LEXIS 781; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 701

Related proceeding at, Appeal dismissed by Jones v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 615 (Fla., Feb. 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Victoria Platzner, Judge - Case No. 90-50143 and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Miami-Dade County v. Jones, 793 So. 2d 902, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1658 (Fla., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate incarcerated under a sentence of death as a result of his convictions for two counts of first-degree murder and two counts of armed robbery, appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) which denied his motion for postconviction relief. On direct appeal, the convictions and sentences had been affirmed. Defendant also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed an elderly couple. Defendant told a nurse they owed him money. Defendant claimed his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to investigate and present a voluntary intoxication defense, and that he was prejudiced because such intoxication negated specific intent, the requisite mental state for first-degree murder. Counsel stated he did not pursue a voluntary intoxication defense for several reasons. First, it was his experience that juries did not accept voluntary intoxication as a defense or mitigating factor, especially when the charge was murder. In addition, defendant told counsel that he was not intoxicated at the time of the murders and that he was innocent. The trial court found none of defendant's witnesses to be credible. The appellate court held defendant did not establish ineffective assistance of counsel in regard to presenting an intoxication defense. The trial court's conclusion that counsel's investigation as to mitigation was reasonable and that defendant failed to establish prejudice was also proper, as counsel could not be deemed ineffective for not presenting conflicting opinions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

640 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Physicians Healthcare Plans, Inc. v. Pfeifler


Nos. SC01-2062 & SC01-2079


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


846 So. 2d 1129; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 666; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 370



May 1, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION: Stay lifted; writ of prohibition denied; remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patients sued appellants, the health care plan and the physicians, in the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit (Florida), for medical malpractice. The case was set for trial on the senior judges' docket. The health care plan and the physicians filed a motion in circuit court to return the case to the elected circuit judge. The circuit court denied the motion. The health care plan and the physician filed writs of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: The health care plan and the physicians challenged the senior judges' docket in the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit and sought to prohibit the assignment of senior judges to preside over long trial medical malpractice and other complex litigation cases. The supreme court found that the Florida Constitution permitted the appointment of nonelected judges, as this was not a violation of suffrage rights. Further, the senior judge assignments in the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit were compatible with the supreme court's instructions and guidance. The senior judge assignments were used to maximize the efficient administration of justice and had the practical effect of supplementing and assisting the circuit court judges rather than usurping the judges' jurisdiction over a particular type of case. Additionally, the senior judge assignments were temporary and thus did not violate the constitutional parameters of Fla. Const. art. V, § 2(b). Finally, the use of senior judges to relieve overcrowding of the civil and criminal dockets in the Seventeenth Judicial Circuit did not constitute a complex case division that required approval by local rule. Thus, the senior judge assignments were proper.


OUTCOME: The petitions for writ of prohibition were denied, the stay on further proceedings below was lifted, and the cause was remanded to the judicial circuit.

Randolph v. State

PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County,

Robert Mathis, Judge - Case No. 88-1357 and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Randolph v. State, 562 So. 2d 331, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 625 (Fla., 1990)



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction relief denied; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery, sexual battery with force likely to cause serious personal injury or with a deadly weapon, and grand theft of a motor vehicle, appealed from an order of the Circuit Court in and for Putnam County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant also petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought postconviction relief. The trial court denied relief. The appellate court found a number of defendant's postconviction claims to be either procedurally barred, facially or legally insufficient, or clearly without merit as a matter of law.
