Wilson v. State


Nos. SC01-2083 & SC01-2333


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


845 So. 2d 142; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 498; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 311



April 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Judgment entered by, Remanded by Wilson v. State, 846 So. 2d 1201, 2003 Fla. App. LEXIS 8245 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., June 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict. Fourth District - Case No. 4D99-3398. (Broward County).

Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Fifth District - Case No. 5D99-2203. (Orange County).
Wilson v. State, 792 So. 2d 601, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 11460 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2001)
Byrd v. State, 794 So. 2d 671, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 11375 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved in part and quashed in part the Fifth District's decision in Byrd; quashed the Fourth District's decision in Wilson in part; and remanded both cases.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(3), the court accepted applications for review of directly conflicting judgments of the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District, Orange County, and the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Broward County (Florida). The first trial court found a presumption of vindictiveness in a first defendant's sentence, while the second trial court found no such presumption as to a second defendant's sentence.


OVERVIEW: In both cases, trial judges participated in unsuccessful plea negotiations. After trials or hearings, both trial judges sentenced the defendants to harsher punishments than those they had rejected. The first intermediate appellate court held that the trial judge's participation raised a presumption of vindictiveness, but the second intermediate appellate court refused to so find. The court held that the presumption did not arise automatically and that the appropriate analysis was a totality of the circumstances review. As to the first defendant, the court found an unrebutted presumption of vindictiveness because the trial court improperly urged the first defendant to accept the plea offer and the disparity between the offered sentence and the one imposed was large. The presumption arose as to the second defendant because the trial judge departed from the role of a neutral arbiter by stating that the offer should have been accepted and the record lacked facts to explain the increased sentence. The court held that the appropriate remedy when an unrebutted presumption of vindictiveness arose was resentencing before a different trial judge. Both cases were remanded for that purpose.


OUTCOME: As to the first defendant, the court approved the holding that an unrebutted presumption of vindictiveness had arisen but quashed the remedy and the determination that the presumption arose automatically. As to the second defendant, the court quashed the decision to the extent that no presumption of vindictiveness was found. Both cases were remanded for resentencing before a different trial judge.


 

643 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Demps


Nos. SC01-1301, SC02-302


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


846 So. 2d 457; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 467; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 307



April 3, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Released for Publication May 14, 2003. Rehearing denied by State v. Demps, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 829 (Fla., May 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: Notices of Appeal and Cross-Appeal in and for Bradford County, Larry G. Turner, Judge - Case No. 77-0116-CFA.
Demps v. State, 761 So. 2d 302, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1112 (Fla., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Bradford County Circuit Court, Florida awarded attorney's fees and expert witness fees in hearings arising from the representation of defendant during the pendency of his final death warrant. The State appealed and one of the attorney's cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The first attorney claimed that he was entitled to be compensated at a higher hourly rate under the circumstances of the case. The supreme court held that an order awarding attorney's fees and costs to a second attorney was reversed, and the case was remanded with directions to enter an order awarding fees and costs corresponding to the rate specified in Fla. Stat. chs. 27.703, 27.711(4) (1999). That portion of the order finding the statutory rate of compensation to be unconstitutional as applied to that attorney was also reversed. Second, the award to the first attorney was affirmed, pursuant to Fla. Stat. chs. 27.710(6), 27.711(4) (1999). The State did not contest the number of hours expended by both the first and second attorney and agreed with fees as reduced to the hourly rate of $ 100 as long as the court made clear the statutory authority for these amounts. Next, the award of attorney's fees to a third attorney was reversed based on the lack of statutory authority for the award, and the award of expert witness fees to both experts was reversed.


OUTCOME: The fee award to the first attorney was affirmed. In discussion of the awards to the second and third attorney, as well as the fees awarded to the experts, the awards were reversed, and the request for appellate fees was denied.

 

644 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Butler v. State


No. SC95158


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


842 So. 2d 817; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 469; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 298



April 3, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 3, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Butler v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 778 (Fla., Apr. 3, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Butler v. State, 100 So. 3d 638, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 1362 (Fla., 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Motion denied by Butler v. Sec'ym Dep't of Corr., 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 57711 (M.D. Fla., Jan. 24, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Frank Quesada, Judge - Case No. CRC 97-04690 CFANO-A.
Butler v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 876 (Fla., May 9, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder in the Circuit Court, Pinellas County, Florida, and was sentenced to death. The trial court denied defendant's motion for new trial. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant fatally stabbed and asphyxiated his former girlfriend. He had told a coworker he was going to kill the victim. Blood on sneakers that were identified as defendant's had a DNA profile consistent with the victim's. The jury convicted defendant and recommended death. The trial judge found one aggravator -- that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel -- and four mitigators. The supreme court held that cross-examination of defendant and other defense witnesses as to defendant's prior assaults on the victim was proper, as this evidence explained and modified direct testimony, was relevant, and its probative value was not outweighed by the prejudicial effect. The State's DNA expert was qualified to testify as to population frequencies of the DNA profile she discovered; while she did not help create the database, she was familiar with samples from which it was created. Nondisclosure of a State witness's probation violation report did not violate Brady, as there was no showing the report was material. The trial court adequately considered the impaired capacity mitigator, the death sentence was proportional, and Florida's capital sentencing scheme was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

645 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Parker v. State


No. SC01-1013


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


843 So. 2d 871; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 459; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 262



March 27, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Fourth District - Case No. 4D00-3914 (Broward County).
Parker v. State, 780 So. 2d 210, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 1089 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After petitioner posted bond in a criminal case, he was arrested on other charges. The trial court found probable cause for the second arrest and revoked the bond in the first case. Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus on grounds that the bond revocation statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 903.0471 (2000), was unconstitutional. The District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), denied the petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with various crimes and was released on bond. Later, he was arrested for drug charges and was again released on bond. The State notified the court of the second arrest; the trial court revoked the bond in the first case without an adversarial hearing. The supreme court rejected petitioner's contention that ch. 903.0471 violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 14, dealing with pretrial release and detention. Fla. Stat. ch. 903.0471 did not violate, but worked hand-in-hand with, Fla. Const. art. I, § 14 to assure the integrity of the judicial process. Fla. Stat. ch. 903.0471 did not violate substantive due process by authorizing a court to deny a second pretrial release upon finding probable cause that a petitioner committed a new crime, as probable cause, which was a sufficient basis on which to make an arrest, was not too low a standard to be constitutional. And ch. 903.0471 did not violate procedural due process by not requiring an adversarial hearing prior to revocation of pretrial release, as the U.S. Constitution allowed a probable cause determination to be made by a judicial officer without an adversarial hearing.


OUTCOME: The statute was held to comport with the Florida and U.S. Constitutions.

 

646 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Grim v. State


No. SC01-256


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


841 So. 2d 455; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 384; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 247



March 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Grim v. Florida, 540 U.S. 892, 124 S. Ct. 230, 157 L. Ed. 2d 166, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5844 (2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Grim v. State, 971 So. 2d 85, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1842 (Fla., 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Grim v. Buss, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 50280 (N.D. Fla., Mar. 31, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Kenneth B. Bell, Judge - Case No. 98-510.
Grim v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1944 (Fla., Oct. 3, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Florida, of first-degree murder and sexual battery upon a person 12 years of age or older with use of a deadly weapon. He was sentenced to death for the first-degree murder conviction and sentenced consecutively to 390.5 months' imprisonment for the sexual battery conviction. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim was bludgeoned and stabbed to death and dumped in a bay. Blood with genetic markers consistent with hers was found at the home of defendant, her neighbor. After defendant was found guilty, he insisted that no mitigating evidence be presented to the jury. The trial court honored this request, but appointed special counsel to present mitigating evidence outside the presence of the jury. The supreme court held that the trial court did not err in giving great weight to the jury's recommendation of a death sentence and had not been required to have mitigation evidence presented to the jury, due to defendant's knowledgeable waiver. The trial court independently weighed aggravating and mitigating circumstances before imposing the death sentence the jury recommended, which was proper. It did not err by excluding the victim's hearsay statements that her life had been threatened by an unnamed party or parities, as no exception to the hearsay rule applied and there was no evidence tending to connect such person to the crime. The death penalty was proportional in light of the aggravating factors. Florida's capital sentencing scheme was not unconstitutional under Ring v. Arizona.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Lawrence v. State


No. SC00-1827


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


846 So. 2d 440; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 386; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 241



March 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Lawrence v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 825 (Fla., May 14, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lawrence v. Florida, 540 U.S. 952, 124 S. Ct. 394, 157 L. Ed. 2d 286, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 7526 (2003)
Related proceeding at Rodgers v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2120 (Fla., Nov. 24, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Lawrence v. State, 969 So. 2d 294, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2012 (Fla., 2007)

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Kenneth B. Bell, Judge - Case No. 98-270-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pled guilty to principal to first degree murder, conspiracy to commit first degree murder, giving alcoholic beverages to a person under 21, and abuse of a dead human corpse, appealed from a judgement of the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida), which gave him the death penalty. Defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to order an evidentiary competency hearing during the trial.


OVERVIEW: Co-defendant had picked up the 18-year-old victim. They met defendant, and all three then drove in defendant's truck to a secluded area in the woods. After imbibing alcoholic beverages, the victim had sex with co-defendant and then with defendant. At some point thereafter, co-defendant shot the victim in the back of the head using defendant's gun. Defendant subsequently cut out the victim's calf muscle. Co-defendant took pictures of the body, including a picture of defendant's hand holding the victim's foot. Defendant kept the calf muscle refrigerated at home. The trial court found that the greater weight of the evidence did not establish that defendant acted under extreme duress or under the substantial domination of another person. No competency hearing was requested. The appellate court held the trial court did not abuse its discretion by not conducting a competency hearing during the penalty phase. Other than defendant's self-serving confession, the record contained no direct evidence that co-defendant had dominated defendant or that defendant's participation was minor. Defendant's death sentence was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Banks v. State


Nos. SC01-1153 & SC02-63


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


842 So. 2d 788; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 387; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 253



March 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Banks v. Crosby, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 15427 (N.D. Fla., July 29, 2005)
Later proceeding at Banks v. State, 97 So. 3d 821, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 1061 (Fla., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Gadsden County, William L. Gary, Judge - Case No. 92-841-CFA and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Banks v. State, 700 So. 2d 363, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1337 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction relief denied; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled no contest to two counts of first-degree murder for the shooting deaths of his wife and his stepdaughter. He filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief alleging ineffective assistance of counsel. The Circuit Court, Gadsden County (Florida), denied the motion. Defendant appealed and also filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove to the wife's trailer, entered without turning on the lights, shot the wife execution-style while she lay sleeping, and then proceeded to the stepdaughter's bedroom. In support of his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion, defendant alleged that trial counsel failed to retain a mental-health expert to evaluate possible statutory and nonstatutory mitigating evidence concerning beatings he received from his father from the age of three to the age of around 11 and his abuse of alcohol. He failed to demonstrate deficient conduct in failing to present the child abuse evidence. And, although defendant had ingested a considerable quantity of alcohol before the murders, his actions both before and during the murders and the length of time over which the alcohol was consumed supported the trial court's finding that there was insufficient evidence to establish that defendant was under the influence of alcohol when he killed the victims. Further, the habeas petition was denied as the death penalty statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed. Defendant's petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Critchfield


No. SC02-386


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


842 So. 2d 782; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 383; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 225



March 13, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 20, 2003. Released for Publication June 11, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1059 (Fla., June 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Fifth District - Case No. 5D01-1617.
Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Critchfield, 805 So. 2d 1034, 2002 Fla. App. LEXIS 17 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the decision below.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Florida Department of Highway Safety and Motor Vehicles (DHSMV) appealed from the affirmance of the trial court's entry of summary judgment for appellee driver by the Florida District Court of Appeal, which held that 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223 violated the single subject rule in Fla. Const. art. III, § 6.


OVERVIEW: The driver claimed that 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223, § 2 lacked a logical or natural connection to the subject matter of ch. 223. The supreme court agreed that the law violated the single subject rule of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223, § 2, which involved assigning bad check debt to a private debt collector, had no natural or logical connection to the law's subject matter: driver's licenses, operation of motor vehicles, and vehicle registrations. The subject matter of ch. 233 was defined in part by the substantial revisions to a state house bill. When the house bill was returned by the state senate, the bill's subject was changed to driver's licenses, vehicle registrations and operation of motor vehicles. The bill was passed at the end of the legislative session. In enacting ch. 223, the legislature unconstitutionally combined two subjects into one law. The DHSMV's argument that § 2 correlated to 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223, §§ 1, 3 did not consider § 2's complete lack of correlation to 1998 Fla. Laws ch. 223, §§ 6-14. There was no connection between assigning bad check debt to a private collector and driver's licenses, vehicle registrations, and motor vehicle operation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Coney


Nos. SC01-1185 & SC02-900


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


845 So. 2d 120; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 274; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 201



March 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Coney, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 785 (Fla., May 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: A Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Fredricka G. Smith, Judge - Case No. F90-13913 and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Coney v. State, 653 So. 2d 1009, 1995 Fla. LEXIS 9 (Fla., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant had been convicted of the murder of his prison homosexual lover and sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), after an evidentiary hearing, vacated the death sentence and granted a new penalty phase proceeding before a jury pursuant to appellant's Fed. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion. The State appealed. Appellant cross-appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant poured solvents on the victim and set him on fire. The victim's dying declaration, admissible under an exception to the hearsay rule, named appellant as his murderer. Appellant said the victim set himself on fire, but testimony from appellant's cellmate and persons from whom appellant obtained solvents supported the victim's declaration. The supreme court, in affirming the appeals court's determination that appellant's counsel was ineffective at the sentencing, but not the guilt, phase, noted that the appeals court had competent and substantial evidence from which it could conclude appellant was prejudiced by his attorney's plain deficiencies in failing to (1) obtain competent medical evaluations and court and prison background information for those evaluations--related to mitigators of mental deficiencies and poor impulse control (brain dysfunction and psychiatric illness) as opposed to ability to stand trial; (2) thoroughly investigate appellant's background, (3) seek additional time and resources. The appellate courts could not conclude that additional evidence would not have affected the seven to five jury vote for the death penalty. Arson was an aggravator.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the order and denied the habeas corpus petition.

Walton v. State


No. SC78070, No. SC76695


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2003 Fla. LEXIS 259; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 183



February 27, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.

NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION, AND IF FILED, DETERMINED.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Substituted opinion at, Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Walton v. State, 847 So. 2d 438, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 902 (Fla., May 29, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Brandt C. Downey III, Judge - Case No. CR 83-00630 CFANO and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Walton v. Dugger, 634 So. 2d 1059, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 957 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) of three counts of murder in the first degree. The trial court sentenced him to death. After his appeal was denied, he filed a motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The motion was denied. He appealed and filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his accomplices committed murder during a robbery for cash and drugs. Appellant contended that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel as to certain issues. On appeal, the court found that because no objection was interposed during the resentencing proceedings, appellant was foreclosed from claiming relief for more comprehensive jury instructions. Further, while it was error for the trial court to allow a mental health professional with an obvious conflict of interest to testify during the postconviction proceedings, any error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the trial court did not actually rely upon the expert's testimony in reaching its decision. Additionally, there was no evidence to support appellant's contention that the State created or originated the sentencing order. Moreover, the trial court had substantial evidence to support the conclusions contained in its sentencing order. Finally, the death sentence was warranted by appellant's relative culpability and leadership of the operation which caused the deaths of the three victims. Accordingly, counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise these meritless claims.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed, and the petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Schrader v. Fla. Keys Aqueduct Auth.


No. SC02-2166


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


840 So. 2d 1050; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 261; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 178



February 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 20, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Monroe County - Bond Validations. Richard G. Payne - Judge - Case No. CAK-02-826.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee Florida Keys Aqueduct Authority (FKAA) filed a complaint under Fla. Stat. ch. 75 in the Circuit Court in and for Monroe County, Florida, seeking validation of its sewer revenue bonds and a judgment that its service area was wholly within the Florida Keys area of critical state concern and that 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 395, § 4 was a general law applicable in that area. The circuit court granted this relief; appellant citizen sought review.


OVERVIEW: Under the authority of 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 395, § 4, the FKAA and a city enacted connection ordinances which included package plants within their scope and required mandatory connections within 30 days of receipt of notification that a publicly-owned or investor-owned sewage system was available. The citizen argued in the circuit court that as § 4 pertained only to local governments within the Florida Keys area of critical state concern, it was a special law unconstitutionally passed as a general law in violation of Fla. Const. art. III, § 10, and that the connection ordinances were unenforceable because their provisions regarding package plants were based solely on the authority granted by 1999 Fla. Laws ch. 395, § 4. The circuit court held that § 4 was properly enacted as a general law and that the connection ordinances were valid and binding. The supreme court agreed. Though § 4 affected a limited geographic area of the state, its primary purpose was one of statewide importance and impact, and that purpose was rationally related to the designation of the Florida Keys as an area of critical state concern; therefore, it was a valid general law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Lugo v. State


No. SC93994


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


845 So. 2d 74; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 254; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 159



February 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 2, 2003.

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, As moot Lugo v. Buss, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 75595 (S.D. Fla., July 13, 2011)
Remanded by Lugo v. Crews, 132 So. 3d 221, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2456 (Fla., Oct. 31, 2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lugo v. Jones, 171 So. 3d 118, 2015 Fla. LEXIS 1180 (Fla., May 28, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Alex Ferrer, Judge - Case No. 95-17381 "C".
Doorbal v. Ferrer, 675 So. 2d 134, 1996 Fla. App. LEXIS 6201 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist., May 7, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), after a jury trial, convicted defendant of all 39 charged crimes including 2 first-degree murders, and sentenced him to death. Most criminal charges involved his participation with other co-defendants in the abduction, extortion, and attempted murder of one victim, or to the abduction, attempted extortion, and murders of two other victims. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Supreme Court had Fla. Const. art. V, § (b)(1) jurisdiction. Defendant's jury was separate from the two co-defendants' jury. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not severing Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organization (RICO) charges (and found sufficient evidence to support RICO's enumerated elements). RICO charges helped to provide the required significant, meaningful relationship, or link, temporal and otherwise, between the events, which extended over six months, so that all defendants and counts could be tried together. Defendants were in a continuing business activity of abduction and extortion. The imposition of the death penalty was supported by the finding that five aggravators of (1) prior violent felony, (2) during the commission of a kidnapping, (3) avoiding or preventing a lawful arrest, (4) pecuniary gain, and (5) cold, calculated, and premeditated, to the two killed, mutilated, burned, and dumped victims, and one aggravator of heinous, atrocious, or cruel to one of those victims, outweighed no statutory and five nonstatutory mitigators, to which little weight was given. Other than a Golden Rule argument the prosecutor's remarks were fair.


OUTCOME: The Supreme Court determined (1) that competent, substantial evidence supported all of defendant's convictions, and (2) that defendant's sentences of death were proportional, and affirmed the convictions and sentences.

Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Kormondy v. State, 983 So. 2d 418, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1896 (Fla., 2007)

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Joseph Q. Tarbuck, Judge - Case No. 93-3302.
Kormondy v. State, 703 So. 2d 454, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 2188 (Fla., 1997)
Hazen v. State, 700 So. 2d 1207, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1352 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Death sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida) which sentenced him to death for a murder committed during a burglary after the jury voted eight to four in recommending the death sentence. Defendant raised several issues including whether the death penalty was constitutional and whether his sentence was proportional given that the codefendants were given life sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two others forcibly entered and burglarized the home of the victim and his wife. The wife was repeatedly raped and the victim was shot in the back of the head by defendant. At resentencing, several witnesses testified on behalf of the State, including the victim's friends, family, neighbors, and members of law enforcement. The defense did not put on any witnesses, relying instead on cross-examination to attack the credibility of each witness. The appellate court held defendant was more culpable than his codefendants, as he confessed to shooting the victim. Thus, his sentence of death was not disproportional. The appellate court had previously determined that while there was insufficient evidence to establish premeditation, there was sufficient evidence to support felony murder. The trial judge considered mitigating circumstances. Given the circumstances inherent in resentencing, the trial court's decision to allow some factual development in the case was not error. The victim impact testimony was proper. Neither Apprendi nor Ring required a finding that the Florida capital sentencing scheme was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the death sentence.

 

656 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Coastal Fla. Police Benevolent Ass'n v. Williams


No. SC00-1860, No. SC00-2072


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


838 So. 2d 543; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 105; 171 L.R.R.M. 3099; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 91



January 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases Consolidated: Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case No. 5D00-618.
Williams v. Coastal State Police Benevolent Ass'n, 765 So. 2d 908, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 10929 (Fla.5th DCA. 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, petitioner sheriff sought a writ of prohibition in the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) to prohibit deputy sheriffs from exercising collective bargaining rights under the representation of respondent labor organization. The District Court denied prohibition, and the sheriff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The labor organization sought, and received, authority from the Public Employees Relations Commission, to enforce the collective bargaining rights of deputy sheriffs in the sheriff's department. The supreme court held Fla. Const. art. I, § 6 provided the right of employees to collective bargaining. The right was fundamental, and the strict scrutiny test was applied to any action tending to undermine it. Both public and private employees had the same broad collective bargaining rights. The plain meaning of the term "employees" in this provision was intended to be applied in its broadest sense to include all employees, public and private, as recipients of the right to bargain. When the Florida Constitution was adopted, the legislature considered whether public employees, as an entire class, had the right to collectively bargain, and the right was extended to all public employees. It was not claimed that the state had a compelling interest in depriving deputy sheriffs of the right to collectively bargain. To the extent any statutory provision prohibited deputy sheriffs from engaging in collective bargaining, it was contrary to the Florida Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal was approved.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Alex Ferrer, Judge - Case No. 95-17381 (B).
Doorbal v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1968 (Fla., Oct. 10, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) for first-degree murder and his sentences of death related to the abduction, extortion, and attempted murder of one person, and the abduction, attempted extortion, and murders of a couple. Defendant asserted, inter alia, that warrants employed by police to search his apartment, home, and vehicle were not supported by probable cause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions involved numerous persons. One victim was kidnapped in order to extort money. The victim was tortured and his family was threatened. Defendant and his accomplices eventually attempted to kill the victim by setting him and a vehicle ablaze. However, the victim escaped the burning vehicle, so defendant and his accomplices ran the victim over. However, the victim survived and testified against defendant. The other circumstances involved defendant and his accomplices murdering a wealthy businessman and his girlfriend. The State presented more than 90 witnesses. Defendant presented no evidence. The appellate court held the police affidavit had sufficiently detailed information to justify the issuance of a search warrant. The challenged witness testimony was either relevant or harmless. The prosecutor's remarks did not affect the jury's verdict. The aggravating circumstances were not offset by the mitigating circumstances. Defendant's death sentences did not lack proportionality.


OUTCOME: The appellate court, having reviewed all of defendant's convictions, determined they were supported by competent, substantial evidence. Defendant's death sentences were proportional. Accordingly, defendant's convictions and his two sentences of death were affirmed.

Damren v. State


No. SC01-1469, No. SC01-2808


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


838 So. 2d 512; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 46; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 81



January 23, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Thomas v. McDonough, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 68770 (M.D. Fla., Sept. 25, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases:

An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Clay County, Robert M. Foster, Judge - Case No. 94-537-CF and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Damren v. State, 696 So. 2d 709, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 605 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from the denial by the Circuit Court in and for Clay County (Florida) of his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, having been convicted of murder, armed burglary, and aggravated assault and sentenced to death. His motion to vacate the judgment and sentence pursuant to Rule 3.851 was rejected.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that he received ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The appellate court disagreed. The failure to present evidence of a potential brain damage in mitigation and the failure to present evidence of petitioner's cocaine addiction were strategic decisions. Petitioner failed to show prejudice by the failure to request an individual voir dire. The failure to present a particular character witness would have been more damaging than helpful. The trial court properly inspected the State's records for Brady materials. The admission of out-of-court statements of the accomplice, who was thereafter murdered, through other witnesses was proper. Further, the statements were admissible under the excited utterances exception. The heinous, atrocious, or cruel nature of the crime had been decided on appeal and could not be relitigated in a habeas petition. The heinous, atrocious, or cruel jury instruction was not unconstitutionally vague, and appellate counsel was not ineffective for failure to object to it. Any issue of the failure to object when the jury was informed that its role was merely advisory was not preserved for appeal, and did not constitute fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion for postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for habeas corpus was denied.

Caribbean Conservation Corp. v. Fla. Fish & Wildlife Conservation Comm'n


No. SC01-1885


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


838 So. 2d 492; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 41; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 46



January 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity First District - Case Nos. 1D00-1389 & 1D00-1804 (Leon County).
 Fla. Fish & Wildlife Conservation Comm'n v. Caribbean Conservation Corp., 789 So. 2d 1053, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 8431 (Fla. 1st DCA 2001).



DISPOSITION: Court of Appeals decision approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, not-for-profit groups and individuals, alleged Fla. Stat. chs. 20.331(6)(c); 370.025(4); and 370.12(1)(c)(3), (1)(h), (2)(g)-(i), 2(k)-(o), 2(p)(1), and 2(q) (1999) unconstitutionally usurped the authority of the Florida Fish and Wildlife Conservation Commission (FWCC) to regulate marine life. They appealed the decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), in favor of respondent agencies.


OVERVIEW: The not-for-profit groups contended the constitutional powers of the FWCC encompassed all marine life without exception, and thus the legislature could not lawfully restrict the FWCC's management or regulatory actions regarding any subclass of marine life. They asserted the legislature could not require the FWCC to comply with the requirements of the Administrative Procedure Act (APA), Fla. Stat. ch. 120, when adopting rules or regulations in respect to those species of marine life that were defined as endangered, threatened, or species of special concern. The supreme court agreed with the lower appellate court that the trial court had applied Davis too broadly. When Fla. Const. art. IV, § 9 and art. XII, § 23(b) were read together, the provisions gave to the FWCC regulatory and executive powers with respect to marine life, including the regulatory and executive powers of the Marine Commission in effect on March 1, 1998. In addition, regulatory and executive powers over some marine life remained with the department of environmental protection regarding endangered and threatened species of marine life.


OUTCOME: The statutes were constitutional with the exception of that portion of the statute which referred to marine species that were "of special concern."

State v. Abreu


No. SC01-2596


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


837 So. 2d 400; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 2; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 16



January 9, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] As Corrected January 23, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Fourth District - Case No. 4D99-2765.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's first trial for burglary of a dwelling ended in a mistrial. At defendant's second trial, the trial court convicted defendant of burglary of a dwelling. Defendant appealed. The Florida District Court of Appeal for the Fourth District reversed defendant's conviction, and remanded the case for a new trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On retrial, the trial court granted the State's request pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(22) (1999), to present a witness's testimony from the first trial in lieu of his live testimony. The prosecutor told the trial judge that the witness had become uncooperative and it was unlikely that the witness would return to Florida for the retrial. The State did not attempt to have the witness declared unavailable for purposes of the retrial, and the record did not contain any supporting documentation that the State attempted to secure the witness's attendance for the retrial. There was no express finding by the trial court that the witness was unavailable. Defendant objected on the ground that his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation was violated. The supreme court found that defendant's right to confrontation was violated and that he was entitled to a new trial. Furthermore, the supreme court held that ch. 90.803(22) violated the Confrontation Clause of the Sixth Amendment in criminal proceedings to the extent that it allowed the prosecutor to use at trial a witness's testimony from a previous judicial proceeding without a showing by the prosecutor that the witness was unavailable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

Porter v. Crosby


No. SC01-2707


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


840 So. 2d 981; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 17; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 33



January 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Porter v. Crosby, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 776 (Fla., Mar. 13, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part Porter v. Crosby, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44025 (M.D. Fla., June 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus
Porter v. Moore, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1337 (Fla., June 20, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed with the Florida Supreme Court for a writ of habeas corpus. He had pled guilty to first-degree shooting murders of two people. He had received a death sentence for one murder and a life sentence for the other. Petitioner filed a motion for postconviction relief, which was denied. The supreme court had affirmed that denial.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise improper prosecutorial antics and arguments which constituted fundamental error. In addition to events occurring prior to his pleading guilty, petitioner alleged an off-the-record discussion, a prosecutorial comment concerning an attorney lying on the floor, and a commotion occurring during the penalty phase closing. Petitioner's trial counsel, however, did not object to any of those items. Thus, the items were not preserved and appellate counsel could not be ineffective for not raising those contentions on appeal unless those contentions constituted fundamental error. There was no basis to reasonably conclude the jury's unanimously recommended death sentence was tainted. None of petitioner's contentions, singularly or collectively, constituted fundamental error. Nor was he prejudiced during the sentencing order, as the trial court only considered in aggravation the statutory aggravating circumstances. Because it did not consider nonstatutory aggravating circumstances, petitioner's appellate counsel was not ineffective for not arguing that claim on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Spencer v. State


Nos. SC00-1051; SC00-2588


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


842 So. 2d 52; 2003 Fla. LEXIS 18; 28 Fla. L. Weekly S 35



January 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Spencer v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 503 (Fla., Mar. 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Belvin Perry, Judge - Case No. CR92-473 and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Spencer v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 631 (Fla., Apr. 11, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed denial of postconviction relief and writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and other crimes involving two attacks on his wife and stepson. The trial court imposed a death sentence, which was affirmed on direct appeal. The Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Florida, denied his motion for postconviction relief. He appealed this denial, and filed a habeas corpus petition claiming the Florida death penalty statute was unconstitutional pursuant to Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: The postconviction petition alleged prosecutorial misconduct and ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The supreme court held that all petitioner's postconviction claims were either procedurally barred, as they were not raised on direct appeal, or were without merit. The lower court's finding, that petitioner received competent, effective assistance of trial counsel, and, to the extent that counsel's performance was less than perfect, petitioner was not prejudiced, was supported by the record. Counsel's decision not to call experts as guilt phase witnesses on the issue of petitioner's alleged dissociative state during the murder (which was supported only by his self-report) was a matter of trial strategy; these experts did testify on this issue during the penalty phase. There were no Giglio violations, as the prosecutor did not intentionally misrepresent the evidence. As to the habeas petition, (1) Apprendi had previously been held not to apply to the Florida death penalty statute; and (2) the claim, that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise instances of alleged prosecutorial misconduct (which had not been objected to) on direct appeal, was meritless.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed and relief was denied under the habeas petition.

Fotopoulos v. State

Writ of habeas corpus granted, in part, Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part Fotopoulos v. Crosby, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 96019 (M.D. Fla., Jan. 29, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Kim Hammond, Judge - Case Nos. 89-7632CFAES, 90-1995CFAES, and 90-6668CFAES and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Fotopoulos v. State, 608 So. 2d 784, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2142 (Fla., 1992)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner's first-degree murder and related convictions, and death sentence, were affirmed, and he moved the Volusia County Circuit Court (Florida) for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and petitioned the Florida Supreme Court for a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court denied his postconviction relief motion, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner and another murdered two victims and tried to murder his wife. The supreme court held counsel's failure to obtain a transcript of pre-trial testimony used to impeach petitioner was not prejudicial as petitioner insisted on testifying. Deciding not to use information from a co-defendant's sentencing was trial strategy. The habeas claims recharacterizing postconviction relief claims as ineffective appellate assistance were procedurally barred. Appellate counsel's failure to raise the admission of relevant evidence of petitioner's abuse of his co-defendant was not ineffective assistance, and any error was harmless.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's convictions were affirmed.

 

667 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Reynolds v. State


No. SC01-1114


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


842 So. 2d 46; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2666; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 1050



December 19, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 26, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Reynolds v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 501 (Fla., Mar. 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity First District - Case No. 1D99-1522 (Leon County).
Reynolds v. State, 784 So. 2d 509, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 4789 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of felony animal cruelty, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 828.12(2) (1997). On appeal, defendant asserted that § 828.12(2) should be construed to require a specific intent, or, if not, should be found facially unconstitutional because it did not include a specific intent element. The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) rejected defendant's assertions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The highest appellate court found that there was a conflict between the lower courts of appeal regarding the issue of whether the cruelty to animals statute required the specific intent to cause a cruel death or excessive suffering. In rejecting defendant's challenge, the highest court found that the question of whether the crime of cruelty to animals required proof of a specific as opposed to a general criminal intent was a matter for the legislature to determine in defining the crime. In the instant case, the legislature required an intentional act that resulted in an animal's cruel death or excessive or repeated infliction of unnecessary pain or suffering. It did not require an intent to cause a cruel death or excessive suffering. The lack of a specific intent to inflict pain or otherwise cause a cruel death did not render the statute unconstitutional. The legislature had, by clear language, declared that one was guilty of the crime regardless of whether they acted with the specific intent to be cruel. It was a general intent crime, as the legislature intended. It was within the authority of the legislature to dispense with specific criminal intent when defining the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

668 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. State


No. SC01-1238


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


837 So. 2d 366; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2669; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 1045



December 19, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 1D99-2562 (Columbia County).
 Reed v. State, 783 So. 2d 1192, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 5955 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2001).



DISPOSITION: Quashed. Certified question answered, and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified its decision for review on the question of whether the trial court's use of a standard jury instruction for aggravated child abuse was fundamental or harmless error. Defendant was convicted of aggravated child abuse and raised an issue for the first time on appeal concerning the definition of malice in the Florida Standard Jury Instructions (Criminal).


OVERVIEW: The question certified was whether giving the standard jury instruction for aggravated child abuse when the instruction inaccurately defined the disputed element of malice was fundamental error. The standard jury instruction contained an erroneous definition of malice. The appellate court held that the trial court erred when it gave the jury the definition of "maliciously" included in the standard jury instruction. The instruction permitted the jury to find defendant guilty based upon a finding of only legal, or technical, malice, rather than actual malice, or malice in fact. The error permitted the jury to find defendant guilty without finding that she harbored ill will, hatred, spite, or an evil intent when she punished her son, thereby reducing the State's burden of proof on an essential element of the offense charged. The failure to use the correct definition was fundamental error as the essential element of malice was disputed at trial, and was material to what the jury had to consider to convict defendant.


OUTCOME: The conviction was quashed and remanded for further proceedings in accord with the decision. The decision was to be retroactively applied to cases pending on direct review or not yet final. The decision was expressly limited in its retroactive application to nonfinal cases.

State v. Lewis


No. SC96890, No. SC02-468


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


838 So. 2d 1102; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2594; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 1032



December 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 14, 2003. Released for Publication February 14, 2003.
Rehearing denied by State v. Lewis, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 818 (Fla., Feb. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus. Notice of Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Susan Lebow, Judge - Case No. 87-9095 CF10A.
Lewis v. State, 572 So. 2d 908, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 1674 (Fla., 1990)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the order denying relief relative to Lewis's conviction; affirmed the order vacating the death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding before a jury; and denied Lewis's petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which granted in part petitioner's motion for postconviction relief, in which the trial court vacated petitioner's death sentence and ordered a new sentencing proceeding. Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus and cross-appealed, asserting that the trial court erroneously denied his motion to vacate his conviction for first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner killed a man and was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. In a postconviction proceeding, the trial court denied a motion to vacate the conviction but vacated the death sentence and ordered a resentencing. The court affirmed and denied a request for habeas corpus relief. The court held that petitioner's counsel provided ineffective assistance in spending a mere 18 hours in preparing for the penalty phase. Thus, petitioner's waiver of the introduction of mitigating evidence at sentencing was invalid. Petitioner was properly denied a new trial because he was not denied effective assistance during the guilt phase. There was no violation in failing to disclose pending charges against a State witness because there was no showing of exculpatory value or prejudice. There was no error in denying petitioner's request for the prosecutor's notes because the request was general and the prosecutor's decision on disclosure was final. As to the habeas petition, although it was error to elicit evidence of petitioner's mother's bribery of a witness, the trial court's instructions rendered the error harmless.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus. The court affirmed the trial court's order, which denied the motion to vacate petitioner's conviction but vacated the death sentence and ordered a resentencing.

 

670 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bunkley v. State


No. SC01-297


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


833 So. 2d 739; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2446; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 967



November 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Clyde Timothy Bunkley v. Fla., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 4273 (U.S., May 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 2D99-4511 (Sarasota County).
Bunkley v. State, 768 So. 2d 510, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 11167 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Approved. Certified question answered in negative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District (Florida). The district court certified the following question: Should the decision in L.B., that a folding pocketknife with a blade of four inches or less fell within the statutory exception to the definition of a "weapon" found in Fla. Stat. ch. 790.001(13) (1995), be applied retroactively?


OVERVIEW: Defendant burglarized an unoccupied restaurant. He was charged with, and convicted of, armed burglary, possession of burglary tools, and resisting arrest without violence. In light of his 15 prior convictions, he was sentenced to life imprisonment on the armed burglary count. The supreme court held jurisprudential upheaval was a major constitutional change of law. The L.B. case clearly was not a decision of that order. It was a routine statutory construction case wherein the court construed the phrase "common pocketknife," and thus, was an "evolutionary refinement" in the law, i.e., it was a conventional change that afforded new or different guidelines for the courts in applying the law. The supreme court construed and refined the phrase "common pocketknife" in the face of evolving circumstances in the field. The decision thus afforded new or different guidelines for Florida courts to use in applying the statute and was an evolutionary refinement in the law. Thus, defendant was not entitled to retroactive application of the decision in regard to the definition of "weapon" under Fla. Stat. ch. 790.001(13) (1995).


OUTCOME: The supreme court answered the certified question in the negative and held that L.B. could not be given retroactive application and applied to final cases.

Marquard v. State


No. SC00-253, No. SC00-1540


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


850 So. 2d 417; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2448; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 973



November 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised May 1, 2003.
Released for Publication May 1, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Marquard v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 670 (Fla., May 1, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Marquard v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1356 (Fla., July 15, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Marquard v. Sec'y for the Dep't of Corr., 429 F.3d 1278, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 24333 (11th Cir. Fla., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Marquard v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1837 (Fla., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Johns County, Robert K. Mathis, Judge - Case No. CF 91-2418 and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Marquard v. State, 641 So. 2d 54, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 863 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm the lower court's denial of Marquard's 3.850 motion for postconviction relief and deny the petition for habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate under sentence of death for first-degree murder and armed robbery, appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court, St. Johns County (Florida), denying his motion for postconviction relief and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant asserted, inter alia, new evidence requiring his sentence be vacated and ineffective counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with his friend, lured defendant's girlfriend into the woods and killed her. Defendant asserted his death sentence should be vacated, based on the fact that his friend's sentence was reduced to life and his friend's admission to cutting the victim's neck while she was still alive. The postconviction court found defendant was not entitled to relief, because he was more culpable, as he was the dominant person. The appellate court found the trial court's decision was proper. His friend's sentence did not mandate a resentencing. The trial court found the friend's most recent testimony did not constitute newly discovered evidence, but was simply the latest version of the events surrounding the homicide that was in direct conflict with his prior testimony and other evidence. The appellate court agreed. Defense counsel's strategic decisions were not so unreasonable as to constitute ineffectiveness. Defendant did not make any specific objections to the mistaken jury instruction, but stated merely he renewed every objection previously made. Such a generic objection did not properly preserve the issue, as the trial court could have corrected its error at the time.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the denial of defendant's postconviction motion and denied the petition for habeas corpus.

Chavez v. State


No. SC94586


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


832 So. 2d 730; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2452; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 991



November 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Chavez v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2449 (Fla., Nov. 21, 2002)

Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Chavez v. State, 12 So. 3d 199, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 977 (Fla., 2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Chavez v. Sec'y Fla. Dep't of Corr., 647 F.3d 1057, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 15287 (11th Cir. Fla., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at Chavez v. State, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 2244 (Fla., Oct. 11, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Chavez v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 436 (Fla., Jan. 31, 2014)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by, Stay denied by, As moot Chavez v. Sec'y, Fla. Dep't of Corr., 2014 U.S. App. LEXIS 2482 (11th Cir. Fla., Feb. 10, 2014)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Chavez v. Palmer, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16425 (M.D. Fla., Feb. 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Marc Schumacher, Judge - Case No. F95-037867.
Chavez v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1150 (Fla., May 30, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) of first-degree murder, kidnapping, and sexual battery, and he was sentenced to death. He appealed. The supreme court's previous opinion was withdrawn, and the following revised opinion was substituted in its place.


OVERVIEW: Defendant abducted, sexually assaulted, and murdered a child. The supreme court held probable cause for his arrest was shown by the discovery in his trailer of the missing child's books. The custodial period when defendant's confession was obtained lasted over 54 hours, but the interrogation was not coercive, as he was given refreshment, breaks, and a 6-hour rest period. The confession was not coerced by questionable information requests stating the victim's need for a decent burial, repeated Miranda warnings were sufficient, and defendant understood his rights. Not obtaining a judicial probable cause determination for continued detention within 24 hours, as required by Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.130, or 48 hours, as required by U.S. Const. amend. IV, did not require suppression of his confession, as the violation did not compel the confession, because defendant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily waived his Miranda rights. He was not detained to gather probable cause evidence; he waived his right to a first appearance in 48 hours; and the official misconduct was not purposeful. Excluding unappointed defense counsel from the interrogation did not require suppression.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Washington v. State


Nos. SC00-1435 & SC01-872


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


835 So. 2d 1083; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2405; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 960



November 14, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Washington v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1701 (Fla., Jan. 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Susan F. Schaeffer, Judge - Case No. CFC9006491CFANO-M.
Washington v. State, 653 So. 2d 362, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1874 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order by the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denying his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 after his conviction of first-degree murder, burglary with a battery, and sexual battery. Petitioner also sought a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that his trial counsel was ineffective in failing to present mitigating evidence of his drug addiction and in failing to disclose his addiction to his expert. The appellate court held that the trial court's rejection of the ineffective assistance of penalty phase counsel claim was proper, as it was a strategic decision. It was not error to summarily deny the ineffective assistance claim as to the guilt phase counsel, since petitioner did not satisfy either Strickland standard. Petitioner's claim that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to request a Frye hearing was procedurally barred, as it had not been raised in the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion. Habeas relief was denied as to the claim that appellate counsel was ineffective for the failure to argue that the trial court erred in failing to hold a Frye hearing. Trial counsel did not raise Frye as an issue below, or request a hearing on the general soundness of the FBI's testing procedures. Appellate counsel could not be deemed deficient for failing to raise an issue that was not raised or preserved at trial. Appellate counsel rendered effective representation under Strickland.


OUTCOME: The denial of post conviction relief was affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Bell v. State


No. SC00-1185


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


841 So. 2d 329; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2381; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 937



November 7, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 21, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Bell v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 516 (Fla., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County, Thomas T. Remington, Judge - Case No. 99-528 CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed convictions but reduced sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Okaloosa County (Florida) of first-degree murder with a deadly weapon and armed kidnapping with a weapon. The trial court followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 17 years old. His 16 year-old girlfriend rented a room from the adult victim. The girlfriend told defendant that the victim was making sexual advances upon her. One night while a teenage friend was staying with the girlfriend, the girlfriend called defendant and told him that the victim had asked the two girls to sleep with him. Defendant went to the victim's home and with the assistance of his girlfriend and her friend beat the victim with a baseball bat, tied the victim up, and transported the victim to a wooded area where they tied the victim to a tree, set him on fire, and slit his throat with a meat cleaver. The supreme court found that (1) the prosecutor's closing argument was not an improper personal attack on defense counsel but a response to defense counsel's own argument to the jury; (2) the trial court abused its discretion in assigning little weight to the mitigator of defendant's age; (3) the trial court's finding of the avoid arrest aggravator was in error; and (4) the statutory mitigator that defendant was 17 years of age was an extremely significant factor that, together with the other mitigation, rendered the death penalty disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed, but the sentence was reduced to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.

 

675 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Atkinson


No. SC01-1775


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


831 So. 2d 172; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2195; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 888



October 24, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Second District - Case No. 2D00-3243 (Polk County).
 Atkinson v. State, 791 So. 2d 537, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 10632 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist. 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's original sentence was corrected and reduced. The State subsequently petitioned for defendant's commitment under the Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.910 et seq. (2000). Defendant petitioned for a writ of prohibition to prevent the trial court from hearing the State's petition. The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) ordered the trial court to discharge defendant, and then certified a question of great public importance for review.


OVERVIEW: The certified question was whether the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 394.910 et seq. (2000), applied to persons convicted of sexually violent offenses, before the effective date of the Act, who were not in lawful custody on the effective date of the Act, January 1, 1999. The highest appellate court found that the Act provided, in pertinent part, that it applied to all persons currently in custody who had been convicted of a sexually violent offense, as set forth in Fla. Stat. ch. 394.925 (2001). The lower appellate court determined that the custody requirement had to be read to require lawful custody. The highest appellate court agreed. Requiring only actual custody, even if unlawful, could produce unreasonable, harsh, or absurd consequences that would be contrary to public policy. In the instant case, defendant's sentence should have expired before the effective date of the Act. Therefore, the highest appellate court found that it would be fundamentally unfair not to give defendant the benefit of his operative release date. Accordingly, the Ryce Act was found to be limited to persons who were in lawful custody on its effective date.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered in the negative, and the decision below was approved.

King v. Moore


No. SC02-1457


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


831 So. 2d 143; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2199; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 906



October 24, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Moore v. King, 537 U.S. 1041, 154 L. Ed. 2d 512, 123 S. Ct. 600, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 8665 (2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Stay denied by King v. Moore, 537 U.S. 1067, 154 L. Ed. 2d 556, 123 S. Ct. 657, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 9068 (2002)
Stay denied by King v. State, 833 So. 2d 774, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2631 (Fla., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: King v. State, 808 So. 2d 1237, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 25 (Fla., 2002)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Petition for habeas relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a prisoner under sentence of death and an active death warrant, petitioned the Florida Supreme Court for a writ of habeas corpus. He sought relief pursuant to Ring, wherein the United States Supreme Court held unconstitutional the Arizona capital sentencing statute to the extent that it allowed a sentencing judge, sitting without a jury, to find an aggravating circumstance necessary for imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: The United States Supreme Court stayed defendant's execution and placed his case in abeyance while it decided Ring. It then issued its decision in Ring, summarily denied defendant's petition for certiorari, and lifted the stay without mentioning Ring in defendant's order. The United States Supreme Court did not direct the Florida Supreme Court to reconsider defendant's case in light of Ring. Significantly, the United States Supreme Court repeatedly reviewed and upheld Florida's capital sentencing statute over the past quarter of a century and, although defendant contended that there were areas of irreconcilable conflict in that precedent, the United States Supreme Court in Ring did not address that issue. As the United States Supreme Court stated that, if its precedent had direct application in a case, yet appeared to rest on reasons rejected in some other line of decisions, the other courts should follow the case that directly controlled, leaving to the United States Supreme Court the prerogative of overruling its own decisions, defendant's petition had to be denied.


OUTCOME: Defendant's petition for habeas relief was denied. The stay of execution was to terminate at 5 p.m. on the 30th day following the filing of the opinion. No motion for rehearing was to be allowed.

678 of 2516 DOCUMENTS



Westerheide v. State


No. SC00-2124


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


831 So. 2d 93; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2176; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 866



October 17, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Westerheide v. State, 2004 Fla. App. LEXIS 17802 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 19, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case No. 5D99-785. (Volusia County).
Westerheide v. State, 786 So. 2d 1192, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 231 (Fla., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal for Volusia County, Florida, affirmed defendant's commitment under, and upheld the constitutionality of, the Jimmy Ryce Act, Fla. Stat. chs. 394.910 to 394.930 (2001) (the Act), and, in defendant's appeal, certified four questions relating to the Act's constitutionality as being of great public importance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a sexual relationship with a 15-year-old. Two experts testified that defendant was a sexual sadist and had an antisocial personality disorder. The trial court found defendant to be a sexually violent predator and ordered him to be confined in a secure facility for control, care, and treatment until his mental abnormality or personality disorder changed so that it was safe for him to be at large. Defendant's expert testified that supervision through probation was sufficient treatment. The supreme court agreed that the Act was not unconstitutional under the Ex Post Facto, Double Jeopardy, Due Process, and Equal Protection Clauses. The Kansas statute that was upheld by the United States Supreme Court's Hendricks decision was compared and found similar to the Act. The Act was not so punitive as to be considered a criminal rather than civil statute, even though detention and medical treatment under the Act started after incarceration for the underlying crime was complete and even though there was evidence that treatment might not ever be effective. The Constitution did not prevent a State from detaining those who posed a high likelihood of danger to others.


OUTCOME: The court found no merit to the defendant's constitutional challenges, answered the certified questions in the negative, agreed that the Act was constitutional, and approved the decision of the intermediate court.

Nelson v. State


No. SC00-876


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2002 Fla. LEXIS 1947; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 797



October 3, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION, AND IF FILED, DETERMINED.

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn by, Rehearing denied by Nelson v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1171 (Fla., July 10, 2003)
Substituted opinion at Nelson v. State, 850 So. 2d 514, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 1170 (Fla., July 10, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Polk County, J. Michael Hunter, Judge - Case Nos. CF97-06806A-XX & CF97-00813A-AP.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed convictions and sentences.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida), after a jury trial, convicted defendant of first-degree murder, burglary of a dwelling with a battery, grand theft (motor vehicle), kidnapping, burglary of a conveyance with a battery, and sexual battery, and, after a nine to three jury recommendation, and the trial court's finding of six statutory aggravators, sentenced defendant to the death. Defendant challenged only his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a 78-year-old female victim's home by climbing through the bathroom window, sexually assaulted the victim in her bed, took her car keys from her purse, placed her in her car trunk, drove around for a period of hours, drove to an orange grove (where he apparently intended to leave her), got stuck in sand, and was pulled out with a witness's assistance, sped off, drove to another location, let the victim out of the trunk, dragged her 175 feet, attempted to strangle her with his bare hands, emptied the contents of a fire extinguisher into her mouth, forced a tire iron into her mouth and through the back of her head, and killed her. The Supreme Court, in affirming, found that defendant's statements to police were properly not suppressed, as they were voluntary. Police use of a "proper burial" technique did not make the otherwise voluntary statement coerced and inadmissible. The statutory aggravators discussed and found were: (1) avoiding arrest (defendant could have escaped, so the reason to kill was to eliminate a witness); (2) cold, calculated premeditation (based on the time-consuming manner of killing); and (3) especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel.


OUTCOME: The supreme court, based on the totality of the circumstances in the case, considered in light of the Court's prior decisions in other capital cases involving similar circumstances, found that the death was a proportionate penalty in this case and affirmed the judgment of conviction and death sentence.
