683 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mayes v. Moore


No. SC00-927


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


827 So. 2d 967; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1880; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 770



September 19, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mayes v. Crosby, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 4315 (U.S., June 2, 2003)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners were convicted of a number of offenses and sentenced to prison. They were released and placed on conditional release. They both violated the terms of their release, and their supervision was revoked. Their sentences were audited and they were given overcrowding credits for their previous confinement. Those credits were then forfeited due to the conditional release revocations. They petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners claimed that at the time of their pleas they were not informed that they were eligible for placement in the conditional release program. Under that program, any gain time they received was converted into conditional release supervision upon their release from prison. Petitioners' gain time was forfeited when the conditional release was revoked. Petitioners argued that Fla. Stat. ch. 947.1405 (2001) was a recidivist statute, which required notice and an opportunity to be heard at sentencing. The court found that it was not a recidivist statute. Because the conditional release did not impose an enhanced criminal penalty or sentence, no actual notice of an offender's eligibility for the program was required. In addition, everyone, including petitioners, was considered to have constructive knowledge of the applicable law. The program did not violate separation of powers, as the power to place inmates on supervision flowed from the Florida Constitution. It was not a bill of attainder because it did not punish individuals for acts already committed. The forfeiture of overcrowding credits was proper as the accrual date, and not the posting date, was the relevant date.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

684 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Coalition to Reduce Class Size


No. SC02-1624


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


827 So. 2d 959; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1879; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 749



September 13, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court in and for Leon County, P. Kevin Davey, Judge, Case No. 02-CA-1490 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D02-2939.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, secretary of state and others, sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) which granted an injunction after it found the fiscal impact statement requirement facially unconstitutional because it violated Fl. Const. art. XI, §§ 3, 5. The supreme court certified the issue to be of great public importance requiring immediate resolution.


OVERVIEW: The legislature had proposed a constitutional amendment which would require a fiscal impact statement to be placed on the ballot for all future proposed constitutional amendments by initiative. The issue was whether 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 390 was necessary to ensure ballot integrity. The supreme court held it was not. The requirements for exercising the power to amend the constitution by initiative were set forth in Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. If those requirements were met, then the sponsor of an initiative had the right to place the initiative on the ballot. However, with the passage of 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 390, an initiative's appearance on the ballot would have been substantially altered, due to the addition of the fiscal impact statement. The effect would have been to weaken the power of the initiative process. Hence, the appellate court was unable to conclude that 2002 Fla. Laws ch. 390 was necessary to ensure ballot integrity.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment finding that the statutorily imposed fiscal impact statement was an unconstitutional imposition on the initiative process was affirmed.

 

685 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sheppard & White, P.A. v. City of Jacksonville


Nos. SC00-331, SC00-352, SC00-353


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


827 So. 2d 925; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1876; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 739



September 12, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Three Cases Consolidated: Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 1D99-39. Second District - Case No. 2D99-894. (Charlotte County).
Sheppard & White, P.A. v. City of Jacksonville, 751 So. 2d 731, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 1461 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2000). Charlotte County v. Shirley, 750 So. 2d 706, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 153 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The rate of pay for conflict attorneys appointed in capital cases was at issue. Petitioner attorney was awarded $ 50/hour, which was affirmed by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which certified a question of great public importance. A second attorney was awarded $ 100/hour, which was reversed and lowered to $ 50/hour, by the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which also certified a question. The cases were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The higher appellate court found that Fla. Stat. ch. 925.036(1) (1997) clearly contemplated that reasonable fees would be paid for competent counsel. The chief or senior judge of each circuit had to determine the prevailing hourly rate for similar representation before an hourly rate could properly be established for capital counsel. The first attorney argued that he could not even pay his overhead on the $ 40/hour originally awarded, which was subsequently raised to $ 50/hour. He argued that it was a confiscatory taking of his time, energy, and talents. He asserted that there was no evidence that the chief judge of the district considered the prevailing hourly rate for similar representation rendered in his circuit. The higher appellate court declined to hold that the chief judge did not fulfill his statutory duty to determine the prevailing rate in the total absence of proof that he failed to do so. Inability to cover overhead alone was not sufficient justification to conclude that the right to counsel was negatively impacted. In the instant cases, there was substantial evidence in the record to support the original trial courts' rulings regarding the fees of both attorneys.


OUTCOME: The decision to award the first attorney $ 50/hour was approved. The decision by the lower appellate court to reduce the second attorney's rate of pay from $ 100/hour to $ 50/hour was quashed, and the matter was remanded so that the second attorney would receive compensation at the rate of $ 100/hour, according to the original determination of the trial court. The certified questions, one of which was rephrased, were answered in the negative.

 

686 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Dufresne v. State


No. SC01-246


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


826 So. 2d 272; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1841; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 728



September 5, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 4D99-1375. (Palm Beach County).
 State v. Dufresne, 782 So. 2d 888, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 479 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist. 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with five counts of child abuse involving different children, contrary to Fla. Stat. ch. 827.03(1) (Supp. 1996). The trial court dismissed, finding the statute to be unconstitutional. The District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed, but certified the question of whether the term "mental injury" in Fla. Stat. ch. 827.03(1)(b) (1996) was unconstitutional because it was vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the term "mental injury" was unconstitutionally vague since it was not defined in Fla. Stat. ch. 827.03. The supreme court disagreed. To withstand a vagueness challenge, a statute had to provide persons of common intelligence and understanding adequate notice of the proscribed conduct. However, the legislature's failure to define a statutory term did not in and of itself render a penal provision unconstitutionally vague. While the legislature could direct that statutes be read in pari materia, the absence of such a directive did not bar construing two statutes in that manner. Fla. Stat. ch. 39, which dealt with protective services for abused and neglected children, defined "mental injury" at Fla. Stat. ch. 39.01(44) (Supp. 1998) as an injury to the intellectual or psychological capacity of a child as evidenced by a discernible and substantial impairment in the ability to function within the normal range of performance and behavior. Fla. Stat. ch. 39 was sufficiently related to child abuse to put a citizen on notice that its provisions might be related to the child abuse provisions of Fla. Stat. ch. 827.03.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered in the negative.

 

687 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Trotter v. State


No. SC02-14


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


825 So. 2d 362; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1757; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 685



August 22, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal--Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Fifth District--Case No. 5D01-873 (Orange County).
 Trotter v. State, 801 So. 2d 1041, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 18007 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist. 2001)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the imposition of a drug trafficking multiplier during his Heggs resentencing, which the original trial court had refused to impose. The Fifth District Court of Appeal certified its decision affirming the use of the multiplier, as it was in direct conflict with the Second District Court of Appeal's opinion in Estrada.


OVERVIEW: Resentencing under Heggs was a de novo sentencing proceeding. The state's highest appellate court agreed with the Fifth District's decision that if the trial court lawfully could have imposed a multiplier at the time of the original sentencing, then double jeopardy principles were not violated when the trial court on resentencing after a Heggs remand imposed a drug trafficking multiplier, even though the trial court declined to impose the multiplier at the original sentencing. Defendant was not deprived of any reasonable expectation of finality in his original sentence because he challenged his sentence on appeal on a legal basis. On remand, the trial court determined that the maximum sentence under the 1994 guidelines without the multiplier was insufficient, and used its discretion to apply the multiplier. A sentence of 72 months' incarceration resulted. Because the sentence imposed on remand was less than the original sentence imposed, the presumption of vindictiveness did not arise, and defendant failed to establish a due process violation.


OUTCOME: The Fifth District's decision was approved, and the Second District's decision in Estrada was disapproved to the extent it was inconsistent with the opinion.

 

688 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sarnoff v. Fla. Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles


No. SC01-351


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


825 So. 2d 351; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1752; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 693



August 22, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal--Direct Conflict First District--Case No. 1D00-1335 (Leon County).
 State Dep't of Highway Safety & Motor Vehicles v. Sarnoff, 776 So. 2d 976, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 16955 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2000)



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner automobile owners appealed the decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict First District (Florida) which, after an appeal by respondent department of highway safety & motor vehicles, held the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the automobile owner's claim for a refund because they had failed to seek relief from the comptroller pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 215.26 (1995).


OVERVIEW: The department had argued the trial court had improperly exercised jurisdiction because the automobile owners had failed to comply with the requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 215.26 (1995) which required the filing of an administrative claim before bringing an action in circuit court. The lower appellate court held the direct file exception in Nemeth applied to facial, rather than as-applied, challenges to the constitutionality of a statute. Since the automobile owners challenged only the agency's interpretation of the statute, the direct file exception did not apply. The supreme court held that since the automobile owners were challenging an agency rule, the administrative process had to be adhered to since adequate remedies may have existed within the administrative realm. Chapter 215.26 permitted the comptroller to give a refund of inspection fees made into the state treasury by error. The automobile owners failed to show that recourse to the administrative process would have been futile since they could have instituted a rule challenge. Thus, their argument that the statute could not provide relief was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower appellate court was affirmed.

 

689 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Tormey v. Moore


No. SC97143


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


824 So. 2d 137; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1481; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 661



July 11, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Mandamus.



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Petition for writ of mandamus granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a former prisoner, was convicted of armed robbery and second-degree murder for offenses that occurred on May 18, 1990. She filed for a writ of mandamus, contesting the number of days she received for overcrowding credits. Respondent Florida Department of Corrections moved to dismiss as moot, on the basis that the prisoner was released from prison, shortly before oral argument, having completed her sentence without the credits.


OVERVIEW: As the issue was of great public importance and likely to recur, the supreme court found that mootness did not destroy its jurisdiction. Petitioner argued that the amended provisional credits statute, which had purportedly gone into effect a few months before her crimes were committed, was unconstitutional because it violated Florida's single subject rule, and because its title was misleading, under Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The court agreed. A reading of the title of the Law Enforcement Protection Act, 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 100, required the conclusion that it provided for increased criminal penalties for persons who committed criminal offenses against law enforcement personnel only. The provisional credits general murder exclusion therein was not reasonably connected with the expressed subject, and the statute failed. Removal of the offending provision would not, in any way, hinder the accomplishment of the valid provisions. Since a relevant reenactment had occurred and became effective May 2, 1991, only those persons who were excluded from receiving provisional credits who committed their offenses on or after January 1, 1990, and before May 2, 1991, were entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied. Petitioner was entitled to relief.

691 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


City of Miami v. McGrath


No. SC01-1562


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


824 So. 2d 143; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1479; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 667



July 11, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity.

Third District - Case No. 3D00-2754.
 McGrath v. City of Miami, 789 So. 2d 1168, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 9495 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist. 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third District Court of Appeal, Florida, declared that Fla. Stat. ch. 218.503(5)(a) was invalid. The appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city contended that the court of appeals erred in finding that that Fla. Stat. ch. 218.503(5)(a) (1999), was a special law which authorized imposition of non-ad valorem taxes in violation of the Florida Constitution. The supreme court disagreed. First, the population classification was nothing more than a descriptive technique used to identify three particular municipalities to which the statute applied. Limiting the statute as such was tantamount to restricting it to those particular municipalities that met the population threshold on the effective date. Second, the statute did not operate uniformly among similarly situated municipalities because it did not apply to all municipalities. As a result of the combination of the population threshold and the limiting date, the statute by its express terms forever excluded any other municipalities that increased in size to meet the population threshold after said date. Third, the statute employed an arbitrary classification scheme because it contained a classification incapable of generic application, and fixed so as to preclude additional entities from satisfying the requirements for inclusion at some future point in time.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Spencer v. Fla. Dep't of Corr.


No. SC00-1898


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


823 So. 2d 752; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1466; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 646



July 3, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Mandamus.



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate petitioned the Florida Supreme Court for a writ of mandamus to respondent department of corrections to restore his gain time, claiming, inter alia, that Fla. Stat. chs. 944.279, .28(2)(a) (2001), dealing with frivolous appeals, violated his constitutional rights to express himself and seek redress.


OVERVIEW: After his conviction for murder, the inmate's appeal was dismissed for failure to list all his prior appeals. The federal trial court found the appeal had not been taken in good faith, the appellate court upheld the order, and the department forfeited a portion of the inmate's gain time. The state supreme court held that the inmate's appeal was not taken in good faith. After the department received the order, it conducted disciplinary procedures, gave the inmate prior notice, and a hearing. The inmate was not restrained from speaking or filing a lawsuit. Sections 944.279, .28 in no way prohibited him from exercising his First Amendment rights or gaining access to the courts; they simply provided for discipline when the inmate engaged in misconduct by filing a frivolous lawsuit. The inmate was not penalized for exercising his rights; he was penalized for abusing his rights.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Hall v. State


No. SC01-42


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


823 So. 2d 757; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1467; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 627



July 3, 2002, Decided

First District - Case No. 1D99-1272

(Gadsden County).
 Hall v. State, 773 So. 2d 99, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 15179 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for review of a decision by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) that upheld the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 921.002 (Supp. 1998), claiming that his sentence was cruel and unusual, and the code violated due process, double jeopardy, separation of powers, and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of possession of cocaine and resisting arrest and was sentenced to consecutive five-year sentences. The state supreme court held that statutorily-mandated consecutive sentencing was constitutionally permissible. The minimum mandatory sentencing schemes did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment. The State's right to appeal a downward departure was not a double jeopardy violation. Separation of powers was not violated since the imposition of concurrent and consecutive sentences was one of substantive law. Defendant was on notice of the available punishments because the code was published. He failed to preserve his equal protection claim.


OUTCOME: The decision was approved.

Mack v. State


No. SC00-2355


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


823 So. 2d 746; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1469; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 630



July 3, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict

Fifth District - Case No. 5D00-1274

(Brevard County).
 Mack v. State, 766 So. 2d 1254, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 12610 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Approved in part, quashed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant applied for review of a decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), claiming that one sentence was illegal and the 10-year habitual felony offender sentences imposed after revocation of his probation in two other cases were illegal sentences subject to correction under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to a number of counts of burglary and grand theft. He was determined to be a habitual felony offender on one count and sentenced to a three and one-half year true split sentence. He was sentenced to probation on the other two counts. After he violated his probation a second time, his probation was revoked in all three cases and he was sentenced as a habitual felony offender. The state supreme court held that even though defendant's sentence on the first count did not exceed the statutory maximum, it was an illegal sentence because it exceeded the amount initially imposed. The habitual offender designation in the other two cases was improper because the sentencing court did not impose a habitual offender sentence; rather, it placed defendant on probation. He could not thereafter be sentenced as a habitual offender upon revocation of his probation.


OUTCOME: The decision was approved as to the determination that the sentence on the first count was illegal; the decision was quashed as to the imposition of habitual offender status on the remaining two counts and remanded for further proceedings.

Vining v. State


No. SC99-67


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


827 So. 2d 201; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1470; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 654



July 3, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 19, 2002. Released for Publication September 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County,

Theotis Bronson, Judge - Case No. CR 89-2395.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery. He received a sentence of death and also a sentence of life imprisonment, as a habitual offender. On appeal, his convictions and sentences were affirmed. He filed for postconviction relief, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. A Huff hearing was held, along with an evidentiary hearing, after which the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) denied relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised 14 claims on appeal, which included a claim that the lower court failed to properly consider several items of evidence withheld by the State. In rejecting this argument, the appellate court found that no material evidence was withheld and there was no prejudice. There were no inconsistencies between the items withheld and the trial testimony, and defendant did not show how the items could have been used to impeach the witnesses. Defendant also argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, as counsel failed to properly object to the lower court's conducting an independent investigation prior to sentencing. Although strongly disapproving of the lower court's actions, the appellate court found that the information relied upon at sentencing, to support the aggravating factors, was otherwise proven at trial. In addition, the lower court informed the parties of what it did. Given the overwhelming evidence supporting the aggravating factors, the error, if any, was harmless. Some of defendant's other arguments were procedurally barred, and defendant's absence from certain trial court proceedings was harmless.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed.

Orange County v. Costco Wholesale Corp.


No. SC01-382


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


823 So. 2d 732; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1394; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 608



June 27, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict. Fifth District - Case No. 5D00-1728 (Orange County).
Costco Wholesale Corp. v. Orange County, 780 So. 2d 198, 2001 Fla. App. LEXIS 945 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist. 2001)



DISPOSITION: Quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent retailer challenged an ordinance of petitioner county in the trial court. The trial court upheld the ordinance. The retailer appealed to the Florida Court of Appeals for the Fifth District. The Court of Appeals reversed the trial court and found the ordinance to be unconstitutional. The county petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The retailer sought to transfer package liquor licenses to two new store locations that were within 5000 feet of existing package stores. The trial court affirmed the ordinance, reasoning that the county's regulation was substantially related to a legitimate government goal. The appellate court found that the government failed to carry its burden of demonstrating a reasonable relationship of the ordinance to public health, morals, and welfare. On appeal, the court found that the trial court correctly determined that the subject ordinance was within constitutional parameters, as nothing demonstrated that the 5000 foot restriction was arbitrary and capricious or unrelated to the health, safety, and welfare of the citizens of Orange County. The challenged ordinance was a valid exercise of police power, bearing a substantial relationship to the health, safety, morals, or general welfare of the community.

698 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mills v. State


No. SC01-68


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


822 So. 2d 1284; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1336; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 593



June 20, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict First District - Case No. 1D99-2159 (Leon County).
Mills v. State, 773 So. 2d 650, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 16610 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2000)



DISPOSITION: Approved in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of battery on a law enforcement officer. He was sentenced as a habitual offender. On appeal, the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the sentence. A timely petition for review was filed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his habitual felony offender sentence violated double jeopardy, as he also received an enhanced sentence for committing battery on a law enforcement officer. Although Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07 (Supp. 1998) was characterized as an enhancement statute in a previous case, the highest appellate court found that Fla. Stat. ch. 784.07 (Supp. 1998) actually reclassified enumerated offenses. There was a qualitative difference between a statute that reclassified enumerated offenses committed against law enforcement officers and enhancement statutes such as the habitual offender statute, which cut across some or all criminal statutes. The application of both statutes was not an improper double enhancement, as the determination of punishment for crimes was a legislative matter. The Double Jeopardy Clause did no more than prevent a sentencing court from prescribing greater punishment than the legislature intended. The statutes involved in the instant case were read in pari materia. There was no error in defendant's being sentenced for being a habitual felony offender, as a result of his battery on a law enforcement officer.


OUTCOME: The lower appellate court's decision was approved to the extent that it was consistent with the instant opinion.

 

699 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Porter v. Moore


No. SC01-2707


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2002 Fla. LEXIS 1337; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 606



June 20, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Porter v. Crosby, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2802 (Fla., June 20, 2002)
Opinion withdrawn by Porter v. Crosby, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 16 (Fla., Jan. 9, 2003)
Substituted opinion at Porter v. Crosby, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 17 (Fla., Jan. 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Porter v. State, 564 So. 2d 1060, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 827 (Fla., 1990)



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to murders of two victims, and received a death sentence and a life sentence. The judgments were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant also filed a motion for postconviction relief which was denied, and the denial was affirmed. Defendant then filed an original petition for habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he received ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The court held that although such claims were recognizable in a habeas petition, claims raised in a habeas petition which were raised in prior proceedings and which had been previously decided on the merits in those proceedings were procedurally barred in the habeas petition. It was improper to argue in a habeas petition a variant to a claim previously decided. Three of defendant's claims were procedurally barred because the court previously addressed those claims or a variant to those claims. Trial counsel did not preserve three other claims of error, so appellate counsel could not have been ineffective for raising those claims unless they constituted fundamental error. Defendant failed to demonstrate how an off the record discussion between the trial judge and the prosecutor prejudiced him. A remark made by the prosecutor and certain courtroom commotion did not amount to fundamental error. Because the trial court did not consider nonstatutory aggravating circumstances, defendant failed to show that his appellate counsel was ineffective for not arguing the claim on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

700 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Reaves v. State


No. SC00-840


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


826 So. 2d 932; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1335; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 601



June 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 9, 2002. Released for Publication September 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Robert A. Hawley, Judge - Case No. 86-729-CF.
Reaves v. State, 639 So. 2d 1, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 476 (Fla., Apr. 7, 1994)



DISPOSITION: Remanded to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing on the claims relating to whether counsel was ineffective; affirmed the trial court's denial of Reaves' postconviction motion in all other aspects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's initial conviction for first-degree murder was reversed on appeal. Upon retrial, a jury again convicted him of first-degree murder. He was sentenced to death. His conviction and sentence were affirmed. He filed a motion and then amended his motion for postconviction relief, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, which was summarily denied, after a Huff hearing, by the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County (Florida). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was entitled to an evidentiary hearing regarding whether trial counsel was ineffective in failing to present a voluntary intoxication defense. In agreeing, the appellate court found that the record showed that the evidence could have supported such a defense. Defense counsel, however, never argued voluntary intoxication. Defense counsel never presented any evidence that supported it. Defense counsel also never mentioned voluntary intoxication during closing arguments, and never discussed how the evidence could have supported this theory or how cocaine affected the user. Moreover, numerous witnesses testified that defendant had a history of serious drug abuse. Since voluntary intoxication was an available defense, and the record was inconclusive as to why counsel did not advance the defense, it was error not to afford defendant an evidentiary hearing on the failure to present it. Defendant also argued that counsel was ineffective for failing to introduce various mitigating circumstances. The appellate court found that there was no reasonable probability that the additional factors would have affected the balance of aggravating and mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for an evidentiary hearing on the claims relating to whether counsel was ineffective for failing to raise a voluntary intoxication defense and the related subclaims. The denial of defendant's postconviction motion was affirmed in all other respects.

 

701 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Sweet v. Moore


No. SC01-2867


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


822 So. 2d 1269; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1329; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 585



June 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Sweet v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2451 (Fla., Dec. 20, 2004) Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus


PRIOR HISTORY: Sweet v. State, 624 So. 2d 1138, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1301 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to death for murder. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal. Certiorari was denied. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief, and an amended motion, which were denied. The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed on appeal. Defendant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the rule prohibiting his lawyers from interviewing the jurors, Fla. R. Bar 4-3.5(d)(4), was unconstitutional. In addition, he claimed counsel was ineffective for failing to raise the issue on direct appeal. The supreme court found that because no objection was raised at trial, appellate counsel could only be deemed ineffective if the failure to raise the constitutionality of the rule rose to the level of fundamental error. The court concluded that defendant failed to demonstrate any error, let alone fundamental error, as there was no indication of juror misconduct. The court previously rejected similar constitutional challenges. Defendant's claim had no merit, and counsel could not be ineffective for failing to raise a meritless claim. Defendant also argued that the jury should have been told it was required to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the aggravators outweighed the mitigators before recommending a sentence of death, and that the failure to give this instruction was erroneous in light of Apprendi. The court found that it had repeatedly rejected the argument that Apprendi applied to capital sentencing schemes. Therefore, the argument was without merit.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

702 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Asay v. Moore


No. SC01-2371


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


828 So. 2d 985; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1400; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 577



June 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Petition Denied October 4, 2002. Released for Publication October 4, 2002. Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus
Post-conviction relief denied at Asay v. State, 892 So. 2d 1011, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2452 (Fla., Dec. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Asay v. State, 580 So. 2d 610, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 810 (Fla., May 16, 1991)



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted and sentenced to death, petitioned for writ of habeas corpus after his convictions for two counts of murder were affirmed on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the judgment against him, raising numerous contentions. First, appellate counsel was not deficient for failing to raise an alleged violation of defendant's right to be present during jury selection. Second, defendant was not denied an opportunity to present mitigation witnesses. Because the claim was raised on appeal, it was procedurally barred. Third, any misstatement in voir dire did not amount to fundamental error. Fourth, a claim that the trial court limited evidence regarding the effect of intoxication on the victims was insufficiently pled. Fifth, appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise objection to the trial court's refusal to consider mitigation evidence after the jury recommended sentencing. Further, no prejudice was shown. Appellate counsel was not deficient in failing to raise additional challenges to the prosecutor's comments on direct appeal that were not objected to by trial counsel. A second assertion of improper prosecutorial argument was insufficiently pled. A claim that the court improperly shifted the burden to defendant was also denied. Finally, the capital sentencing statute was not unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

703 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lemon


No. SC00-2549


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


825 So. 2d 927; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1156; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 563



June 6, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 18, 2002. Rehearing Denied August 29, 2002. Released for Publication August 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Fourth District - Case No. 4D00-1861 (Broward County).
Lemon v. State, 769 So. 2d 417, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 11342 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 4th Dist. 2000)



DISPOSITION: Quashed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to aggravated assault with a firearm, shooting into an occupied dwelling, and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. She moved to correct illegal sentence pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a). The trial court denied the motion. Defendant appealed to the Florida Court of Appeals for the Fourth District, which reversed and remanded the case to the trial court. The State applied for review of the decision.


OVERVIEW: A 1995 sentencing guidelines sheet was prepared for defendant's sentencing. The trial court sentenced defendant to an upward departure outside the guidelines to 96 months' imprisonment, with a 3-year minimum mandatory sentence due to the use of a firearm. Defendant argued that the sentence was improper because 1994 sentencing guidelines sheet, which mandated a lower sentencing range, should have been used in her case. On appeal, the court found that defendant was not adversely affected by application of the 1995 guidelines because her sentence of 96 months was an upward departure sentence that could have been imposed under either the 1994 or the 1995 guidelines. The statutory aggravating circumstances cited by the trial court were valid under both the 1994 and the 1995 sentencing guidelines scoresheet. Accordingly, because defendant was not adversely affected by the amendments made in 1995 Fla. Laws ch. 184, she was not entitled to Heggs relief. The appellate court approved the holdings of the Florida Court of Appeals for the Fourth District in Ray and Kwil.


OUTCOME: The judgment was quashed, and the Second District's decisions in Ray and Kwil were approved.

705 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Chavez v. State


No. SC94586


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2002 Fla. LEXIS 1150; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 517



May 30, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION, AND IF FILED, DETERMINED.

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn, Substituted opinion: Chavez v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2452 (Fla. Nov. 21, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Marc Schumacher, Judge - Case No. F95-037867.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) of homicide, kidnapping, and sexual battery after the trial court denied his motions to suppress evidence, for acquittal, and for mistrial. The trial court sentenced defendant to death for the homicide and to consecutive terms of life imprisonment for the convictions of kidnapping and sexual battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant abducted and sexually abused a boy before shooting and killing him when he tried to flee the trailer in which defendant lived. Defendant dismembered and hid the boy's body. Later, defendant's employer, believing defendant had stolen her gun, searched the trailer and found the stolen gun defendant had used to kill the boy as well as a book bag with the boy's name written on books. The employer notified the police. Defendant voluntarily went with the police. Evidence was found in the trailer. After more than 50 hours of interrogation through an interpreter, with breaks for refreshments, sleep, and two trips to the crime scene, defendant gave the police a written statement. On appeal, the court found that (1) probable cause existed for defendant's arrest; (2) the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress his confession; (3) it was not reversible error for the jurors to be photographed; (4) a mattress from the trailer was admissible, even though blood stains on the mattress did not belong to defendant or the victim; (5) the State was able to prove the corpus delicti without the confession; and (6) the aggravating instructors were properly applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

706 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Young v. Moore


No. SC00-1106


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


820 So. 2d 901; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1152; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 514



May 30, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.



DISPOSITION: Writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner moved for a writ of habeas corpus, while serving a prison sentence for a first-degree scheme to defraud in violation of the Florida Communications Fraud Act, specifically Fla. Stat. ch. 817.034(4)(a)1.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner contended that the Florida Department of Corrections (department) was precluded from imposing a gain time calculation based on a gain time statute from a year different than that used for sentencing. The court of appeals disagreed. The statute governing a gain time calculation specifically directed the department to calculate the same as of the date the crime was committed. Moreover, because a scheme to defraud was a true continuing offense, Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275(4)(b)3 was applicable. Petitioner's claim that the department's application of the reduced gain time statute was violative of the ex post facto clause was also without merit. Because the gain time statute was in effect when petitioner consummated his offense, there was no unconstitutional retroactive application. Finally, the department's action did not frustrate the legislature's intent to maintain continuity between the sentencing guidelines and gain time statutes. There was no retroactive cancellation of gain time credits, nor did petitioner have any expectation of higher gain time when he consummated his crime nearly 10 months after the reduced gain time statute had taken effect.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied.

 

707 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Cook v. City of Jacksonville


Nos. SC00-1745 & SC00-1908


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


823 So. 2d 86; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1095; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 495



May 23, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 18, 2002. Released for Publication July 18, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction. First District - Case No. 1D99-4593. (Duval County). Second District - Case Nos. 2D99-836 & 2D99-846. (Pinellas County).
Pinellas County v. Eight Is Enough in Pinellas, 775 So. 2d 317, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 6051 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist. 2000) City of Jacksonville v. Cook, 765 So. 2d 289, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 10700 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist. 2000)



DISPOSITION: Quashed; Cook remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff officeholders appealed from judgments, respectively, of the Florida Courts of Appeals for the First and Second District, upholding charter provisions of defendants, city and county, imposing term limits on their offices.


OVERVIEW: A home rule city and a home rule county in Florida each enacted term limitation provisions relating to certain constitutionally authorized officials of local government. The affected officials challenged the provisions as their limitation deadlines approached (in fact, the high court considered one official's appeal despite the expiration of his term while the matter was pending). The high court held that Fla. Const. art. VI, § 4, explicitly set forth the qualifications and disqualifications for certain positions authorized by the Florida Constitution. That section had been amended to permit imposition of term limits on certain officials, but there was no mention of the particular offices involved in the instant appeals. Therefore, since the constitutional provision set forth the only qualifications and disqualifications permitted in the case of constitutionally authorized offices, the local governments exceeded their powers when they attempted to place term limits on them.


OUTCOME: The court quashed both appellate decisions. In the case in which the trial court decision had not been in the officeholders' favor, so that it could not simply be reinstated, the court remanded the matter to the appellate court for further consistent proceedings.

 

708 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. State


No. SC00-1751


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


819 So. 2d 705; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 1096; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 505



May 23, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 23, 2002. Released for Publication July 23, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Cox v. Florida, 154 L. Ed. 2d 799, 123 S. Ct. 889, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 54 (U.S. 2003).
Writ of certiorari denied Cox v. Florida, 537 U.S. 1120, 123 S. Ct. 889, 154 L. Ed. 2d 799, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 54 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cox v. State, 966 So. 2d 337, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1188 (Fla., 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Cox v. State, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 391 (Fla., Mar. 12, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida) of first-degree murder and a sentence of death. The charges resulted from a chain of events within the correctional institute that culminated in a victim's death and an assault upon another victim. The trial court found four aggravating circumstances. While it found no statutory mitigating factors, it found numerous nonstatutory mitigators.


OVERVIEW: Defendant discovered that someone had broken into his personal footlocker and stolen approximately $ 500. Upon making this discovery, he indicated that when he discovered who had stolen from him, he would stab and kill that person, and that he did not care about the consequences. A discovery violation occurred due to an investigator's nondisclosure. However, the State's discovery violation was inadvertent and the defense was not procedurally prejudiced by the violation. Where during cross-examination by the defense, a witness informed the jury that defendant was serving two life sentences, the information did not vitiate the entire trial. The trial court properly gave the jury a proper curative instruction and proceeded with the trial. The State was entitled to decline an offer to stipulate and present evidence concerning the prior felonies. The prosecutorial misrepresentation of the law was harmless error. The trial court received sufficient evidence to conclude that the instant murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated. In comparison with other decisions upholding the imposition of the death penalty, the sentence given defendant was not disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

709 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


In re Constitutionality of House Joint Resolution 1987


No. SC02-194


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


817 So. 2d 819; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 874; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 443



May 3, 2002, Decided



DISPOSITION: House Joint Resolution 1987 is valid and approved as the 2002 reapportionment for the Florida Legislature.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A house joint resolution apportioned the Florida Legislature. Pursuant to Fla. Const. art. III, § 16(c), the state attorney general (designated as an opponent) filed an original proceeding in the state's highest court, in which it petitioned for a declaratory judgment determining the validity of the apportionment. The proponents at oral argument, supporting the joint resolution, were the state speaker of the house and senate president.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court noted that legislative reapportionment was primarily a matter for legislative consideration and determination. Unless it could be shown that the joint resolution violated a provision of the United States Constitution or the Florida Constitution, the court found that it could not declare the resolution invalid. The maximum deviation from the largest and smallest house districts was 2.79 percent, and the maximum for the senate districts was 0.03 percent. Both were well within the general 10 percent limit. The districts also conformed with the state constitutional contiguity requirements. Claims of racial and language discrimination, as well as claims of political gerrymandering, were fact intensive and required fact development, which the court found were better suited for a trial court. In making its determination in the instant matter, the court found that, to the extent it could do so under the state constitution, it was obligated to consider the Voting Rights Act of 1965, specifically 42 U.S.C.S. § 1973 (1994). It did so, within the time constraints of Fla. Const. art. III. The supreme court found that no constitutional violation had been shown.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the house joint resolution was valid and it was approved as the 2002 apportionment of the state legislature. The holding was without prejudice to the right of any protestor to file an as-applied challenge to the validity of the plan for specified reasons. For such a case, standing was not conferred upon any party involved in the instant case, and issues of standing were to be resolved by the trial court.

 

710 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Lee County Elec. Coop. v. Jacobs


No. SC01-373


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


820 So. 2d 297; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 869; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 379



May 2, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 19, 2002. Released for Publication June 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Public Service Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-profit electric distribution cooperative filed a complaint with appellee Florida Public Service Commission asking the commission to conduct a full investigation and evidentiary hearing on a non-profit electric generation and transmission cooperative's new rate schedule. The generation and transmission cooperative moved to dismiss the complaint. The commission dismissed the complaint. The electric distribution cooperative appealed.


OVERVIEW: The non-profit electric generation and transmission cooperative provided electricity to its owner-members, one of which was the non-profit electric distribution cooperative. The non-profit electric distribution cooperative purchased all of its power requirements from the non-profit electric generation and transmission cooperative pursuant to a wholesale power contract between them, and supplemented and amended from time to time. The non-profit electric generation and transmission cooperative approved a new rate schedule applicable to all of its members. The Rural Utilities Services approved the new schedule. The non-profit electric distribution cooperative alleged that the commission had jurisdiction to hear the complaint pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 366.04(2)(b) (1997). The commission concluded that it did not have jurisdiction to prescribe a wholesale rate structure for a rural electric cooperative. On appeal, the supreme court concluded that the commission did not err in granting the motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. Any contention over the current rate schedule was to be more appropriately raised in an action filed in the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

711 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. State


No. SC95136


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


816 So. 2d 554; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 787; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 335



April 18, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Jerald Bagley, Judge - Case No. 86-12910B.
Garcia v. State, 568 So. 2d 896, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 1116 (Fla., 1990)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions for a double murder and the imposition of the death penalty by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), on remand, after a previous conviction was reversed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to allow defendant to impeach a witness with the witness's prior inconsistent statements. In light of the impeachment value of the videotaped statements, the exclusion of the statements impermissibly limited defendant's right to cross-examine the key witness against him. The error was compounded when, during closing argument, the State told the jury why they should believe the witness. The trial court also erred in refusing to admit the prior sworn testimony of a former codefendant in both the guilt and the penalty phases of the trial under the prior testimony exception to the hearsay rule. The State had a similar motive in cross-examining the former codefendant, and had cross-examined the former codefendant on his reliability and credibility. Additionally, the prior testimony would have been independently admissible during the penalty phase, as defendant could have used the testimony to show his minor participation, or that he was acting under substantial domination, or both. The trial court also erred by admitting hearsay statements as to the victim's state of mind during the guilt phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The convictions were reversed and the sentences were vacated. The case was remanded for a new trial.

Spencer v. State


Nos. SC00-1051; SC00-2588


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


2002 Fla. LEXIS 631; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 323



April 11, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] NOT FINAL UNTIL TIME EXPIRES TO FILE REHEARING MOTION, AND IF FILED, DETERMINED.

THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion: Spencer v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 18 (Fla. Jan. 9, 2003).
Rehearing denied, Opinion withdrawn: Spencer v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 15 (Fla. Jan. 9, 2003).
Rehearing denied by, Opinion withdrawn by Spencer v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2800 (Fla., Apr. 11, 2002)
Rehearing denied by, Opinion withdrawn by Spencer v. State, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 15 (Fla., Jan. 9, 2003)
Substituted opinion at Spencer v. State, 842 So. 2d 52, 2003 Fla. LEXIS 18 (Fla., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Belvin Perry, Judge - Case No. CR92-473.
Spencer v. State, 691 So. 2d 1062, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 1512 (Fla., 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, aggravated assault, aggravated battery, and attempted second-degree murder. He received the death penalty. His sentence was affirmed by the supreme court. He subsequently appealed from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. He also petitioned the supreme court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The trial judge found three aggravating circumstances, no statutory mitigating circumstances, and one nonstatutory mitigating circumstance prior to imposing the death penalty. Defendant raised numerous issues including ineffective counsel. The supreme court concluded that defendant's substantive claims of prosecutorial misconduct could and should have been raised on direct appeal and thus were procedurally barred from consideration in a postconviction motion. It also concluded that defendant received competent, effective assistance of counsel in the presentation of his defense, and to the extent that counsel's performance was less than perfect, defendant was not prejudiced by it. It also determined no Brady violation occurred in defendant's case since the identity was not suppressed by the State, and the officer did not possess any evidence that was favorable to defendant. Any claims relating to pretrial publicity or juror bias were procedurally barred because they were not raised on direct appeal. Defendant's other claims were without merit or were unpreserved. Finally, there was no basis to find his counsel was ineffective for purposes of his habeas petition.


OUTCOME: Defendant was not entitled to relief and his petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied. The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed.

Gorby v. State


Nos. SC95153, SC00-405


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


819 So. 2d 664; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 636; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 315



April 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 18, 2002. Rehearing Denied June 11, 2002. Released for Publication June 11, 2002.
Post-conviction relief denied at Gorby v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 867 (Fla., May 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Dedee Castello, Judge - Case No. 90-1189.

And An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Gorby v. State, 630 So. 2d 544, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1931 (Fla., 1993)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's convictions of first-degree murder, grand theft auto, burglary with a battery, and robbery, and his death sentence, were affirmed, he moved the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida) for postconviction relief. The trial court denied his motion, and he appealed. He also petitioned for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered the victim and stole his car. The supreme court held defendant's postconviction relief motion showed no ineffective trial counsel assistance for (1) failing to investigate or present mitigating evidence; (2) not discovering an inmate State witness's letter seeking special treatment, which was not Brady material as no "deal" was made; (3) not challenging a State expert because she trained under someone who allegedly exaggerated her qualifications; (4) not raising that the medical examiner was a suspect in his wife's recent death; and (5) not raising the State's failure to give a State witness perjury immunity who allegedly testified falsely at trial. Defendant was not unable to present his case due to underfunding of counsel's office, and he had a mental health expert's competent assistance, who did not have to testify at the penalty phase. None of the issues raised in defendant's habeas petition, including the trial court's instructions on aggravating circumstances, showed his appellate counsel was ineffective.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed, and defendant's habeas corpus petition was denied.

 

714 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Barley v. S. Fla. Water Mgmt. Dist.


No. SC00-1998


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


823 So. 2d 73; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 632; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 308



April 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 19, 2002. Released for Publication July 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Fifth District - Case No. 5D98-3178 (Orange County).

Barley v. South Fla. Water Mgmt. Dist., 766 So. 2d 433, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 10937, 25 Fla. L. Weekly D 2092 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, taxpayers, appealed from a decision by the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) declaring a Florida statute valid and construing a provision of the Florida Constitution, after the taxpayers brought a declaratory judgment action in the Circuit Court of the Ninth Judicial Circuit in and for Orange County, which entered judgment on the pleadings for respondent, a water management district.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers claimed that non-polluters were constitutionally prohibited from paying for pollution abatement in the Everglades Protection Area (EPA) or the Everglades Agricultural Area (EAA) because under the Fla. Const. art. II, § 7(b), polluters were to pay for pollution abatement for the pollution they caused. The taxpayers also sought a declaration that Fla. Stat. ch. 373.4592(8)(a) (Supp. 1994) violated Fla. Const. art. II, § 7(b), because Fla. Stat. ch. 373.4592(8)(a) (Supp. 1994) prohibited the water management district from raising additional revenues from EAA polluters who were not paying for 100 percent of the costs of abating the pollution they caused. The appellate court held that there was no express language in Fla. Const. art. II, § 7(b) prohibiting the taxpayers from being required to contribute for pollution abatement in the EPA or EAA. The words "primarily responsible" were given their ordinary meaning, which included a recognition that polluters would not bear the total burden. Other persons or entities also continued to have responsibility. The water management district's levy of taxes was not unconstitutional as applied to the taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court of appeal was approved.

 

715 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


White v. State


No. SC00-1148


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


817 So. 2d 799; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 544; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 291



April 4, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 16, 2002. Released for Publication May 16, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: White v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 9316 (U.S. Dec. 16, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied White v. Florida, 537 U.S. 1091, 123 S. Ct. 699, 154 L. Ed. 2d 638, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 9316 (2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at White v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1224 (Fla., July 12, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Margaret T. Waller, Judge - Case No. CR78-1840.
White v. State, 729 So. 2d 909, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 364 (Fla., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) judgment, after the jury voted for the death sentence, the circuit court found four aggravators and assigned weight to one statutory and nine nonstatutory mitigating factors, found the aggravators greatly outweighed the mitigators, and resentenced defendant to death for a 1978 murder. Defendant appealed. The Florida Supreme Court had jurisdiction under Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found by the jury to have taken the victim, whom he and two other co-participants had beaten up, to a remote spot, stabbed her 14 times, and slit her throat. Defendant then gave the knife to one of the other co-participants who also cut her throat. The supreme court had remanded the case to the circuit court for resentencing after the United States Supreme Court in Hichcock v. Dugger held that Florida jury instructions had to permit a jury to consider nonstatutory mitigators. The supreme court affirmed that the trial court, in the resentencing, did not commit error in (1) limiting direct and cross examination of a co-participant with respect to his 25 other felonies, which included a stabbing death in which he blamed another as a perpetrator, by which defendant attempted to show the co-participant either killed the woman or coerced defendant to kill her, (2) disregarding the 22 year gap between killing and resentencing, (3) not finding evidence and instructing on the extreme duress and substantial domination mitigator, (4) considering hindering of law enforcement by killing her to keep her quiet after her beating, and (5) finding the death proportional.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

716 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Fuchs v. Robbins


Nos. SC96182, SC96183, & SC96674


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


818 So. 2d 460; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 545; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 288



April 4, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Third District - Case Nos. 3D98-275 & 3D98-274 An Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case No. 2D98-03123 (Hillsborough County).

 Fuchs v. Robbins, 738 So. 2d 338, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 9590 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist. 1999).



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, the Second District of the Court of Appeal (Florida) held that appellant tax appraiser did not have standing in a case involving assessment of appellee taxpayer's property. In other combined cases, the Third District of the Court of Appeal (Florida) held that appellee tax appraiser had standing in a case involving assessment of appellant taxpayer's property. The tax appraiser and taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tax appraisers sought review of decisions of the value adjustment board (VAB) which had upheld challenges made by the taxpayers. The intermediate appellate court affirmed the lower court rulings in both cases. In one case, the intermediate appellate court held that the tax appraiser did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 196.012(6). In the second case, the intermediate appellate court held that the tax appraiser did have standing to challenge the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 192.042. The appellate court held that although state officers were allowed defensively to raise the question of a law's constitutionality, they were required to presume that legislation affecting their duties was valid, and did not have standing to initiate litigation for the purpose of determining otherwise. An appraiser was not allowed, in an action filed by a property appraiser seeking review of an adverse decision of the VAB which had overturned the appraiser's ad valorem tax assessment on a subject property, within an appeal pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 194.036, to challenge the constitutionality of an applicable valuation statute.


OUTCOME: One decision was affirmed, and one decision was reversed.

Schwab v. State


No. SC97008, No. SC00-1629


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


814 So. 2d 402; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 537; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 275



March 28, 2002, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order of the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Florida, denying his motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was released from prison after serving three and one-half years of an eight-year sentence for committing sexual battery on a 13-year-old boy. Several years later he was convicted again for first-degree murder, sexual battery of a child, and kidnapping. He was sentenced to death on the murder conviction and received consecutive life sentences on the other conviction. On direct appeal, petitioner's conviction and sentence was affirmed. He raised 11 claims in his postconviction appeal. Each claim was rejected. Petitioner presented no evidence to show how he was prejudiced by the absence of the transcripts of the grand jury proceeding. At the penalty phase, counsel was not ineffective for acknowledging petitioner's prior felony conviction for sexual battery.


OUTCOME: The denial of the postconviction motion was affirmed, and the petition for habeas corpus was denied.

719 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


No. SC00-514


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


814 So. 2d 390; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 440; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 250



March 21, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case No. 2D98-3946 (Manatee County).

 State v. Johnson, 751 So. 2d 183, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 1119 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State subpoenaed defendant's medical records and blood tests under Fla. Stat. ch. 27.04 (1997), got them, and charged her with DUI manslaughter. She moved to suppress. The trial court granted her motion. The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed and certified conflict with another district's decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was in a single-car crash in which her passenger died. She was hospitalized with injuries and in the course of treatment her blood was drawn. In seeking to prosecute her, the State tried to notify her, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3025(4)(d) (1997), that her hospital records were being subpoenaed. After the failed attempts to serve notice, which failed to include checking driver license records or post office forwarding addresses, both of which would have yielded the correct address, the State used the Fla. Stat. ch. 27.04 (1997) investigative subpoena power. The supreme court found that the State attorney's ch. 27.04 subpoena power could not override Fla. Stat. ch. 395.3025(4)(d)'s notice requirement. However the exclusionary rule did not, because of the State's past transgression, foreclose the State from subpoenaing defendant's records prospectively in a constitutional and statutorily permissible manner. The State had made a good faith effort to comply with ch. 395.3025's procedural requirements. The State could not use information it gathered from improperly obtained patient records when seeking a second subpoena under ch. 395.3025(4)(d).


OUTCOME: The decision was quashed and certain decisions of other district's were disapproved to an extent. The case was remanded.

Morrison v. State


No. SC94666


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


818 So. 2d 432; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 441; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 253



March 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari denied: Morrison v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7734 (U.S. Oct. 15, 2002).
Rehearing denied by Morrison v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2812 (Fla., May 29, 2002)
Writ of certiorari denied Morrison v. Florida, 537 U.S. 957, 123 S. Ct. 406, 154 L. Ed. 2d 308, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7734 (Oct. 15, 2002)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Post-conviction relief denied at, in part State v. Morrison, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 2349 (Fla., Nov. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Released for Publication May 29, 2002. An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Henry E. Davis, Judge - Case No. 97-991-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) of first-degree murder, armed robbery with a deadly weapon, burglary of a dwelling with intent to commit battery, and with an assault or battery. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder conviction and to consecutive life imprisonment terms for the other convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an elderly, disabled man's apartment, killed him, and stole his money. The supreme court found that (1) the trial court sufficiently inquired upon defendant's complaint to determine whether counsel was rendering effective assistance; (2) the trial court did not err in excusing for cause a venireperson who was unsure if he would be able to vote for the death sentence; (3) the trial court did not err in sustaining the State's peremptory strikes to venirepersons who expressed unequivocal discomfort with the death penalty; (4) any ambiguity in the prosecutor's comments as to the State's burden of proof was clarified by an instruction to disregard the statement and trial court readings of the standard reasonable doubt instructions; (5) the trial court did not err in sustaining a hearsay objection where counsel failed to advise the court of the relevancy of the answer he was seeking; (6) the trial court did not err in denying purported reputation evidence; (7) reasonable jurors could conclude that defendant committed premeditated murder; (8) the trial court did not err in applying an aggravating circumstance instruction; and (9) the death penalty was proportionate.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

721 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Comer v. Moore


No. SC00-1341


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


817 So. 2d 784; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 430; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 245



March 14, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 15, 2002. Released for Publication May 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.



DISPOSITION: Habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, contending that the 85 percent minimum service provision of Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275 was invalid and thus he was entitled to additional gain time.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving a nine-year sentence in connection with a number of crimes. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275(4)(b)(3), he could not be awarded more than 10 days of incentive gain time credit per month, and the total of his gain time could not exceed 15 percent of his sentence. In other words, the statute mandated that he actually serve a minimum of 85 percent of his sentence incarcerated. Defendant challenged this requirement as invalid. However, the general provision that created the requirement for serving 85 percent of the sentence imposed was enacted by Fla. Stat. ch. 95-294, § 2, otherwise known as the Stop Turning Out Prisoners Act. It amended Fla. Stat. ch. 944.275 to provide that all inmates, not just career criminals, with offense dates similar to defendant's, had to serve 85 percent of their sentences.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

722 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Advisory Opinion to the Ag Re Authorization for County Voters to Approve Or Disapprove Slot Machs. Within Existing Pari-Mutuel Facilities


No. SC01-1000


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


813 So. 2d 98; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 433; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 243



March 14, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Advisory Opinion to the Attorney General.



DISPOSITION: Proposal to be removed from the ballot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida Attorney General presented a proposed initiative petition to amend Fla. Const. art. X, § 19, to authorize county voters to approve or disapprove slot machines at existing pari-mutuel facilities.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the amendment proposal at issue failed to comport with the single subject requirement of Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. This limitation existed because § 3 did not afford the same opportunity for public hearing and debate that accompanied the proposal and drafting processes. The proposed amendment mandated imposition of a state tax on slot machines which would produce revenue subject to appropriation by the legislature. However, absent amendment to Fla. Const. art. XI, § 7, the proposed amendment would be subject to a two-thirds vote. The initiative purported to create a mechanism for authorizing and taxing slot machines for a particular purpose in the same proposal, which would effectively amend Fla. Const. art. XI, § 7, to remove the new state tax from the ambit of that provision. The ballot summary provided both that the amendment authorize county voters to approve or disapprove slot machines at existing pari-mutuel facilities only and that, by simple majority vote, rather than the two-thirds vote, for new state taxes, the legislature would be required to license, regulate and tax such slot machines, and to use the proceeds for a specified purpose.


OUTCOME: The supreme court directed that the proposed amendment be removed from the ballot.

 

723 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Malicki v. Doe


No. SC01-179


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


814 So. 2d 347; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 434; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 234



March 14, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Third District - Case No. 3D99-549. (Dade County).

 Doe v. Malicki, 771 So. 2d 545, 2000 Fla. App. LEXIS 9429, 25 Fla. L. Weekly D 1756, 25 Fla. L. Weekly D 1852 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist. 2000) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent parishioners sued petitioners, a priest and neighborhood and local religious organizations, alleging that the priest molested them on the neighborhood organization's premises; he unlawfully served alcohol; and the organizations were negligent in their hiring, retention, and supervision of him. Dismissal of the suit was reversed by the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida). The priest and organizations sought review.


OVERVIEW: The parishioners were a minor and an adult female who worked for the organizations. They alleged sexual assault and/or battery. The organizations' motion to dismiss argued that resolution of the issues involved internal ecclesiastical decisions of their world organization as required by its law, and therefore the First Amendment barred resolution by the civil court. The court of appeal framed the issue as whether the neighborhood and local organizations had reason to know of their priest's misconduct and did nothing to prevent reasonably foreseeable harm from being inflicted on the parishioners, which did not require inquiry into the religion's religious doctrines and practices. The supreme court addressed the negligence counts and joined the majority of jurisdictions in finding no First Amendment bar to "third-party" tort actions against religious institutions grounded on alleged torts by clergy. Laws establishing standards of conduct implicated neither the Free Exercise nor Establishment Clause unless adherence to those standards interfered more than incidentally with religious belief or activity. The foreseeability inquiry went to the specific danger at issue.


OUTCOME: The decision was approved. A decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) was disapproved. The case was remanded.
