Carroll v. State


Nos. SC94611; SC00-46


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


815 So. 2d 601; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 383; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 214



March 7, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing Denied April 19, 2002. Released for Publication April 19, 2002.
Post-conviction proceeding at Carroll v. State, 904 So. 2d 430, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1188 (Fla., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Belvin Perry, Judge - Case No. CR90-12464, and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Carroll v. State, 636 So. 2d 1316, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 491 (Fla., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sexual battery on a child under 12; 3 aggravators and 1 nonstatutory mitigator were found; and he was sentenced to death. The conviction and sentence were affirmed. The Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) denied him Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 postconviction relief. He appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: A 10-year-old girl was raped and strangled. Her front door was found ajar. Witnesses saw defendant driving her stepfather's missing truck. Defendant was found a mile from the truck with blood on his shirt and genitalia. Semen, saliva, and pubic hair consistent with his was found on the victim. The supreme court found that claims of ineffective assistance of postconviction counsel were not a valid basis for relief. Even assuming trial counsel was deficient for not providing additional background information to doctors who examined defendant's competence to stand trial, neither doctor testified that, with the materials, they would have found defendant incompetent. Contrary to defendant's assertion that trial counsel did not present much of an insanity defense, counsel presented lay and expert witnesses. Even with additional information collected by collateral counsel, another doctor acknowledged that it was a close call whether two statutory mental mitigators existed. By not providing trial counsel with requested mitigation-witness names, defendant could not claim ineffective counsel in that regard. The prosecutor's calling defendant the "boogie man" was not fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Moore v. State


Nos. SC00-2483, SC01-708


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

Moore v. State, 701 So. 2d 545, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1508 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted armed robbery, conspiracy to commit armed robbery, armed burglary, and arson. Three aggravators and two mitigators were found and defendant was sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Five years after conviction, defendant initiated Fla. R. Crim. Sireci v. Moore


No. SC01-1399


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


825 So. 2d 882; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 340; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 183



February 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Petition Denied April 15, 2002. Released for Publication April 15, 2002.
Later proceeding at Sireci v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 759 (Fla., Apr. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus
Sireci v. State, 773 So. 2d 34, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1754 (Fla., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner's first-degree murder conviction and death penalty were affirmed. After a limited evidentiary hearing on his second postconviction relief motion, he was granted a new penalty phase, and the death penalty was again imposed. Subsequent postconviction relief motions were denied, and he sought habeas corpus relief, in an original proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner alleged his appellate counsel was ineffective, and his execution would be cruel and unusual. The supreme court held the evidence showed the dominant motive for the murder was avoiding petitioner's arrest. Aggravating factors applied to his punishment were not duplicative as the avoiding lawful arrest aggravator focused on his motive; the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravator focused on how the crime was executed; and the in the course of a robbery or for pecuniary gain aggravator focused on the crime's context. In spite of the trial court's failure to state the individual facets of its finding that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated, the evidence was sufficient, and, if it was not, sufficient evidence of four other aggravators existed. Petitioner's shackling before the jury was justified by his attempt to have a witness killed, and he was not prejudiced, as the shackling was concealed. Counsel was not ineffective by not raising these issues. His claim that the death penalty was cruel and unusual because he might be incompetent at the time of his execution was not ripe.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's requested relief was denied.

Olive v. Maas


No. SC00-317


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


811 So. 2d 644; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 219; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 139



February 14, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Olive v. Maas, 911 So. 2d 837, 2005 Fla. App. LEXIS 13869 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 1st Dist., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Notice of Appeal and Notice of Cross-Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court in and for Leon County, N. Sanders Sauls, Judge, Case No. 99-1027 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D00-258.
Olive v. Maas, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 534 (Fla., Feb. 23, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lawyer sought a declaration as to his rights under the Registry Act, Fla. Stat. ch. 27.710 (Supp. 1998), and his proposed contract with appellee Executive Director of the Commission on the Administration of Justice in Capital Cases. The trial court permanently enjoined the director from excluding him from the registry. Both sides appealed. The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the case to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The lawyer routinely represented death row defendants in postconviction proceedings. A judge appointed him to represent a particular defendant, but the lawyer declined to sign the contract with appellee commission comptroller. Other counsel was appointed. The lawyer alleged (1) that strict application of act's fee limits unconstitutionally curtailed a trial court's power to ensure adequate representation, (2) limits in the act would compel him to violate the rules of professional conduct, and (3) that the director had excluded him from the registry list of available lawyers for such defendants. The supreme court found that the lawyer had standing to seek, and the trial court had jurisdiction to enter, declaratory relief as to the first counts. Although the lawyer never signed the contract, he had been on the list, initiated a meeting with the client, and never declined appointment. Trial courts were authorized to grant fees in excess of the statutory schedule where unusual circumstances existed in capital collateral cases. The professional conduct rules themselves prohibited frivolous claims. The director only excluded the lawyer from the list as to the present client.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court to dissolve the permanent injunction.

Gilliam v. State


No. SC95370, No. SC00-1438


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


817 So. 2d 768; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 168; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 129



February 7, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 23, 2002. Released for Publication May 23, 2002.
Post-conviction relief denied at Gilliam v. Sec'y for the Dep't of Corr., 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 5182 (11th Cir. Fla., Mar. 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County, Michael Chavies, Judge - Case No. F82-14766, and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Gilliam v. State, 582 So. 2d 610, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 718 (Fla., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Denial of motion for postconviction relief affirmed and petition for habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Miami-Dade County (Florida) of first-degree murder and sexual battery. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. The trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant appealed the judgment. Defendant also filed a habeas corpus petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had a history of child abuse, drug and alcohol abuse, epilepsy, and domestic violence, was convicted of sexually assaulting and strangling a woman. Defendant alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. The supreme court found that (1) counsel was not ineffective in making a tactical decision to reveal to the jury defendant's prior rape conviction based upon counsel's understanding of the facts surrounding the rape, where the State later rebutted defense counsel's version of the rape; (2) counsel was not ineffective because counsel presented evidence of defendant's intoxication on the night of the crime, as well as his history of drug and alcohol abuse; (3) counsel was not ineffective for failing to discover police records indicating the victim was a prostitute, since the evidence would have been irrelevant and inadmissible; (4) counsel was not ineffective for failing to request an instruction as to epileptic seizures negating specific intent, since counsel obtained an insanity defense instruction; and (5) counsel was not ineffective for not presenting evidence to the penalty jury that was later presented to the sentencing judge.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's postconviction motion was affirmed, and the supreme court denied defendant's petition for habeas corpus.

Bottoson v. State

SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

January 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari denied, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4997 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Stay granted by Bottoson v. Florida, 534 U.S. 1121, 151 L. Ed. 2d 962, 122 S. Ct. 981, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 609 (2002).
Writ of certiorari denied: Bottoson v. Florida, 536 U.S. 962, 153 L. Ed. 2d 844, 122 S. Ct. 2670, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4997 (2002).

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Anthony H. Johnson, Judge--Case No. 79-04512, and An Original Proceeding--Habeas Corpus Bill Jennings, Capital Collateral Regional Counsel--Middle Region, Tampa, Florida.
Bottoson v. State, 443 So. 2d 962, 1983 Fla. LEXIS 3184 (Fla., 1983).



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction relief denied, habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an inmate under a death sentence, appealed an order of the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Florida, which denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant also filed a successive petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that (1) he was mentally retarded and that his upcoming execution violated the Eighth Amendment; (2) the trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's request for a Single Photon Emission Computed Tomography (SPECT) Scan or a Positron Emission Tomography (PET) Scan; and (3) the supreme court did not properly conduct a de novo review of defendant's first postconviction motion. The supreme court held that (1) defendant failed to prove retardation under the test for determining mental retardation where he failed to meet two out of the three requirements of the test; (2) trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant leave to obtain a SPECT/PET scan because it appeared that defendant's claim that he had brain damage not only was speculative, but he had also failed to relate the need for this testing to any substantive claim he had made in his motion for postconviction relief; and (3) defendant's habeas claim was procedurally barred because he improperly attempted to obtain a second appeal of issues that were raised prior to his motion for postconviction relief and his appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Sweet v. State


No. SC00-1509


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


810 So. 2d 854; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 138; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 113



January 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Remanded by, Petition denied by, in part Sweet v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 978 (Fla., July 1, 2004).


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Frederick Tygart, Judge--Case No. 91-2899-CF.
Sweet v. State, 624 So. 2d 1138, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1301 (Fla., 1993)



DISPOSITION: Denial of post-conviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, three counts of attempted first-degree murder, and burglary. Four aggravators, no statutory mitigators, and the nonstatutory mitigator that defendant "lacked true parental guidance as a teenager," were found. He was sentenced to death, which was affirmed. The Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida) denied postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had felony convictions. He apparently was an unidentified perpetrator in the robbery of a woman. Later he ordered her to let him in her place. The four females present opened the door to leave and defendant forced his way in and shot them, killing a girl. His theory of defense was that someone else was the shooter, but no such evidence was presented. The supreme court found that there was no evidence that the woman's boyfriend, who had been violent toward her in the past, was the shooter, and defendant presented no such evidence postconviction. Presentation of another potential witness might have allowed that witness's out-of-court identification of defendant as the shooter to come into evidence. Other potential witnesses would have presented cumulative testimony and opened the door to testimony of defendant's juvenile record. His claim that counsel did not adequately prepare was belied by the fact that he pushed counsel to bring his case to trial. Thus his right to effective assistance was not violated. As to the mental health mitigation presented postconviction, its presence at penalty phase would not have led to imposition of a sentence other than death.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

731 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Wike v. State


No. SC00-2141


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


813 So. 2d 12; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 69; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 95



January 24, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 15, 2002. Released for Publication March 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Paul A. Rasmussen, Judge--Case No. 88-547-CF.

Wike v. Florida, 522 U.S. 1058, 139 L. Ed. 2d 655, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 217, 118 S. Ct. 714 (1998).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida) of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, sexual battery, and attempted murder. Following an evidentiary hearing, the trial court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant removed two little girls from their home and drove them to a secluded area. There he raped the girls and slit their throats with a knife. One girl survived and identified defendant. Defendant alleged ineffective assistance of counsel on his post-conviction motion. The supreme court found that defendant failed to prove ineffectiveness of counsel in trial counsel's (1) failure to move for change of venue against defendant's wishes; (2) failure to investigate witnesses and present alibi evidence, since defendant failed to prove a viable alibi defense from witnesses could have been presented; (3) failure to ensure defendant's presence at all critical stages of the trial; and (4) failure to ensure defendant's presence at sidebar conferences during the penalty phase.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

732 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Floyd v. State


Nos. SC97043; SC00-1533


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


808 So. 2d 175; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 28; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 75



January 17, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Richard A. Luce, Judge--Case Nos. 84-00578 CFANO and 84-00589 CFANO and an Original Proceeding--Habeas Corpus.
Floyd v. State, 497 So. 2d 1211, 1986 Fla. LEXIS 2841 (Fla., 1986)



DISPOSITION: Habeas corpus denied, denial of post-conviction relief affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. On remand, two aggravators and no mitigators were found, and he was resentenced to death; the sentence was affirmed on direct appeal. The Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 postconviction motion and motion to reconsider. He appealed and petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Defendant cashed a check on a woman's account. The next day she was found dead in her bedroom, killed the previous afternoon, according to the medical examiner. Defendant tried to cash another of her checks and was arrested trying to flee. Her blood was found in his clothing. Defendant claimed that his trial counsel was ineffective in the guilt phase and during voir dire for resentencing, and did not adequately investigate mitigating evidence during the penalty phase. The supreme court found that the trial court should have held an evidentiary hearing on these claims. Upon review of the summary denial of postconviction relief without an evidentiary hearing, the supreme court had to accept defendant's factual allegations as true to the extent they were not refuted by the record. Defendant pointed out that his original counsel called no defense witnesses and was later disbarred. He alleged that information relating to his severe substance abuse and organic brain damage was available to penalty phase counsel. The trial court should have held an evidentiary hearing on defendant's Brady claims. Photos of the victim were relevant to show the extent of her injuries.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief without an evidentiary hearing was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The matter was remanded for the limited purpose of conducting an evidentiary hearing on defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of counsel and his Brady claim. The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

733 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


King v. State


No. SC02-01 & SC02-02


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


808 So. 2d 1237; 2002 Fla. LEXIS 25; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 65



January 16, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 17, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: King v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4996 (U.S. June 28, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Susan F. Schaeffer, Judge--Case Nos. 77-01696CFANO & 77-02173CFANO, and An Original Proceeding--Habeas Corpus.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's denial of King's successive 3.850 motion was affirmed, the successive habeas corpus petition was denied, and all pending motions for stay of execution was denied. King's separate motion for a stay of execution pending his application for a writ of certiorari from the United States Supreme Court was also denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's murder conviction and death sentence were affirmed. Twenty years later, his third death warrant, the second after resentencing, was signed. His motion for DNA testing was dismissed. Defendant filed a successive Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851 motion which the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) denied. He appealed and also filed a successive petition for writ of habeas corpus and motions seeking a stay of execution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel filed public record requests and sought DNA testing of vaginal washings and a rectal swab taken from the murder victim. He also requested testing of hairs. The postconviction court found the DNA request sufficient and ordered the State to respond. The State responded that the washings and swab no longer existed and therefore could not be tested. The trial court found that DNA testing was not known in when the crimes occurred, and the State could not have known that specimens destroyed after other analysis might someday have been scrutinizable for DNA. Defendant showed no bad faith on the State's part. Even in 2002, a medical examiner could destroy such specimens after a year. The supreme court agreed that defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims were procedurally barred. He showed no prejudice from a juror whose father was in law enforcement, which may or may not have been known by defendant's counsel at trial. Although he was convicted on circumstantial evidence, none of it had changed and defendant had no new evidence. There was no law providing repeat DNA testing. Aggravating circumstances did not have to be charged by indictment.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed. No motion for rehearing was allowed.

Francis v. State


No. SC94385


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


808 So. 2d 110; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2306; 27 Fla. L. Weekly S 2



December 20, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 3, 2002.

Released for Publication February 11, 2002.
Rehearing denied by Francis v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2810 (Fla., Feb. 11, 2002)
Writ of certiorari denied Francis v. Florida, 537 U.S. 1090, 154 L. Ed. 2d 635, 123 S. Ct. 696, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 9297 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Edward A. Garrison, Judge--Case No. 97-8545 CF A02 W.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Palm Beach County, Florida, convicted defendant by jury of two counts of first-degree murder, of robbery with a deadly weapon, and one count of grand theft and of burglary with assault or battery. Four statutory aggravators, two statutory mitigators, and six nonstatutory mitigators were found. He was sentenced, among other things, to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lived with his mother, nephews, and aunt next door to two elderly twin widows. A nephew saw defendant walk from his home with a duffel bag in the direction of the widows' home. That day, the two widows were found stabbed to death therein. Evidence revealed that on that day defendant called the nephew and asked him if he had seen the bag's contents, defendant visited his heroin-dealer in a car matching the victims', saw the news about them but did not react, tried to burn items including a lady's pocketbook, and returned home in different clothes without glancing at the taped-off crime scene. The supreme court held that there had been probable cause to arrest him. The record did not show that officers left him in an interrogation room for over three hours in an effort to elicit a statement. Defendant reinitiated statements to police after having requested a lawyer. The trial court properly accepted as race-neutral the State's challenge to a juror who seemingly responded light-heartedly when told of the murder charges. Robbery was not shown to have been an afterthought. The Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(m) aggravator was not shown.


OUTCOME: The convictions and death sentences were affirmed.

Evans v. State


No. SC96404


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


808 So. 2d 92; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2291; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 823



December 13, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari denied: Evans v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7648 (U.S. Oct. 15, 2002). Released for Publication February 12, 2002.
Rehearing denied by Evans v. State, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 2816 (Fla., Feb. 12, 2002)
Writ of certiorari denied Evans v. Florida, 537 U.S. 951, 123 S. Ct. 416, 154 L. Ed. 2d 297, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7648 (Oct. 15, 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Evans v. State, 995 So. 2d 933, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1459 (Fla., Aug. 28, 2008)
Request denied by State v. Evans, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1202 (Fla., May 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Robert A. Hawley, Judge - Case No. 97-754-CFA.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County (Florida) of murder and sentenced to death. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim's wife hired defendant to kill the victim. A six-year preindictment delay did not prejudice defendant, absent record evidence supporting his claim of unavailable witnesses. His unpreserved claim of material differences between the complaint and trial evidence did not require reversal, as he was able to show the jury such differences. Defendant was properly precluded from asking about cannabanoids in the victim's blood, because he did not lay a proper foundation. A detective's direct examination did not elicit hearsay and did not "open the door" to let defendant elicit hearsay on cross-examination, nor did the "rule of completeness" require such cross-examination. Excluding defendant's parents from individual juror voir dire was not error. The State could ask prospective jurors' views on the testimony of an individual granted immunity. The State's guilt phase closing argument could state evidentiary inferences. Defendant did not show an immaturity mitigator. Failure to consider defendant's artistic ability mitigator was harmless. Defendant's relative culpability made his death sentence proportionate to a co-defendant's life sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

736 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hayes v. State


No. SC96813


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


803 So. 2d 695; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2278; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 780



November 21, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case Nos. 3D99-566 & 3D98-929 (Dade County).

Hayes v. State, 748 So. 2d 1042, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 12534 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 3d Dist. 1999) 



DISPOSITION: Approved the Third District's decision and held that Hayes properly was convicted of both robbery and grand theft of a motor vehicle. Also approved the First District's decision in Henderson and disapproved the Fifth District's decision in Castleberry.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery under Fla. Stat. ch. 812.13 (1997) and grand theft of a motor vehicle under Fla. Stat. ch. 812.014 (1997). In a decision acknowledged to be in conflict with that of another court of appeal, the Florida Third District Court of Appeal affirmed defendant's convictions, and he sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed the victim in the victim's residence, taking a number of items, including the victim's car keys. Defendant then went outside the residence and took the victim's automobile. To determine whether defendant's prosecution and punishment for robbery and theft of the automobile were barred by double jeopardy, the trial court had to examine the location of the items taken, the lapse of time between the takings, the number of owners of the items taken, and the intervening events between the takings. After defendant took the items from the victim's residence, the robbery was complete. Defendant exited the residence to steal the victim's automobile. Only upon taking the car did the grand theft of the automobile occur. Thus, the taking of the items from inside the residence occurred at a different time and a different place than the taking of the motor vehicle. Although there was only a single victim and there were no acts intervening between the two crimes, the robbery was sufficiently separate in time, place, and circumstances from the theft of the motor vehicle parked outside the residence to constitute distinct and independent criminal acts.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

Looney v. State


No. SC00-458


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


803 So. 2d 656; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2210; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 733



November 1, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 21, 2001. Released for Publication December 21, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Looney v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5049 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Looney v. Florida, 536 U.S. 966, 122 S. Ct. 2678, 153 L. Ed. 2d 850, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5049 (June 28, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Looney v. State, 941 So. 2d 1017, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1339 (Fla., June 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, N. Sanders Sauls, Judge - Case No. 1997-215-CF.
Hertz v. State, 803 So. 2d 629, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2209 (Fla., Nov. 1, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed the judgment and sentence of the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, Florida, which imposed the death penalty upon the defendant for burglary of a dwelling while armed, armed robbery with a firearm, arson of a dwelling, and use of a firearm during the commission of a felony. Jurisdiction was provided by Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed arguing that 1) a venireperson was impermissibly struck from the venire because her opposition to the death penalty did not rise to the level justifying exclusion; 2) the trial court erred in admitting evidence of collateral crimes; 3) the trial court erred by admitting several particularly gruesome photographs of the victims; 4) seven issues relating to the penalty phase. The supreme court held that 1) the State's challenge for cause was proper because the venireperson was unwilling to consider the penalties provided by state law; 2) the nexus between the flight and the murders was strong, and defendants' actions were relevant to consciousness of guilt and did not become an impermissible facet; 3) it was error to admit irrelevant autopsy photographs, but it was harmless given the direct evidence; 4) Apprendi did not apply to capital sentencing schemes, victim impact evidence was properly admitted, and the sentence was proportional given the five aggravating circumstances found: previous violent felony, committed during robbery and arson, for pecuniary gain, commission to avoid arrest; cold, calculated, and premeditated; and heinous, atrocious, and cruel.


OUTCOME: The defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Hertz v. State


No. SC00-457


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


803 So. 2d 629; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2209; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 725



November 1, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 21, 2001. Released for Publication December 21, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Hertz v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5013 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Related proceeding at Looney v. State, 803 So. 2d 656, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2210 (Fla., Nov. 1, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Hertz v. Florida, 536 U.S. 963, 122 S. Ct. 2673, 153 L. Ed. 2d 846, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5013 (June 28, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hertz v. State, 941 So. 2d 1031, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1342 (Fla., June 22, 2006)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hertz v. McNeil, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 95303 (N.D. Fla., Sept. 25, 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Vacated by, in part, Remanded by Hertz v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1082 (Fla., May 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, N. Sanders Sauls, Judge - Case No. 97-214CF.
Hertz v. State, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 259 (Fla., Jan. 29, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Wakulla County, Florida, that convicted him a on a jury verdict of first-degree murder, burglary of a dwelling while armed with a firearm, armed robbery with a firearm, arson of a dwelling, and use of a firearm in the commission of a felony, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two accomplices robbed the victims, shot them, and set fire to their home. They fled in the victims' vehicles. One of them testified against defendant and the other accomplice, and received a life sentence. The appellate court held that the State's challenge for cause of a juror who stated she could not impose the death penalty was properly upheld. The finding that defendant was competent to stand trial was supported by the evidence. Any error in admitting an autopsy photo was harmless. Evidence that defendant tried to run down an officer was properly admitted. The evidence, including the accomplice's testimony that defendant killed the victims in both a premeditated manner and during the course of a robbery, burglary, or arson, was sufficient to convict. Aggravating factors were properly applied: that defendant committed the murders to avoid arrest; that they were committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner; that the murders were heinous and cruel, and were committed for pecuniary gain. The death sentence was not disproportionate, and the trial court properly found that the testifying accomplice's conduct had been less culpable than defendant's.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed.

 

741 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. T.G.


No. SC96081


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


800 So. 2d 204; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2136; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 709



October 25, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict. Fifth District - (Seminole County). Case No. 5D98-1406.

 T.G. v. State, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 293 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist. 1999) 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed Court of Appeals. Case remanded to the trial court so it can properly advise T.G. of his right to assistance of counsel, ensure by a thorough inquiry that any waiver is free and intelligent, and allow T.G. to enter a new plea if appropriate.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, pleaded no contest in the trial court to felony charges and violation of community control. The Florida Fifth District Court of Appeal (Seminole County) reversed the trial court's adjudication of delinquency and disposition. The State sought review, and the supreme court accepted jurisdiction based on a conflict with other district courts of appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was without counsel at both the plea and the disposition hearings. At the plea hearing, the trial court asked defendant whether he wished to have appointed counsel but made no further inquiry after defendant answered in the negative. The trial court made no inquiry at the disposition hearing with respect to counsel. Defendant did not bring a motion in the trial court to withdraw the plea prior to appealing the judgment. The court of appeal disagreed with decisions from other districts and found that the requirement in criminal cases that appellate review of a plea was precluded absent a motion to withdraw the plea did not apply to juvenile cases. The supreme court held that a juvenile who was represented by counsel could not challenge the plea on appeal without having filed a motion to withdraw. However, the trial court's failure to follow Fla. R. Juv. P. 8.165 to determine whether defendant made a free and intelligent waiver of the right to counsel was fundamental error, and the resulting plea was involuntary as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal's opinion was disapproved to the extent that it held that juveniles were not required to file a motion to withdraw a plea before challenging the validity of the plea, but the result was approved and the case was remanded.

 

742 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. SC96333


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


804 So. 2d 1218; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2137; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 718



October 25, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, A. Thomas Mihok, Judge - Case No. 80-101. Johnson v. State *1, 58713 (Nov. 17, 1983, Fla., Per Curiam) 442 So. 2d 193, 1983 Fla. LEXIS 2959 
Johnson v. State, 442 So. 2d 193, 1983 Fla. LEXIS 2959 (Fla., 1983)



DISPOSITION: No error found in trial court's summary denial of Appellant's rule 3.850 motion for postconviction relief and order below affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) of first-degree murder and second-degree murder. The conviction was affirmed on appeal, as was the denial of his first post-conviction relief motion and petition for writ of habeas corpus. He filed a second post-conviction relief motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's claim for post-conviction relief based on newly discovered evidence had to show the evidence would probably produce an acquittal. A Miranda card defendant had refused to sign after his arrest did not satisfy this requirement due to his subsequent unrelated inculpatory statements. These statements also prevented proof of prejudice from an alleged Brady violation. Evidence that his second-degree murder victim was the type of person who would have resisted defendant's robbery attempt merely bolstered his second-degree murder conviction, instead of first-degree murder. Defendant's inability to obtain juror background information did not support post-conviction relief, in the absence of reasons why the records were not obtained when the first post-conviction relief motion was filed and allegations of specific juror misconduct revealed since that motion. Defendant was not allowed to interview the jurors in the absence of sworn allegations which, if true, would require the trial court to order a new trial. Electrocution and lethal injection were constitutional, as was the statute allowing an inmate to choose between them.


OUTCOME: The trial court's summary denial of defendant's post-conviction relief motion was affirmed.

Evans v. State


No. SC95993


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


800 So. 2d 182; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2008; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 675



October 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Evans v. State, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 2174 (Fla., Nov. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Jay Paul Cohen, Judge - Case No. CR 96-5639/A.



DISPOSITION: affirm Evans' conviction for first-degree murder and his sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida) of murder and was sentenced to death after the trial court found him to be competent to stand trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, the victim, and two others planned to commit a robbery. The victim drove off and abandoned the others before the robbery was completed. When the victim later entered defendant's apartment, he was immediately grabbed and beaten, bound and gagged, and then forced to wait in a back room when police officers came to the door. After the officers left, the victim was marched outside to a culvert where defendant chastised him for leaving them, told him they would be the last persons he would ever see, and then shot him six times. On appeal, the supreme court found the trial court did not err in (1) finding defendant competent to stand trial; (2) denying defendant's motion for a mistrial after a State's witness referred to defendant's prior criminal record; (3) finding shell casings to be relevant evidence; (4) finding the murder was committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner and was especially heinous, atrocious, and cruel; and (5) balancing the aggravating factors against the mitigating factors. Further, admitting evidence of defendant's gang membership was harmless error and the death sentence was proportional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Card v. State


No. SC00-182


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


803 So. 2d 613; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2006; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 670



October 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Writ of certiorari denied: Card v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5012 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Corrected by, Rehearing denied by Card v. State, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2321 (Fla., Dec. 20, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Card v. Florida, 536 U.S. 963, 122 S. Ct. 2673, 153 L. Ed. 2d 845, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5012 (June 28, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Card v. State, 992 So. 2d 810, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1231 (Fla., 2008)
Writ of habeas corpus granted, Vacated by, Remanded by Card v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 984 (Fla., May 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Bay County, Dedee Costello, Judge - Case No. 81-518.
Card v. State, 652 So. 2d 344, 1995 Fla. LEXIS 12 (Fla., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Bay County (Florida) of murder, robbery, and kidnapping and sentenced to death. In postconviction proceedings, his death sentence was vacated after an evidentiary hearing because of an improper procedure used in permitting the State to prepare the original sentencing order. After a new penalty phase hearing before a new jury, the trial court imposed the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed an office clerk repeatedly during a robbery, kidnapped her, and drove her to a secluded area. Defendant then stabbed her to death, leaving her body. On appeal, the supreme court found (1) defendant waived his objection to the successor judge's denial of defendant's motion for recusal by not raising it at the time she ruled on the motion or when the order was entered; (2) the trial court did not err in failing to grant a mistrial with respect to the prosecutor's comments during closing argument because the trial court gave the jurors curative instructions and any errors did not compromise the integrity of the judicial process or deprive defendant of a fair penalty phase hearing; (3) there was competent, substantial evidence to support the statutory aggravators the trial court applied; (4) while the trial court erred in failing to find and weigh certain mitigating evidence, the statutory and nonstatutory mitigating evidence would not have resulted in a lesser sentence; and (5) although a relative's testimony exceeded the proper bounds of victim impact evidence, defense counsel did not preserve the issue for review by contemporaneously objecting to the testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

745 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Bover v. State


No. SC95649


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


797 So. 2d 1246; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1927; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 652



October 4, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict Third District - Case No. 3D98-1835 (Dade County).



DISPOSITION: Quashed decision below, approve Judge, Bell, Botelho and Freshman and remanded for proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded no contest in the trial court as a habitual offender and was sentenced. His motion for correction of an illegal sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) was denied, and the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed, noting that its decision conflicted with other district courts of appeal. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's motion to correct an illegal sentence under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) alleged he was sentenced on the predicate offenses in the same proceeding. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084(5) (1993), for an offense to count as a prior felony for habitual offender adjudication, defendant had to have been sentenced separately for it from any other prior felony used to establish the adjudication. The State conceded defendant's predicate felony sentences did not meet this requirement. The court of appeal affirmed denial of relief, finding a challenge to the habitual offender adjudication had to be brought under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, and was subject to that rule's two-year limitation period. Because the requisite predicate felonies essential to qualify defendant for habitualization did not exist, his erroneous habitual offender adjudication could be corrected under Rule 3.800(a), so long as the error was apparent from the face of the record. Because defendant did not originally object to his adjudication on the basis of a lack of requisite prior sequential convictions, the State could, on remand, present evidence of other convictions which would satisfy that requirement.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal's decision was quashed, and the matter was remanded.

 

746 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Amendments to Fla. Rules of Crim. Proc. 3.704 & 3.992 (crim. Punishment Code)


No. SC01-1446


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


810 So. 2d 826; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1929; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 626

747 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Downs v. Moore


No. SC00-2186


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


801 So. 2d 906; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1905; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 632



September 26, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 3, 2001. Released for Publication December 3, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Downs v. State, 572 So. 2d 895, 1990 Fla. LEXIS 1191 (Fla., 1990)



DISPOSITION: We conclude that Downs is not entitled to relief and hereby deny the petition for writ of habeas corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's murder conviction was affirmed, as well as the denial of his motion for postconviction relief, he filed a habeas corpus petition in the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise a claim of the prosecutor's improper comment on defendant's silence when questioned by police because defendant had waived his right to silence and trial counsel did not preserve the issue for review. The mitigation instructions proposed by defendant and denied by the trial court were adequately covered by the trial court's "catch-all" mitigation instruction and defendant's argument, so the failure to raise the issue on appeal was not ineffective assistance. Defendant did not make the necessary showing in his motions to disqualify the prosecutor's office and the trial court, so failing to argue this on appeal was not ineffective assistance. An admitted driver's license with defendant's picture and another person's name was not used as an improper nonstatutory aggravator, nor was the issue preserved for appeal, so the failure to raise it was not ineffective assistance. Trial counsel also did not object to the prosecutor's argument asking the jury to impose a death sentence, so appellate counsel was not ineffective for not raising this unpreserved issue.


OUTCOME: Defendant's habeas corpus petition was denied.

 

748 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


Nos. SC96641, SC00-473


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


796 So. 2d 511; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1865; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 621



September 20, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Diana M. Allen, Judge - Case No. 86-12224 Div. C and An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's summary denial. Finally, we deny Thompson's petition for habeas relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) of first degree murder, and the conviction was eventually affirmed. The trial court summarily denied his motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed that denial and petitioned the supreme court for habeas corpus relief.


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant's counsel did not challenge for cause a juror who had difficulty accepting the idea defendant had a right not to testify. Counsel also did not use a peremptory challenge to excuse the juror, nor did he use any peremptory challenges. At the crime scene, a male Caucasian hair was found inside the female victim's underpants. Defendant was African-American. Counsel did not investigate the hair's origin. At trial, a witness testified, to defendant's surprise and in the jury's presence, concerning defendant being seen on the day of the crime with a gun. The prosecutor was aware of the information prior to trial. Counsel did not request a hearing on whether the prosecutor violated discovery rules by not revealing the information. An evidentiary hearing on the claims was required. Defendant's other ineffective assistance claims on appeal were rejected. Defendant's habeas petition argued appellate counsel should have asserted trial court error by not excusing the juror. The claim was rejected because trial counsel had not exhausted all peremptory challenges.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed in that three of defendant's claims were remanded for an evidentiary hearing. Defendant's habeas petition was denied.

 

749 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brake


No. SC00-119


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


796 So. 2d 522; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1867; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 608; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 651



September 20, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity

Second District - Case No. 2D98-02773.



DISPOSITION: We reverse in part and affirm in part the decision below. As interpreted by this Court, we conclude that section 787.025 is not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad, but that section 787.015(2)(b) must be deleted as an unconstitutional statutory presumption. We remand to the trial court to allow the defendant to withdraw his plea of nolo contendere and to conduct further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of violating Fla. Stat. Ann. § 787.025 (1997), upon his plea of nolo contendre, reserving the right to appeal denial of his motion to dismiss the information and declare § 787.025 unconstitutional. He appealed. Florida's Second District Court of Appeal declared the statute invalid. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: According to police, the defendant approached a 10-year-old girl who was playing and asked her if she wanted to see his house and get a toy. He gave her a toy and she left with him on his bicycle. The sole issue on appeal to the district court was the trial court's denial of his motion to dismiss on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutionally vague for not defining the term "other than lawful purpose." The Second District Court of Appeal ruled the statute was unconstitutionally vague and reversed his conviction. The district court found Fla. Stat. Ann. § 787.025 unconstitutionally vague because it did not define the term "for other than a lawful purpose." The supreme court concluded the term "for other than a lawful purpose" could be defined in a manner that saved the statute from vagueness and overbreadth and resolved any vagueness doubts in favor of defendants.


OUTCOME: The decision below was reversed in part and affirmed in part and remanded to the trial court to allow the defendant to withdraw his plea of nolo contendere and to conduct further proceedings.

 

750 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Stewart v. State


No. SC96177


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


801 So. 2d 59; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1869; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 615



September 20, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Daniel L. Perry, Judge - Case Nos. 85-4025; 85-4825.
Stewart v. State, 588 So. 2d 972, 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1592 (Fla., 1991)



DISPOSITION: We affirm the trial court's denial of Stewart's 3.850 motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida) of first-degree felony murder, attempted second-degree murder with a firearm, robbery with a firearm, and arson. The convictions were affirmed on appeal, and the trial court denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victims picked up defendant when he was hitchhiking. When they stopped to drop him off, he shot them, and one eventually died. Defendant argued he received ineffective counsel assistance because counsel did not use a voluntary intoxication defense and did not present evidence in the penalty phase of his childhood abuse. Counsel's strategic decision not to use voluntary intoxication, due to defendant's detailed crime accounts, was not ineffective assistance. Neither defendant nor any family member interviewed mentioned childhood abuse. The record did not support defendant's allegations that counsel did not obtain jail records of his suicide attempts or inadequately prepared his mental health expert. The prosecution's failure to provide defendant's jail records was not a Brady violation because the information was equally available to defendant as to the prosecution. The trial court's decision not to remove defendant's shackles before the jury did not abuse discretion as the shackles were unobtrusive, given defendant's stationary position at counsel table during trial, and necessary, given defendant having removed manacles on previous occasions.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

751 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Ocala Breeders' Sales Co. v. Fla. Gaming Ctrs.


No. SC95561


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


793 So. 2d 899; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1580; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 521



August 16, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 1D97-4783.



DISPOSITION: First District's decision finding section 550.615(9) unconstitutional as a special law affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff gaming center filed a complaint for declaratory judgment against defendant breeders and defendant Florida Division of Pari-Mutuel Wagering, asking the trial court to declare Fla. Stat. ch. 550.615(9) unconstitutional. After the trial court declared the statute unconstitutional, the breeders and the division appealed to the Florida First District Court of Appeal. The appellate court affirmed the trial court. The breeders appealed.


OVERVIEW: The breeders owned a permanent thoroughbred horse racing/sales facility and conducted horse sales. The breeders applied for and received a license to conduct intertrack wagering pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 550.61(8) (Supp. 1990), an earlier version of Fla. Stat. ch. 550.615(9), containing the same licensure criteria. The trial court found the statutory provisions created an impenetrable barrier to all intertrack wagering applicants except the breeders. The Florida Supreme Court agreed. The statute was unconstitutional as a special law enacted under the guise of a general law in violation of Fla. Const. art. III, § 10. Fla. Stat. ch. 550.615 was enacted to increase revenues at pari-mutuel wagering facilities by providing protection to thoroughbred horse breeders from the state policy against off-track betting, but no rational relationship existed between this purpose and the detailed licensure criteria in the disputed statute. Curiously, the breeders were the only business entity that had ever obtained a nonwagering thoroughbred racing permit. Fla. Stat. ch. 550.615 violated the equal protection rights of other potential licensees.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

Farina v. State


No. SC93050


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


801 So. 2d 44; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1579; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 527



August 16, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Denied November 29, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2280. As Revised on Denial of Rehearing November 29, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Farina v. Florida, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4316 (U.S. June 10, 2002).
Rehearing denied by Farina v. State, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2280 (Fla., Nov. 29, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Farina v. Florida, 536 U.S. 910, 122 S. Ct. 2369, 153 L. Ed. 2d 189, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4316 (June 10, 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Farina v. State, 937 So. 2d 612, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1482 (Fla., July 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, C. McFerrin Smith, III, Judge - Case No. 92-32105CFAES.
Farina v. State, 763 So. 2d 302, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1439 (Fla., July 13, 2000)
Farina v. State, 679 So. 2d 1151, 1996 Fla. LEXIS 671 (Fla., Apr. 18, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Anthony Farina's sentence of death affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Florida, convicted defendant and his brother of first-degree murder while robbing a fast food restaurant. The supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction, but vacated his death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding due to error in the jury selection process. On remand, a jury recommended the death penalty. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his co-defendant brother were convicted of murder, but his brother's sentence of death was vacated because he was only 16 years of age. Defendant then contested the appropriateness of his death sentence. The supreme court found that the victim impact evidence was properly admitted. In addition, the supreme court determined that the record supported the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator because victim's hands were tied behind her back and she was conscious as two of her co-workers were shot. Furthermore, the supreme court found that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated without any pretense of moral or legal justification. Additionally, the facts supported the avoid arrest aggravator because defendant knew that he was likely to be recognized by some of the employees; defendant was armed with a gun, knife, and rope, and wore gloves during the crime; defendant and co-defendant discussed the need to eliminate witnesses; and then defendant consecutively shot the victims execution style. Also, the supreme court determined that defendant was a major participant in an armed robbery. Finally, the death sentence was upheld in similar cases.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment sentencing defendant to death.

Mann v. Moore


No. SC00-2602


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


794 So. 2d 595; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1405; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 490



July 12, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 2001. Released for Publication September 5, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Mann v. Moore, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4989 (U.S. June 28, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Mann v. Moore, 536 U.S. 962, 122 S. Ct. 2669, 153 L. Ed. 2d 843, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 4989 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Mann v. Moore, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 24475 (M.D. Fla., Apr. 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mann v. State, 770 So. 2d 1158, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1898 (Fla., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that Fla. R. App. P. 9.140(b)(6)(E) operated to bar the defendant's petition. There was sufficient confusion procedurally that to bar a habeas petition relying upon Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851(b)(2) continuing to apply to death-row prisoners convicted and sentenced before January 1, 1994, would be unjust. Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(1) (1979) made clear that the maximum penalty available for a person convicted of a capital felony was death. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for not raising on appeal an issue with little or no merit. The defendant's claim regarding the unobjected to prosecutorial comments was procedurally barred, because they were raised in his initial brief denying his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion. The defendant's argument over the prosecutorial comments were barred and did not demonstrate a deficiency in counsel's performance that prejudiced him. The defendant's arguments over the prosecutor's discussions of the defendant's sexual behavior were procedurally barred because they were a variant to arguments already made. The defendant's competency to be executed claim was not yet ripe and was without merit.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

754 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Keshbro, Inc. v. City of Miami


No. SC94058. No. SC95600 (Two Cases Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


801 So. 2d 864; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1409; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 469



July 12, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Case No. SC94058 Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction Third - Case No. 3D98-1151 (Dade County) Case No. SC95600 Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict Second District - Case No. 2D98-01850 (Pinellas County).



DISPOSITION: Based on the foregoing, we approve the decisions reached in Keshbro and Kablinger.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In separate cases, petitioner motel and respondent apartment sued respondent first city and petitioner second city for inverse condemnation. The trial courts granted summary judgment to the motel and apartment, and the cities appealed. The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) reversed the first trial court's judgment; the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the second court's judgment. The motel and the second city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The cities ordered a motel and an apartment to close temporarily under the cities' nuisance ordinances, due to illegal activities occurring there. The motel and apartment sued the cities for compensation for losses caused by the closures, and both were granted summary judgment. The first intermediate appellate court reversed; the second affirmed. The motel and the second city appealed, and the cases were consolidated, The instant court held that, as the temporary closures rendered the properties economically idle, the cases were to be analyzed under Lucas. Lucas's "nuisance exception", under which a regulation that eliminated the value of property was not a taking if the purpose of the regulation was to control a public nuisance, applied to the motel but not to the apartment. The motel was the scene of numerous drug- and prostitution-related arrests, and the first city acted reasonably in ordering its temporary closure. No compensation was due the motel. But there was no such record of illegal activity at the apartment, and so closing it for one year was not specifically tailored to abate the drug nuisance, making its closure a compensable taking.


OUTCOME: The judgments were approved.

Slawson v. State


No. SC90045


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


796 So. 2d 491; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1356; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 455



July 5, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Diana Allen, Judge - Case No. 89-05619 Div. C.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the circuit court's order finding Slawson competent to make a knowing, intelligent, and voluntary waiver of collateral counsel and collateral proceedings. We further affirm the circuit court's order discharging CCRC-M from representing Slawson, and we dismiss with prejudice the appeal currently pending in this Court from the summary denial of Slawson's initial rule 3.850 motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of first-degree premeditated murder and one count of manslaughter, and received four death sentences. The Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, Florida, found defendant competent to waive collateral counsel and collateral proceedings, and discharged . On behalf of defendant, his collateral counsel sought review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered a pregnant woman, her husband, and two children, and cut the fetus from her womb, causing its death. His collateral counsel filed two motions for postconviction relief, and appealed from their denial. Defendant then filed pro se motions asking the instant court to relinquish jurisdiction and the trial court to discharge his collateral counsel and dismiss the appeals. The trial court, after a hearing, found defendant to be competent to waive collateral counsel and proceedings. The instant court remanded so that defendant could undergo a mental health evaluation. The trial court appointed three mental health professionals to evaluate him; in their reports, two opined that defendant was competent, the third opined that he was not. The trial court again found defendant to be competent, but again the instant court remanded, ordering a hearing in which the experts would testify in person. At this hearing, all three testified that defendant was competent, and the trial court so ruled. The instant court approved this ruling. As defendant's competence had been established at an adversary hearing, the dismissal of collateral counsel and proceedings was proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the appeal from the summary denial of collateral counsel's motion for post-conviction relief was dismissed.

Jones v. Moore


No. SC00-660


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


794 So. 2d 579; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1362; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 459



July 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 5, 2001. Released for Publication September 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Jones v. State, 732 So. 2d 313, 1999 Fla. LEXIS 446 (Fla., 1999)



DISPOSITION: All relief in petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of and sentenced to death for first-degree murder. His conviction was affirmed on direct appeal. His subsequent postconviction relief motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 was denied, and the denial was affirmed. He then filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus challenging the legality of his conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not prejudiced by appellate counsel's failure to raise evidentiary objections overruled at trial. The trial court's rulings did not err, but if they did, admission of the evidence was harmless. Defendant's prison escape two weeks before the murder, during which he threatened a corrections officer, was admissible to show his state of mind. Photos of defendant were admitted because they showed him with guns similar to the murder weapons. Consideration of the denial of defendant's severance motions previously dealt with on appeal was barred. The denial of severance motions not considered on appeal did not abuse discretion. Appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise unpreserved claims objecting to the admission of autopsy photographs. Defendant showed no prejudice from appellate counsel's failure to raise the admission of autopsy photos objected to at trial. Defendant's unpreserved objections to prosecutorial comments did not raise fundamental error. Consideration of the advisory jury's instruction on sentencing aggravators found inapplicable was procedurally barred, as an attempt to use habeas to reargue the wisdom of the death sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's habeas corpus petition was denied.

Cook v. State


No. SC94134


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


792 So. 2d 1197; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1255; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 424



June 28, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Thomas M. Carney, Judge - Case No. 84-19874C.
Cook v. Florida, 502 U.S. 890, 112 S. Ct. 252, 116 L. Ed. 2d 206, 1991 U.S. LEXIS 5053 (1991)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of two counts of first-degree murder, two counts of attempted robbery, burglary, and unlawful possession of a firearm while engaged in a criminal offense. The Dade County Circuit Court (Florida) denied defendant's motion to vacate his convictions and death sentence, which was supplemented with a motion to compel production of public records from various agencies. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised 20 issues on appeal. Because the record did not conclusively refute his allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel at the penalty phase, the appellate court held that the trial court had to conduct an evidentiary hearing to determine if counsel failed to investigate defendant's family history and possible mental health mitigators, and whether there was a reasonable possibility that such failure, if any, affected the outcome of the penalty proceeding. The appellate court also found that during the Huff hearing, defendant's counsel did not mention that requested public records had not yet been received. Further, the state attorney stated he had no indication that any public records requests were outstanding and defendant's counsel did not offer any evidence to refute this claim, nor did she explicitly explain which records were outstanding and the purpose for which they were sought. Therefore, the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to compel production of public records was proper. Defendant's other claims were either procedurally barred, insufficiently pled, or meritless.


OUTCOME: The denial of postconviction relief was affirmed in all respects except ineffective assistance of counsel at penalty. On that issue, the case was reversed and remanded to the trial court to hold an evidentiary hearing.

Clark v. State


No. SC00-515


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


790 So. 2d 1030; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1259; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 421



June 28, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Second District - Case No. 2D98-4287. (Hardee County).



DISPOSITION: We approve the decision of the district court to the extent that it consistent with our decisions in Grant, McKnight, Cotton, and Ellis.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged his sentence from the District Court of Appeal, Hardee County, Florida, under the Prison Releasee Reoffender Act (Act) arguing that the Act was unconstitutionally vague, in that he was not put on notice of its effect for committing a crime while incarcerated.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced under the Prison Releasee Reoffender Act for an offense he committed three months after being released from prison. He challenged the constitutionality of the Act on vagueness grounds, which was rejected by the supreme court. His arguments were the same as those raised in four prior cases before the court, which upheld the Act as constitutional. The publication of the laws and statutes gave all citizens constructive notice of the consequences of their actions. The district court was correct in strictly construing the statute against petitioner, as he was included in the Act's coverage. Moreover, petitioner's related argument, that the legislature simply did not intend for incarcerated persons to be subject to sentencing under the Act, was similarly unavailing. Finally, the argument that the 1999 amendment nullified the 1997 version had no merit. The modification simply added the definition of prison releasee offenders, of which petitioner qualified.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court of appeal was affirmed.

Atwater v. State


No. SC94865, No. SC99-179


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


788 So. 2d 223; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1133; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 395



June 7, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Atwater v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 2446 (Fla., Dec. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Two Cases:

An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus. Raymond Gross, Judge - Case No. 89-13299-K CFANO.
Atwater v. State, 730 So. 2d 679, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 4793 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of 3.850 relief affirmed and habeas corpus relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated case, prisoner appellant under sentence of death sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Florida, which denied his motion for postconviction relief. He also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court denied prisoner's writ of habeas corpus finding that his claims were either improper, procedurally barred, or without merit. In light of the evidence against prisoner, defense counsel properly attempted to maintain credibility with the jury by being candid as to the weight of the evidence. Faced with the prospect of a guilty verdict for first-degree murder and in light of the State's evidence, defense counsel's concession was reasonable and did not amount to a constitutional violation. The concession was made to a lesser crime than charged, during rebuttal closing argument, and after a meaningful adversarial testing of the State's case; even if defense counsel had denied prisoner's guilt to any crime, there was no reasonable possibility the jury would have reached a different conclusion. Also, prisoner did not establish any prejudice caused by defense counsel's failure to present the requested mitigating evidence as fact, as opposed to the presentation of that evidence through physician testimony; there was no reasonable probability that re-presenting virtually the same evidence through other witnesses would have altered the outcome in any manner.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of postconviction relief was affirmed and habeas relief was denied.

Waterhouse v. State


No. SC95103


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


792 So. 2d 1176; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1107; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 375



May 31, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County,

Robert E. Beach, Judge - Case No. 80-192 CF.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the trial court's summary denial of all claims asserted in appellant's motion for postconviction relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder, and after six aggravators, of which four were affirmed, and no mitigators were found, was sentenced to death. The Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) summarily denied his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 postconviction relief motion. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Supreme Court held that several claims were procedurally barred because they should have been raised on direct appeal. As to his ineffective assistance of counsel claims, appellant failed to allege how he was prejudiced by failures to object or raise asserted error. Appellant himself, not his counsel, elected not to present mitigating evidence nor to meet with a mental health expert. Defense counsel fully utilized the trial court's considerable leeway in cross-examining state witnesses on sexual battery evidence. Admission of appellant's in-custody statements as to guilt were harmless in relation to the penalty phase. The prosecutor could properly argue that sympathy toward defendant was inappropriate. None of the lawyers who represented appellant throughout the years was ineffective in failing to seek the trial judge's recusal. The trial judge's comment to the parole commission did not constitute a prejudgment of any pending or future motions that appellant might have filed, and was not made outside the official post-sentence investigative process in a manner indicating predisposed bias against appellant.


OUTCOME: Summary denial of all claims asserted in appellant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed.

 

761 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bradford


No. SC96910


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


787 So. 2d 811; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1108; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 369; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 401



May 31, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Counsel Corrected June 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity.

Fourth District - Case No. 4D98-2480.

(Broward County).



DISPOSITION: The district court's decision quashed and the case remanded with directions that Bradford's conviction be reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent licensed chiropractor was prosecuted and convicted by petitioner state for unlawful insurance solicitation in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 817.234(8). The District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Broward County (Florida), expressly held the statute to be valid. Respondent sought review.


OVERVIEW: Respondent had a business relationship with a company engaged in scheduling appointments with chiropractors for persons involved in motor vehicle crashes. After obtaining a motor vehicle accident report, a company representative telephonically solicited persons listed on it to schedule an initial examination with respondent, and possible subsequent treatment, if necessary, for injuries arising from the crash. Respondent examined the solicited individuals, determined that treatment was necessary, and later billed their personal injury protection insurance carrier for services rendered. Petitioner acknowledged that respondent's conduct contained no element of fraud. The Florida Supreme Court held that because the legislature did not include fraudulent intent as an element of unlawful insurance solicitation, Fla. Stat. ch. 817.234(8) unconstitutionally infringed upon the protections afforded commercial speech by U.S. Const. amend. I. The statute was facially unambiguous and its legislative history showed fraud was not an element. The statute did not materially advance petitioner's goal of preventing insurance fraud, nor was such a blanket ban narrowly tailored to meet such a goal.


OUTCOME: The district court's decision was quashed and the case remanded with directions that respondent's conviction be reversed.
