Carter v. State


No. SC92501


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


786 So. 2d 1173; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 1067; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 347



May 24, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict Fifth District - Case No. 5D97-2235 (Orange County).



DISPOSITION: Quashed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal, Florida, which affirmed the trial court's denial of his motion for postconviction relief. The Fifth District reasoned that petitioner's improper habitualization was not illegal, and therefore, was not remediable under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) as long as the sentence was within the statutory maximum for the offense.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner received a 40-year sentence as a habitual offender for second-degree murder with a weapon. At the time petitioner committed his offense, the habitual offender statute in existence did not provide an enhanced habitual offender penalty for a defendant who committed a life felony. On review, the supreme court held that a habitual offender sentence was illegal where the habitual offender statute in effect at the time of the offense prohibited the imposition of a habitual offender sentence. Because petitioner received a habitual offender sentence when the existing law did not authorize the imposition of a habitual offender sentence, the supreme court ruled that his sentence was illegal for purposes of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.800(a) as a matter of law. It also referred the question of whether Rule 3.800(a) should have been amended to identify specifically those matters that were sufficiently important to be raised at any time to the Criminal Appeals Reform Act Committee and the Florida Bar Criminal Procedure Rules Committee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

763 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Moore


No. SC00-1599


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


792 So. 2d 447; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 962; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 316



May 10, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 29, 2001. Certiorari Denied February 19, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 765.



DISPOSITION: Habeas relief Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner was sentenced to death, and his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 was denied. Prisoner petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner argued that his appellate counsel was ineffective in failing to argue that: (1) he was mentally retarded and that his execution would be unconstitutional; (2) the circuit court's finding that he was the leader of the criminal acts committed by him and the codefendant was not supported by the evidence; (3) the detective's pretrial deposition testimony contradicted the trial judge's findings; and (4) it was error to use his assault conviction as an aggravating circumstance. The supreme court denied habeas relief because: (1) it was clear that the prisoner's mental capacity was a focal issue in the various proceedings, and it had already considered and rejected the issue; (2) counsel argued that there was no evidence that the prisoner encouraged the codefendant to kill the victim, and that there was no competent evidence supporting the finding that the prisoner goaded the codefendant into killing the victim; (3) the failure to present evidence at trial was not a claim concerning effectiveness of appellate counsel which was the sole subject of the petition; and (4) counsel could not be deemed ineffective for failing to raise a meritless issue on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied habeas relief.

Happ v. Moore


No. SC00-1198


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


784 So. 2d 1091; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 868; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 301



May 3, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Happ v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2508 (Fla., Dec. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Happ v. Florida, 510 U.S. 925, 114 S. Ct. 328, 126 L. Ed. 2d 274, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 6499 (1993)



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Happ's initial and supplemental petitions for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion for writ of habeas corpus in which he alleged ineffective assistance of appellate counsel stemming from an appeal from his convictions for first-degree murder, burglary of a conveyance with a battery therein, kidnapping, and sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted for first-degree murder, burglary of a conveyance, kidnapping, and sexual battery. On the murder charge he was sentenced to death. He filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, wherein he alleged multifarious grounds of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel, including failing to point out in the motion for rehearing that the court relied on inaccurate facts, and failing to argue the trial court erred by finding a witness unavailable to testify and by allowing his former testimony. The court held to establish ineffective assistance of appellate counsel, petitioner was required to show specific errors indicating counsel's performance fell outside the range of professionally acceptable performance, and the deficient performance compromised the appellate process so as to undermine confidence in the fairness and correctness of the appellate result. The court denied the petition, holding petitioner failed to meet his burden of proof as his appellate counsel could not be deemed ineffective for failing to raise unpreserved or non-meritorious issues on appeal and because the petition was improperly utilized to reargue facts previously decided.


OUTCOME: Petition denied, because appellate counsel could not be deemed ineffective for failing to raise unpreserved or non-meritorious issues on appeal, a writ of habeas corpus could not be used to reargue previously decided issues, and the balance of petitioner's claims were found baseless in fact.

T.M. v. State


No. SC00-1194


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


784 So. 2d 442; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 838; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 266



April 26, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case No. 2D98-3778. (Pinellas County).



DISPOSITION: Decision quashed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida District Court of Appeal certified two questions of great public importance regarding a juvenile curfew ordinance requesting the court to determine whether the level of scrutiny it applied in reviewing the constitutionality of the ordinance was appropriate, and whether the ordinance was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was cited for violating a juvenile curfew ordinance. He moved to dismiss the case, arguing the ordinance was unconstitutional because it infringed upon certain fundamental rights, was vague and overly broad, and was inconsistent with state law. The trial court granted the motion, finding parents had a fundamental right to raise their children without governmental intrusion and the ordinance was not narrowly tailored in the least restrictive manner to achieve a compelling governmental interest. The court of appeals reversed, finding the ordinance did not infringe on any fundamental rights of juveniles or parents and found the various exceptions to the ordinance sufficiently narrowed its scope to withstand heightened scrutiny. The court of appeals certified two questions of great public importance asking whether the level of scrutiny it applied in reviewing the constitutionality of the ordinance was appropriate, and whether the ordinance was constitutional. The court quashed the court of appeals decision and remanded, holding the court of appeals erred by employing a heightened standard of scrutiny rather than strict scrutiny review to the ordinance in question.


OUTCOME: Decision quashed, because the court of appeal applied a heightened standard of scrutiny rather than strict scrutiny review to the ordinance in question. Therefore, the matter was remanded to the court of appeals with instructions to apply a strict scrutiny analysis.

Mills v. State


No. SC01-775


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


786 So. 2d 547; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 844; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 275



April 25, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied May 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3517.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Seminole County, O. H. Eaton, Jr., Judge - Case No. 79-653CFB.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been sentenced to death, and for whom a death warrant had been signed, sought postconviction relief in the Circuit Court, Seminole County (Florida), under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The trial court denied the relief requested, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged codefendant testified falsely and lacked credibility, rendering the trial judge's override of the jury's life recommendation error. A claim for relief based on newly discovered evidence had to show the evidence would probably result in a life sentence. This version of codefendant's story did not exonerate defendant and only put the codefendant's credibility into doubt, as had already been done at trial. Defendant claimed a person guilty of felony murder was more likely than a person guilty of premeditated murder to receive a death sentence because felony murder automatically established an aggravating factor of murder in the course of another dangerous felony. This claim had been repeatedly denied and was procedurally barred. Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.852(h)(3), as well as Fla. Stat. ch. 119.19 (2000), provided for production of public records after the governor signed a death warrant. The rule was intended to provide for an update of information previously received or requested and not an eleventh hour attempt to delay execution. Defendant's demands were overly broad, of questionable relevance, and unlikely to lead to discoverable evidence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief was affirmed because his "new evidence" was not likely to result in a life sentence, his claim of the automatic imposition of an aggravating circumstance had previously been ruled on, and his records request was of questionable relevance.

 

768 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. Moore


No. SC95299


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


786 So. 2d 521; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 736; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 229



April 12, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 16, 2001.



DISPOSITION: The instant petition for writ of mandamus granted and the First District Court of Appeal instructed to reinstate petitioner's appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida Supreme Court considered petitioner's application for a writ of mandamus in which he sought to compel the appellate court to reinstate his appeal after the appellate court dismissed it because petitioner had neither filed a large number of papers related to his case nor paid the $ 250 filing fee required under the Prisoner Indigency Statute, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 57.085 (1999).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was instructed by the appellate court to pay a $ 250 filing fee or obtain an order determining him indigent, for appellate purposes, from the lower court in order for the denial of his mandamus petition to be heard. Petitioner filed an affidavit of insolvency, but the appellate court first dismissed his appeal. The trial court soon denied petitioner's request for indigency for failing to submit copies of numerous pleadings he had filed in last five years as required by the Prisoner Indigency Statute, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 57.085 (1999)(Statute). Petitioner argued in his mandamus petition filed with the state supreme court that the Statute violated his constitutional right of access to the courts. The state supreme court agreed because it found the copy requirement compelled an otherwise indigent prisoner to provide copies of numerous pleadings obtainable only through great difficulty, delay, and expense, and provided no meaningful alternative. The state supreme court then declared that the copy requirement would not apply to any inmate who sought to have his case reinstated where the case was dismissed for failure to comply with it.


OUTCOME: Application for writ of mandamus granted and appellate court instructed to reinstate appeal because the copy requirement of the Prisoner Indigency Statute violated petitioner's constitutional right of access to the courts. The statute significantly obstructed his ability to have his case heard without providing numerous pleadings obtainable only through great difficulty, delay, and public expense, and provided no meaningful alternative.

State v. Rife


No. SC95752


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


789 So. 2d 288; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 740; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 226



April 12, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case No. 5D98-38 (Brevard County).



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered in the affirmative and approve the decision of the Fifth District.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State sought review of the decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal, Florida, which certified to be of great public importance the questions of whether: (1) willingness or consent of a minor could be considered as a mitigating factor in sentencing; and (2) whether the mitigation should also apply where defendant was in a position of custodial or familial authority with the victim.


OVERVIEW: Respondent admitted to having sex with the 17-year-old victim but contended, and the victim agreed, that it was consensual. Sexual activities began before respondent became her guardian. Respondent was convicted of sexual battery and a downward departure sentence was imposed upon the finding that victim consented. The State appealed the imposition of the downward departure sentences; the appellate court affirmed and certified two questions to be of great public importance. On review, the supreme court found that the record supported the presence of consent as a mitigating factor and further held that the legislature did not intend to preclude a trial court from utilizing Fla. Stat. ch. 921.0016(4)(f) as a basis for imposing a downward departure sentence. The supreme court affirmed the certified questions and concluded that trial judges were not prohibited as a matter of law from imposing a downward departure based on a finding that the victim was an initiator, willing participant, aggressor, or provoker of the incident.


OUTCOME: The certified questions were answered in the affirmative and the appeals court decision was approved.

Sebring Airport Auth. v. McIntyre


Case Nos. SC94118 & SC94105


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


783 So. 2d 238; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 629; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 197



April 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Second District - Case No. 2D97-02707.



DISPOSITION: Decision affirmed and Second District's opinion approved only to extent consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated case, appellants sought review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Florida, which declared unconstitutional a portion of Fla. Stat. ch. 196.012(6) (Supp. 1994). The invalidated provision would have created an ad valorem tax exemption for certain private enterprises by statutorily defining these types of activities as serving a governmental, municipal, or public purpose or function.


OVERVIEW: On review, the appellate court found that the operation of the commercial enterprises were purely proprietary, for profit, and not governmental functions. The exemptions contemplated in the legislation at issue related to "governmental-governmental" functions as opposed to "governmental-proprietary" functions; legislatively deeming a governmental-proprietary purpose to be a "governmental-governmental" purpose did not change its true nature and did not result in the constitutional awarding of a tax exemption where, absent the legislation, there clearly could be no exemption. Neither the instant court, nor the legislature could grant ad valorem taxation exemptions not provided for in the constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Doe v. Am. Online, Inc.


No. SC94355


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


783 So. 2d 1010; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 449; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 141



March 8, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 2001. Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6591.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 4D97-2587 (Palm Beach County).



DISPOSITION: Answered in the affirmative the first certified question and the rephrased question, which combines the second and third certified questions, and approved the decision of the Fourth District below.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother brought suit against respondent Internet service provider, alleging various tort claims. The trial court granted respondent's motion to dismiss with prejudice, finding that the immunity Congress provided for interactive computer services in 47 U.S.C.S. § 230 applied to petitoner's claims. The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed and certified questions involving the preemption of state tort law by federal law.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed her son, who was 11 years-old, and two other minor males were lured to engage in sexual activity. She asserted that a person photographed and videotaped these acts and used respondent's chat rooms to market the photographs and videotapes. The supreme court first addressed whether 47 U.S.C.S. § 230 preempted Florida law as to causes of action based in negligence against an Internet service provider (ISP) as a distributor of information allegedly in violation of Florida criminal statutes prohibiting the distribution of obscene literature and computer pornography. The fundamental issue was whether companies that provided access to the Internet were subject to common-law civil tort causes of action based upon the laws of each of the 50 states, or whether Congress acted to make ISPs immune from such common-law civil actions. The supreme court specifically concurred that 47 U.S.C.S. § 230 expressly barred any actions and the supreme court was compelled to give the language of this preemptive law its plain meaning.


OUTCOME: The supreme court answered in the affirmative the first certified question and the rephrased question, which combined the second and third certified questions, and approved the decision of the appellate court below. Petitioner's cause of action against respondent was barred by the plain language of the federal statute.

Natural Parents of J.B. v. Fla. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


No. SC96171


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


780 So. 2d 6; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 333; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 86



February 22, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 4D98-2255. (Broward County).



DISPOSITION: Decision approved and certified question answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida Fourth District Court of Appeal, having quashed a trial court order which found that the statutory requirement that courts be closed in termination of parental rights (TPR) proceedings was unconstitutional, certified the question whether Fla. Stat. 39.467(4) (1997) (now Fla. Stat. Ann. § 39.809(4) (2000)) which required mandatory closure of all hearings in TPR proceedings, was valid under the United States and Florida constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a dependency action alleging that petitioners' daughter was made ill and required numerous hospitalizations as a result of petitioner mother's Munchausen-by-Proxy syndrome. The court denied petitioners' motion to close the dependency hearing. The State later moved to terminate petitioners' parental rights (TPR). The trial court declared that the Fla. Stat. 39.467(4) (1997) (now Fla. Stat. Ann. § 39.809(4) (2000)) requirement that the TPR proceeding be closed to the public was unconstitutional. The district court quashed the trial court's order and certified the question of the constitutionality of the statutory closed-court requirement. The supreme court held the legislature had validly declared that public policy required the mandatory closure of TPR proceedings. Because no presumption of openness in juvenile proceedings was constitutionally required, there was no requirement that an order of closure be made only after a case-by-case determination. Petitioners failed to overcome the presumption in favor of the validity of the statute and failed to demonstrate that the statute unconstitutionally usurped the public's right of access to TPR proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the affirmative and approved the decision of the district court, finding that the statute which required that all hearings involving termination of parental rights be confidential and closed to the public, was valid under the United States and Florida constitutional provisions respecting access of the public and media to judicial proceedings.

Crocker v. Pleasant


No. SC95148


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


778 So. 2d 978; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 151; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 61



February 1, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 4D98-0633. (Palm Beach County).



DISPOSITION: Fourth District's decision quashed and case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida Fourth District Court of Appeals affirmed a trial court decision which held that appellants were precluded from bring a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against appellees for violating their due process rights by burying their son without notifying them. However, it certified a question to the instant court to determine whether a previous decision of the court did indeed preclude appellant's § 1983 action.


OVERVIEW: Appellants' 23 year-old son was found dead. An officer, employed by appellee city, identified and located, but never communicated with, appellants. Two months after his death, decedent was buried by appellee county. When appellants later learned that their son had been buried, they filed an action against appellees, alleging that the failure to notify them of their son's death was a violation of their due process rights. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to appellees. The court of appeals affirmed, but certified the question whether a previous decision of the court had precluded all 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims grounded on interference with an interest in a dead body. The supreme court answered in the negative. The court first determined that appellants had a substantive right to possession of their son's remains for burial. It then held that its previous opinion about the constitutionality of a cornea removal statute, was not inconsistent with recognition of a limited substantive right to a loved one's remains. Finally it concluded that appellants' substantive right was legitimate claim of entitlement entitled to procedural due process under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative and quashed the decision of the court of appeals, holding that appellants had a legitimate claim of entitlement to procedural due process in connection with burial of their son and noting that on remand appellant's action would require them to prove a level of misconduct which constituted a constitutional deprivation of their procedural rights.

Muhammad v. State


No. SC90030


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


782 So. 2d 343; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 39; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 37



January 18, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised April 5, 2001. Rehearing Denied April 5, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Fla. LEXIS 625.
Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5801.
Rehearing denied by Muhammad v. State, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 625 (Fla., Apr. 5, 2001)
Writ of certiorari denied, Motion granted by Florida v. Muhammad, 534 U.S. 944, 122 S. Ct. 323, 151 L. Ed. 2d 241, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 7350 (2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Muhammad v. Florida, 534 U.S. 836, 122 S. Ct. 87, 151 L. Ed. 2d 49, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5801 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Muhammad v. McNeil, 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 24685 (11th Cir. Fla., Nov. 10, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Richard D. Eade, Judge - Case No. 95-12739 CF10a.



DISPOSITION: Conviction upheld. Death penalty vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Broward County (Florida), which, following a jury trial, convicted the appellant guilty of first-degree murder and imposed a death penalty sentence on the appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to death for first-degree murder. Appellant requested a waiver of sentencing proceedings before a jury, which the trial court denied. At the sentencing proceeding, appellant did not present mitigating evidence. As a result, the jury heard only the appellee State's evidence and argument as to why the death penalty should have been imposed. On appeal, the appellant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in failing to consider mitigating evidence present in the record and in denying appellant's request for a waiver of jury sentencing proceedings. The court upheld appellant's conviction, but vacated the death penalty and remanded for new sentencing. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to honor the appellant's waiver. However, the court held that reversible error occurred due to the trial court's decision to afford great weight to the advisory jury's recommendation in imposing the death penalty when that jury did not hear any evidence in mitigation. Notwithstanding the jury's recommendation, the trial court was required to make an independent determination, based on the aggravating and mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: Appellant's sentence was vacated. Reversible error occurred due to the trial court's decision to afford great weight to the jury's recommendation when that jury did not hear any evidence in mitigation and the defendant had, in fact, requested waiver of the advisory jury. Accordingly, the court vacated the sentence of death and remanded for resentencing proceedings before the trial court.

Valle v. State


No. SC94754


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


778 So. 2d 960; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 44; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 46



January 18, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Richard Margolius, Judge - Case No. 78-5281 A.



DISPOSITION: Denial of postconviction relief affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County Florida, which denied his petition for postconviction relief after an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of first-degree murder, attempted murder, and possession of a firearm, was sentenced to death for murder. On direct appeal, the court reversed the convictions and sentences, remanding for new trial. On retrial, appellant was again convicted and again sentenced to death. The convictions and sentences were affirmed by the court. The United States Supreme Court subsequently vacated appellant's death sentence, remanding the case to the court for further consideration regarding admissibility of model prisoner testimony. The court remanded for sentencing hearing before a new jury. On resentencing, the jury recommended death. After the court affirmed the death sentence, appellant petitioned for postconviction relief, which the trial court summarily denied. The trial court also denied appellant's second postconviction motion, without an evidentiary hearing. The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing on two claims. The trial court denied the claims and appellant challenged. The court affirmed the trial court.


OUTCOME: Denial of postconviction relief was affirmed. The trial court's final order was supported by the testimony presented at the evidentiary hearing. Accordingly, the court found no due process violation and no reversible error as a result of the trial court's adoption of a substantial portion of the State's proposed order.

 

778 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Glock v. Moore


Nos. SC00-2432 & SC00-2535


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


776 So. 2d 243; 2001 Fla. LEXIS 5; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 9



January 5, 2001, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases: An Original Proceeding - Writ of Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Wayne L. Cobb, Judge - Case No. 83-1383 CFAES.



DISPOSITION: Denial of Glock's motion for postconviction relief affirmed and Glock's petition for habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida) and brought a writ of habeas corpus challenging the trial court's order summarily denying his successive motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of first-degree murder, kidnapping, and robbery and was sentenced to death. He claimed newly discovered evidence had arisen, bearing directly on the denial of his motion to suppress, which arose from the circumstance of defendant being stopped on the New Jersey turnpike while driving the murder victim's stolen car. Defendant asserted that the stop was illegal because it was predicated on impermissible racial or drug profiling. The court held defendant offered nothing that would challenge the his validly stopped vehicle 17 years earlier. Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.851(b)(4) was not intended for use by defendants as an 11th hour attempt to delay an execution rather than a focused investigation into some legitimate area of inquiry. Defendant did not show good cause as to why he did not make public records requests until after the death warrant was signed. His death sentence was not applied in an arbitrary and capricious manner, and he was executed on January 11, 2001.


OUTCOME: Order denying postconviction relief affirmed. Impermissible racial or drug profiling would not have resulted in suppression of evidence based on an unlawful stop 17 years earlier. No abuse of discretion in denying motions to compel and in determining defendant's right to public records was not denied. Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied. Death sentence was not applied in arbitrary and capricious manner, and defendant was executed.

 

779 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Gore v. Harris


No. SC00-2431


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


773 So. 2d 524; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2474; 26 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



December 22, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court, in and for Leon County, N. Sanders Sauls, Judge, Case No. CV 00-2808. Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D00-4745.



DISPOSITION: Appellants afforded no relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a contest to results of the 2000 presidential election in Florida, the United States Supreme Court reversed and remanded a Florida Supreme Court decision that had ordered a manual recount of certain ballots.


OVERVIEW: The state supreme court had ordered the trial court to conduct a manual recount of 9000 contested Miami-Dade County ballots, and also held that uncounted "undervotes" in all Florida counties were to be manually counted. The trial court was ordered to use the standard that a vote was "legal" if there was a clear indication of the intent of the voter, Fla. Stat. ch. 101.5614(5) (2000). The United States Supreme Court released an opinion on December 12, 2000, which held that such a standard violated equal protection rights because it lacked specific standards to ensure equal application, and also mandated that any manual recount would have to have been completed by December 12, 2000. On remand, the state supreme court found that it was impossible under that time frame to adopt adequate standards and make necessary evaluations of vote tabulation equipment. Also, development of a specific, uniform standard for manual recounts was best left to the legislature.


OUTCOME: Because adequate standards for a manual recount could not be developed by the deadline set by the United States Supreme Court, appellants were afforded no relief.

State v. Miles


No. SC95490


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


775 So. 2d 950; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2322; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 1082



November 30, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance.

First District - Case No. 1D97-3606.

(Escambia County).



DISPOSITION: Decision of the First District quashed in part and approved in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Florida First District Court of Appeals certified a question regarding whether the State was entitled to the presumption of impairment when it laid the three-prong predicate for admissibility of blood-alcohol test results, establishing the scientific reliability of the blood-alcohol test results, in a matter related to charges of driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in an automobile accident which resulted in the death of a passenger of another vehicle. Without defendant's consent, the law enforcement officers required him to submit to a blood draw pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 316.1933 (1995). He was charged with driving under the influence of alcohol/manslaughter (DUI/manslaughter) and other related charges. Defendant filed a motion to suppress or in the alternative a motion in limine to exclude the blood alcohol test results. The following question was presented: Where the State lays a three-pronged predicate for admissibility of blood-alcohol test results, establishing scientific reliability, was the State entitled to presumptions of impairment? Testing did not occur until some 14 days after the blood draw, which could have impacted the integrity of the blood sample. The absence of maintenance standards rendered Fla. Admin. Code Ann. R. 11D-8.012.11D-8.012(3) inadequate and inconsistent with the purpose of the implied consent law as it related to ensuring the reliability of test results. The State was not entitled to the presumptions of impairment associated with the implied consent statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court was quashed in part and approve it in part, and remanded for proceedings consistent with the opinion. State was not entitled to presumptions associated with the implied consent statutory scheme.

Drew v. State


No. SC95785


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


773 So. 2d 46; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2167; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 1029



November 9, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions

Second District - Case No. 2D98-00877

(Polk County).



DISPOSITION: Quashed the decision in Drew and approved the decision in Hankins; remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon application for review from the Florida Second District Court of Appeal, the court addressed conflicting decisions on the issue of whether the act of removing hubcaps or tires from a vehicle in and of itself constitutes a burglary.


OVERVIEW: In determining whether the act of removing hubcaps or tires from a vehicle in and of itself constitutes a burglary the Florida Second District Court of Appeal (Second District) held that there was a burglary and the Florida Fifth District Court of Appeal (Fifth District) held there was not. Upon the application for review from the Second District, the court addressed conflict and quashed the decision of the Second District and approved the decision of the Fifth District. Based on the purpose and history of the offense of burglary at common law and the court's interpretation of the burglary statute which required an entering of a conveyance with the intent to commit an offense therein, the sole act of removal of hubcaps or tires from a motor vehicle, while clearly constituting an act of criminal larceny, did not constitute a burglary.


OUTCOME: The court quashed one of the conflicting decisions and approved the other finding that based on the purpose and history of the offense of burglary at common law and the court's interpretation of the burglary statute, the sole act of removal of hubcaps or tires from a motor vehicle, while clearly constituting an act of criminal larceny, did not constitute a burglary.

 

783 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gaines


No. SC95738


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


770 So. 2d 1221; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2129; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 987



November 2, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected December 21, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity.

Fourth District. - Case No. 4D98-2789.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following dismissal of the case brought against defendant for possession of cocaine with intent to sell, the State appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), denying its motion for a rehearing from a rejection of its appeal, concluding that Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07(1)(l) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: During defendant's trial on a charge of possession of cocaine with intent to sell, the trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress. The case was subsequently dismissed and the State appealed the dismissal, contending that the trial court erred in suppressing the evidence. The trial court rejected the State's appeal on double jeopardy grounds and the State filed a petition for a rehearing, citing Fla. Stat. ch. 924.07(1)(l) as independent statutory authority for the appeal. The trial court then denied the State's motion for a rehearing, concluding that ch. 924.07(1)(l) was violative of the Florida Constitution. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court alone had the power to define the scope of interlocutory appeals, such that ch. 924.07(1)(l) was unconstitutional to the extent that it provided the State with the right to an interlocutory appeal not provided by court rule. Also, Fla. R. App. P. 3.190(h)(4) granted the trial court discretionary authority to entertain defendant's motion to suppress made during trial.


OUTCOME: Appellate court's decision was affirmed. To the extent that the relevant statutory provision provided the State with a right to an interlocutory appeal not provided by court rule, such provision violated the Florida Constitution.

 

784 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Grant v. State


No. SC99-164


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


770 So. 2d 655; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2128; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 990



November 2, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict

Second District - Case No. 2D98-04943 (Pinellas County).
Grant v. State, 745 So. 2d 519, 1999 Fla. App. LEXIS 15606 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 2d Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Decision of Second District approved. Portion of decision quashed. Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his concurrent 15-year sentences received as a habitual felony offender pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 and a prison releasee reoffender pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(8) following his conviction of sexual battery in the Fourth District Court (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's conviction pursuant to his guilty plea to a charge of sexual battery, defendant received concurrent 15 year sentences as a habitual felony offender pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 (1997) and a prison releasee reoffender (PRR) pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.082(8) (1997), the Prison Releasee Reoffenders Act. Defendant appealed his sentences, contending that the two sentences imposed upon him for a single offense violated double jeopardy and that the PRR classification in the Act violated equal protection. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The imposition of an applicable longer, concurrent term of imprisonment with a PRR mandatory minimum sentence did not violate double jeopardy. However, the imposition of two concurrent equal sentences was error because such sentencing was not authorized by the Act. The Act did not violate equal protection principles, was not an ex post facto law, and did not apply only to prisoners released after its effective date.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences were affirmed in part and reversed in part. The statutory provision providing for sentencing of prison releasee reoffenders (PRR) did not allow the trial court to sentence defendant to concurrent equal sentences as a PRR and habitual felony offender. The statute did not violate equal protection or double jeopardy prohibition and was not an ex post facto law. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Arbelaez v. State


No. SC89375


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


775 So. 2d 909; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2035; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 976



October 19, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Leslie Rothenberg, Judge - Case No. 88-5546.

Revised Opinion of July 13, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1450.
Arbelaez v. State, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1450 (Fla., July 13, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Appeal remanded to the trial court with instruction to conduct an evidentiary hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) summarily denying him relief on his motion for postconviction relief from his convictions for first-degree murder and kidnapping and from his death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner appealed the trial court's order summarily denying him relief on his motion for postconviction relief from his convictions for first-degree murder and kidnapping and from his death sentence. Petitioner claimed that he had received ineffective assistance of trial counsel during both the penalty phase and the guilt phase of the trial proceedings and that the trial judge erred in denying his motion to disqualify her. The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing on petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase of the trial proceedings and otherwise affirmed the trial court. Petitioner had stated sufficient allegations of mitigation to warrant an evidentiary hearing to determine whether counsel was ineffective for failing to properly investigate and present such evidence of mitigation. The trial court properly denied the other claims of ineffective assistance of counsel without evidentiary hearings as to those claims. Petitioner had not stated legally sufficient grounds to disqualify the trial judge. Neither the trial judge's "tough-on-crime" stance nor her former employment as a prosecutor was legally sufficient for disqualification.


OUTCOME: Court remanded for an evidentiary hearing on petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel during the penalty phase of the trial proceedings, and otherwise affirmed the trial court. Neither the trial judge's "tough-on-crime" stance nor her former employment as a prosecutor was legally sufficient to disqualify her from petitioner's trial.

Chi. Title Ins. Co. v. Butler


No. SC95312


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


770 So. 2d 1210; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 2034; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 899



October 19, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 6, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal of Judgment of Circuit Court, in and for Leon County, Terry P. Lewis, Judge, Case No. 94-1428 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 1D99-938.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certification from the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), appellants challenged the ruling of the Leon County Circuit Court, which declared several anti-rebate statutes regarding the premiums to be negotiated between title insurance agents and consumers in violation of Fla. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a builder and developer, challenged the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. chs. 626.611(11), 626.8437, 626.9541(1)(h)(3.a)., 627.780, 627.782, and 627.783 (1997), and Fla. Admin. Code Ann. r. 4-186.003(13)(a), which prohibited title insurance agents from negotiating or rebating to their clients any portion of the risk premium charged by title insurers for the issuance of title insurance. Appellee sought the right to negotiate the agent's share of the risk premium only. The trial court ruled that the statutes were unconstitutional. Accepting certification of the question, the court affirmed, holding that to the extent the provisions violated the due process requirements of Fla. Const. art. I, § 9. While the legislature had an interest in protecting title insurers and agents against insolvency and insuring quality of services, it could not impose regulations in a manner that harmed the public and violated a citizen's property rights to freely negotiate the cost of services from a provider.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order declaring the statutes unconstitutional was affirmed. Appellants did not explain how a blanket prohibition against title insurance agents' negotiating their portion of the risk premium with their customers promoted a public interest. The statutes violated the right to freely negotiate the cost of services.

Sexton v. State


No. SC94487


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


775 So. 2d 923; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1993; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 818



October 12, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 15, 2001.
Post-conviction relief denied at Sexton v. State, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1610 (Fla., Sept. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, J. Rodgers Padgett, Judge - Case No. 94-1299-B.
Sexton v. State, 697 So. 2d 833, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1058 (Fla., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), finding him guilty of first-degree murder of his son-in-law and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's mentally challenged son killed victim, appellant's son-in-law, upon appellant's orders and because he was afraid of his father. Upon retrial, appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The testimony regarding the killing of victim's son, a collateral bad act, was relevant to explain appellant's motive for having victim killed and the total domination appellant exerted over his family; thus, it was admissible. Defense counsel did not object when the witnesses read their prepared statements providing victim impact testimony. The failure to contemporaneously object to a comment because it constituted improper victim testimony rendered the claim procedurally barred absent fundamental error. Because the jury was already aware of the child's death, the victim testimony was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Appellant's death sentence was proportionate to other cases where "masterminds" were sentenced to death, even though they did not actually commit the murder. Thus, conviction and death sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; testimony regarding killing of victim's son was admissible collateral bad acts evidence because it was relevant to explain appellant's motive for having victim killed and his domination over his family. Appellant was the "mastermind" and his death sentence was proportionate, even though he did not actually commit the murder.

Rutherford v. Moore


No. SC99-150


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


774 So. 2d 637; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1994; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 891



October 12, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 21, 2000. Released for Publication December 21, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rutherford v. State, 727 So. 2d 216, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 2423 (Fla., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Habeas relief denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus in connection with his conviction for murder and armed robbery and the subsequent death sentence that he received, contending that he had received ineffective assistance of appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus in connection with his conviction for murder and armed robbery and the subsequent death sentence that he received. Petitioner claimed that he had received ineffective assistance of appellate counsel when his counsel failed to raise on appeal the denial of numerous pretrial motions and the use of various jury instructions, failed to raise on appeal the improper admission of gruesome photographs, and failed to argue on appeal that error occurred when the trial court failed to file the written sentencing order until eight days after the sentence was imposed. The court denied habeas relief. The underlying issues raised by petitioner were without merit, such that appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise those issues on appeal. The admission of the photographs did not constitute an abuse of discretion on the part of the trial court because the photographs were relevant to show the circumstances of the crime and the nature and extent of the victim's injuries. The short lapse prior to the filing of the sentencing order also was not erroneous.


OUTCOME: Habeas relief was denied. The underlying issues raised by petitioner were without merit, such that petitioner's appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to raise those issues on appeal.

CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW: Several witnesses saw appellant standing over victim and saw him hurl a concrete block down on victim's head five or six times. Two acquaintances picked up appellant hitchhiking. Appellant told the acquaintances that he had killed victim. Appellant was convicted and sentenced to death for first-degree murder. Holland v. State


No. SC89922


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


773 So. 2d 1065; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1979; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 796



October 5, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5776.
Writ of certiorari denied Holland v. Florida, 534 U.S. 834, 122 S. Ct. 83, 151 L. Ed. 2d 46, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 5776 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Holland v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 2208 (Fla., Nov. 10, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Charles M. Greene, Judge - Case No. 90-15905 CF10A.
Florida v. Holland, 513 U.S. 943, 115 S. Ct. 351, 130 L. Ed. 2d 306, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 7324 (1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which convicted him for murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The trial court imposed the death penalty upon appellant's conviction of murder. He raised several points of error on appeal. Rejecting his contentions, the court affirmed. Applying the Gentry test, the trial court did not err in refusing to grant appellant's request for a voluntary intoxication instruction. Attempted sexual battery in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(1)(h) was deemed a general intent crime, and the voluntary intoxication instruction was only applicable to specific intent crimes. The trial court's error in admitting inaudible portions of a videotape was harmless. A detective properly testified regarding what appellant said during the interrogation. The trial court's sentencing order contained a thorough evaluation of the aggravating and mitigating factors; therefore, imposition of the death penalty was proper.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed; appellant was not entitled to an instruction on voluntary intoxication as a defense, erroneously admitted videotape was harmless, and the trial court properly considered the aggravating and mitigating factors in imposing the death penalty.

 

793 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Belair v. Drew


No. SC96168


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


770 So. 2d 1164; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1980; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 741



October 5, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict. Fifth District - Case No.5D99-1265. (Brevard County).



DISPOSITION: Decision below quashed. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified conflict with Williams, which held that certiorari review should be granted where a party's constitutional rights may be abridged by the continuance of the proceedings below and, therefore, such abridgement could not be remedied on final appeal, in action challenging constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(b) (1997).


OVERVIEW: Respondent paternal grandmother of minor child petitioned the trial court for visitation under Fla. Stat. ch. 752.01(1)(b) (1997). Petitioner sought a trial court ruling that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated her right to privacy. However, the trial court refused to rule on the constitutional challenge and granted respondent temporary visitation. Petitioner then petitioned the appellate court for writ of certiorari, which the appellate court denied on the ground that intrusion into the trial court process was not shown to be warranted. The court concluded the appellate court erred in denying certiorari review, reasoning that the trial court's ruling, on its face, directly contravened petitioner's right to privacy and decision-making in rearing her child. Additionally, while the trial court may later determine the forced visitation was unlawful, the harm petitioner sought to avoid would have already been done. Thus, the court agreed with Williams, and concluded the appellate court erred in not granting certiorari review to petitioner and addressing the challenged statute.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision of the appellate court and remanded the case, because the appellate court erred in not granting certiorari review to petitioner and addressing the challenged statute. While the trial court may later determine the forced visitation was unlawful, the court concluded the harm petitioner sought to avoid would have already been done.

Booker v. State


No. SC93422


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


773 So. 2d 1079; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1983; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 803



October 5, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 22, 2000. Released for Publication December 22, 2000. Certiorari Denied May 14, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3809.
Writ of certiorari denied Booker v. Florida, 532 U.S. 1033, 121 S. Ct. 1989, 149 L. Ed. 2d 779, 2001 U.S. LEXIS 3809 (2001)
Post-conviction relief denied at Booker v. State, 969 So. 2d 186, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1533 (Fla., 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Booker v. McNeil, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111410 (N.D. Fla., Oct. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County, Robert P. Cates, Judge - Case No. 77-2332-CFA.
Booker v. Singletary, 90 F.3d 440, 1996 U.S. App. LEXIS 17469 (11th Cir. Fla., 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County, Florida, entered after a new penalty phase hearing before a new jury, imposing the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: The State of Florida charged defendant with first-degree murder, sexual battery, and burglary, all stemming from the death of a 94-year-old victim. Upon his conviction, the jury imposed the death penalty. The court affirmed. The trial court did not err by refusing to inform the jury regarding the consecutive sentences defendant received for his prior burglary, sexual battery, and aggravated assault convictions. With respect to his objection to the State's use of a peremptory challenge, defendant conceded that the State presented a race-neutral reason for the peremptory challenge. The trial court did not err in finding the State's reason to be genuine. Defendant was not entitled to a special instruction regarding mitigating circumstances, because the instruction given correctly tracked the standard jury instruction regarding mitigating circumstances, Fla. Std. Jury Instructions (Crim.) 112. The trial court's error in temporarily prohibiting a witness from being in court was harmless. Considering the aggravating circumstances under a proportionality analysis, the death sentence was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's death sentence. Points of error raised on appeal were meritless and harmless.

797 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Keen v. State


No. SC88802


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


775 So. 2d 263; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1893; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 754



September 28, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Paul L. Backman, Judge - Case No. 84-9474CF10.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, vacated, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his first degree murder conviction and death sentence, upon his second retrial for the death of his wife, by the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida) where the trial judge overrode the jury's advisory sentence of life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his roommate told police that appellant's wife disappeared from his boat after the three's boat trip. Appellant's brother told the wife's life-insurers that that was false, the roommate admitted that he had helped appellant in the wife's drowning, and appellant was convicted of murder. The jury, on appellant's second retrial, recommended life in prison, but the trial judge gave the death sentence. The court reversed the conviction, acquitted as to the death sentence, and remanded. Instead of merely referring to a "tip" that changed the case from missing person to murder, a detective state witness had hearsay-testified that the insurers (who did not testify) had received information (inferably supplied by appellant's brother, who did not testify) that it was a murder. The State also improperly used that sequence of events substantively in its closing. The events leading to the investigation were not relevant. The trial judge improperly overrode based on his view of the aggravators and mitigators rather than via Tedder analysis. The life sentence was reasonably based on the roommate's disparate treatment. Appellant's other claims were meritless.


OUTCOME: Conviction was reversed, death sentence was vacated and appellant was acquitted of it, and case was remanded. Detective's irrelevant, hearsay testimony as to source of tip that led to murder investigation was highly prejudicial. Death sentence override, based on trial judge's view of mitigators and aggravators, of jury life recommendation violated Tedder. Appellant was acquitted of death penalty for cruel and unusual/double jeopardy purposes.

 

798 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Cherry v. State


No. SC90511


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


781 So. 2d 1040; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1894; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 719



September 28, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 27, 2001. Released for Publication March 27, 2001. Certiorari Denied October 1, 2001, Reported at: 2001 U.S. LEXIS 6404.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Gayle Graziano, Judge - Case No. 86-4473CFAWS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a motion for postconviction relief following an evidentiary hearing finding that counsel was not ineffective in the penalty phase proceedings, following his conviction for first degree murder and sentence of death in the Volusia County (Florida) Circuit Court.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to death after being convicted of two murders. On appeal, the supreme court affirmed the denial of all claims for postconviction relief except those alleging counsel was ineffective in the penalty phase of the trial. The trial court denied relief after an evidentiary hearing. Appellant challenged that finding. The supreme court affirmed, holding that counsel was not ineffective for failing to more fully present mitigating evidence at the penalty phase. Although counsel presented no witnesses and raised only one objection, counsel testified that he discussed the possibility of a death sentence with appellant, asked appellant about possible witnesses for background information and that appellant refused to divulge any such witnesses. Further, there was no evidence beyond speculation that appellant suffered from mental retardation or organic brain damage. Appellant continued to rely on an innocence defense and refused to communicate with counsel at the penalty phase.


OUTCOME: Trial court judgment affirmed. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to more fully present mitigating evidence at the penalty phase; appellant continued to rely on an innocence defense and refused to communicate with counsel at the penalty phase about possible mitigating witnesses. Evidence about retardation or brain damage was only speculative.

 

799 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


Mann v. State


No. SC94885


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


770 So. 2d 1158; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1898; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 727



September 28, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, James R. Case, Judge - Case No. CRC-80-08741-CFANO-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida), denying his motion for postconviction relief after he was convicted sentenced to death for the murder and kidnapping of a 10-year-old.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a prisoner under sentence of death, challenged the circuit court's denial of his motion for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The court affirmed the circuit court's denial. Appellant was convicted in 1982 of kidnapping and first-degree murder in the death of a 10-year-old and was sentenced to death. After several remands and resentencings, appellant asserted in his motion for postconviction relief that counsel was ineffective. The record demonstrated that defense counsel considered other ways in which mental mitigation could have been presented and made a tactical decision to present evidence of appellant's pedophilia. Because appellant did not show any deficiency in counsel's performance, an evidentiary hearing was properly denied. Appellant's final subclaim, that counsel was ineffective for failing to object to a prior violent felony instruction, was procedurally barred because it was decided adversely to appellant on direct appeal and was now being recast as a claim of ineffective assistance.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. Counsel was not ineffective for strategically choosing to introduce certain evidence. Counsel's failure to object to the remaining comments that appellant claimed were improper did not demonstrate a deficiency that prejudiced appellant. Thus, the circuit court properly denied relief.

 

800 of 2516 DOCUMENTS


J.B. v. Fla. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.


No. SC95890


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


768 So. 2d 1060; 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1896; 25 Fla. L. Weekly S 715



September 28, 2000, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity First District - Case No. 1D98-1310 (Leon County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the basis of express and direct conflict with a number of other district court cases, petitioner father appealed a decision by the District Court of Appeal, Statutory Validity First District, Leon County (Florida), which affirmed the termination of petitioner's parental rights to his children.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered an order terminating petitioner father's parental rights. The appellate court affirmed the termination, and petitioner appealed the decision. Petitioner argued that 24 hours notice of an advisory hearing was insufficient to protect his due process rights, and that the trial court's failure to appoint counsel for and adjudicatory hearing was in error. The court held 24 hours notice of the advisory hearing was insufficient to satisfy minimum due process requirements. The court found because petitioner's failure to appear at the hearing resulted in entrance of a consent by default pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 39.462(1)(d), the hearing was in effect a de facto adjudicatory hearing. There was no evidence that such short notice was necessitated by any emergency or potential danger to the children. The opportunity to appeal did not cure the insufficient notice, as the only issue petitioner could argue was his failure to attend the hearing, and he never received a meaningful opportunity to contest the termination of parental rights. The court held petitioner was entitled to appointment of counsel, as he did not knowingly and intelligently waive that right.


OUTCOME: The court quashed and remanded the decision, because petitioner was not given sufficient notice of an advisory hearing, and the trial court erred in failing to appoint counsel for petitioner for an adjudicatory hearing, thereby depriving petitioner of due process of law guaranteed by the Florida and U.S. Constitutions.
